Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Sitting Posture and Tashahhud Recitation
Ruling on sitting posture and recitation of Tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct sitting posture and Tashahhud recitation for a man and woman in the Hanafi school, and identify the wajib/sunnah rulings.

Core Idea
Tashahhud is wajib, not rukn; sitting posture is sunnah and differs by gender.

This lesson covers the rulings on sitting posture (iftirash for men, tawarruk for women) and the recitation of the Tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud. Understanding the distinction between wajib and sunnah in salah is crucial for correct prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
Recognize that the Tashahhud is wajib and the sitting posture is sunnah. Distinguish between what is obligatory and what is recommended.
Wajib requires compensation if omitted forgetfully; sunnah does not.
2
Distinguish between man and woman posture
A man sits iftirash (on left foot with right foot erect). A woman sits tawarruk (legs drawn to the right side). This is the sunnah mu'akkadah.
Tawarruk covers more of the woman's body.
3
Identify the Tashahhud wording
The Tashahhud is that of Ibn Mas'ud, beginning with 'At-Tahiyyatu lillahi'. It is recited in both the first and final sittings.
Hanafis adopt this version due to its strong chain.
4
Note the finger pointing ruling
During the testimony, raise the index finger when saying 'La ilaha' and lower it when saying 'illa Allah'. This is sunnah.
The gesture symbolizes tawhid.
5
Differentiate first and final sitting
In the first sitting, only the Tashahhud is recited; no salawat or du'a. In the final sitting, add salawat and supplications.
If more is added in the first sitting, sajdah al-sahw is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا فرغ الرجل من سجدتي الركعة الثانية افترش رجله اليسرى وجلس عليها، ونصب يمناه، ووجه أصابعها نحو القبلة، ووضع يديه على فخذيه وبسط أصابعه، والمرأة تتورك . وقرأ تشهد ابن مسعود ، وأشار بالمسبحة في الشهادة يرفعها عند النفي، ويضعها عند الإثبات، ولا يزيد على التشهد في القعود الأول، وهو: التحيات لله والصلوات والطيبات، السلام عليك أيها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته، السلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين، أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، وأشهد أن محمدا عبده ورسوله.
And when the man finishes the two prostrations of the second rak'ah, he sits on his left foot (iftirash), erects his right foot, points its toes towards the Qiblah, places his hands on his thighs and spreads his fingers. And the woman sits in tawarruk. And he recites the Tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, and points with the index finger in the testimony, raising it at negation and lowering it at affirmation. He does not add to the Tashahhud in the first sitting. It is: 'At-Tahiyyatu lillahi was-Salawatu wat-Tayyibatu, As-Salamu 'alayka ayyuha an-Nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, As-Salamu 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillahi as-salihin, Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh.'
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on sitting posture after the second rak'ah and the recitation of the Tashahhud. For a man, the sunnah posture is iftirash: sitting on the left foot with the right foot erect, toes pointing to the Qiblah, hands placed on the thighs with fingers spread. For a woman, the sunnah is tawarruk: sitting with both legs drawn to the right side (the left foot emerges from under the right thigh). The Tashahhud recited is that of Ibn Mas'ud (radiAllahu 'anhu), which is the Hanafi choice. During the testimony, the worshiper raises the index finger when saying 'La ilaha' (negation) and lowers it when saying 'illa Allah' (affirmation). In the first sitting (after two rak'ahs), no more than this Tashahhud is recited; the Salat 'ala an-Nabi and supplications are only in the final sitting.

Key Terms
افترش (iftirash): Sitting on the left foot, with the right foot erect, toes pointing to Qiblah. This is the sunnah sitting for a man.
تتورك (tawarruk): Sitting with both legs drawn to the right side, left foot emerging from under the right thigh. This is the sunnah sitting for a woman.
تشهد ابن مسعود (tashahhud Ibn Mas'ud): The specific wording of the Tashahhud as narrated by 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (radiAllahu 'anhu), which begins 'At-Tahiyyatu lillahi...'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the sunnah posture for a woman during the Tashahhud according to the Hanafi school?
A) Iftirash like a man
B) Tawarruk
C) Cross-legged
D) Standing

Key Takeaway
The Tashahhud is wajib, not rukn; its omission requires sajdah al-sahw if forgetful, and the sunnah posture differs for men (iftirash) and women (tawarruk).

The Tashahhud: Hanafi Preference and Linguistic Meaning
Commentary explaining the Tashahhud words and the dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which Tashahhud to recite, explain the meaning of its key words, and identify the practical difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i versions.

Core Idea
Hanafis adopt Ibn Mas'ud's Tashahhud; the worshiper directly greets Allah, not merely narrates.

The Tashahhud is an integral recitation in the prayer, yet its precise wording is a point of legitimate ikhtilaf. In this lesson, we explore why the Hanafi school chose the version of Ibn Mas'ud over that of Ibn 'Abbas, and what each word signifies. We also clarify the spiritual intention behind the recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that multiple companions transmitted tashahhud wordings. The Hanafis adopted Ibn Mas'ud's version; the Shafi'is adopted Ibn 'Abbas's version.
The passage lists 'Umar, 'Ali, Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, 'A'ishah, Jabir, and others.
2
Understand the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi preference is based on the fiqh (juristic insight) of the narrators, not merely the height of the chain. Ibn Mas'ud was a faqih companion.
The Madhhab Dispute Map details the opposing school's evidence.
3
Parse the key terms
Analyze the words 'al-tahiyyat' (verbal worship), 'al-salawat' (bodily worship), and 'al-tayyibat' (financial worship), and see how they correspond to Allah's response of 'salam', meaning of salawat, and 'barakah'.
These three categories cover all forms of worship.
4
Grasp the worshiper's intent
Understand that the Hanafi view holds the worshiper is directly greeting Allah and sending salam upon the Prophet and righteous, not merely narrating a story. This affects the intention (niyyah) during recitation.
Contrast with the view that it is a reported greeting from Allah.
5
Note the practical difference
Identify the exact textual differences: Hanafis omit 'al-mubarakatu' and recite 'ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh', while Shafi'is include 'al-mubarakatu' and recite 'ashhadu anna Muhammadan rasulullah'.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence of the dispute).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن العمر الله تشهدا، ولعلي هه تشهدا، ولعبد الله بن عباس لما تشهدا، ولعبد مسعود همه تشهدا، ولعائشة تشهدا، ولجابر همه تشهدا، ولغيرهم أيضا تشهدا وعلماؤنا أخذوا بتشهد ابن مسعود لله، والشافعي بتشهد ابن عباس ما، وهو: 'التحيات المباركات الصلوات الطيبات الله، سلام عليك أيها ورحمة الله وبركاته، سلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين، وأشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، وأشهد أن محمدا رسول الله'، وبين الفريقان وجوها لتفصيل ما ذهبا إليه، ومحله المطولات العناية بتصرف وزيادة: ٢٧٢/١] التحيات: التحيات جمع تحية من حيا فلان فلاناً إذا دعا له عند ملاقاته كقولهم: حياك الله أي أبقاك الله، والمراد هنا أعز الألفاظ التي تدل على الملك والعظمة، وكل عبادة قولية الله تعالى والمراد بالصلوات هنا العبادات البدنية ونحوها، والطيبات: العبادات المالية الله تعالى وهي الصادرة منه ليلة الإسراء، فلما قال ذلك النبي بإلهام من تعالى، ردّ الله عليه وحياه بقوله: 'السلام' إلخ'، فقابل التحيات بالسلام الذي هو تحية الإسلام، وقابل الصلوات معناها، وقابل الطيبات بالبركات المناسبة للمال؛ لكونها للنمو والكثرة. فلما أفاض سبحانه بإنعامه على النبي بالثلاثة مقابل الثلاثة والنبي الله أكرم خلق الله وأجودهم، عطف بإحسانه ذلك الفيض لإخوانه الأنبياء والملائكة وصالحي المؤمنين من الإنس والجن، فقال: 'السلام علينا إلخ'، فعمهم بها كما قال : 'إنكم إذا قلتموها أصابت كل عبد صالح في السماء والأرض'، وليس أشرف من العبودية في صفات المخلوقين، وهي الرضا بما يفعل الرب، والعبادة ما يرضيه والعبودية أقوى من العبادة؛ لبقائها في العقبى بخلاف العبادة، والصالح: القائم بحقوق الله تعالى وحقوق العباد، فلما أن قال ذلك إحساناً منه شهد أهل الملكوت الأعلى والسموات جبريل بوحي وإلهام أن قال كل منهم: 'أشهد إلخ '، أي أعلم وأبين، وجمع بين أشرف أسمائه وبين أشرف وصف للمخلوق وأرقى وصف مستلزم للنبوة لمقام الجمع، فيقصد المصلي إنشاء هذه الألفاظ مرادة له قاصداً معناها الموضوعة له من عنده كأنه يحيي الله سبحانه وتعالى، ويسلم على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعلى نفسه، وعلى أولياء الله تعالى خلافا لما قاله بعضهم: إنه حكاية سلام الله لا ابتداء سلام من المصلي. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٨٤]
Know that 'Umar had a tashahhud, 'Ali had a tashahhud, 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas had a tashahhud, 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud had a tashahhud, 'A'ishah had a tashahhud, Jabir had a tashahhud, and others had tashahhuds. Our scholars (Hanafis) adopted the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him), and al-Shafi'i adopted the tashahhud of Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him), which is: 'At-Tahiyyatu al-mubarakatu as-salawatu at-tayyibatu lillahi, salamun 'alayka ayyuha an-Nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, salamun 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillahi as-salihin, wa ashhadu an la ilaha illallah, wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan rasulullah.' Between the two groups there are aspects to detail what each has adopted. The place for this is in the lengthy books. [Al-'Inaya 1:272 with changes and additions] 'At-Tahiyyat': it is the plural of tahiyyah from 'hayya' meaning he greeted; the meaning here is the most noble words indicating sovereignty and greatness, and every verbal worship. 'As-Salawat' here means bodily acts of worship and the like. 'At-Tayyibat': means financial acts of worship. And they (the words) were revealed on the night of Isra'. When the Prophet said that by inspiration from Allah, Allah responded to him and greeted him with 'As-Salam' etc. He thus matched the tahiyyat with salam, which is the greeting of Islam; he matched as-salawat with its meaning; he matched at-tayyibat with al-barakah appropriate to wealth because it is for growth and abundance. When Allah bestowed upon the Prophet these three corresponding to the three, and the Prophet is the most generous of creation, he then turned that blessing to his brothers the prophets, angels, and righteous believers from men and jinn, saying 'As-Salamu 'alayna ila akh.' Thus he included them as he said: 'When you say it, it reaches every righteous servant in heaven and earth.' And there is nothing nobler than servitude in the attributes of creation. It is being pleased with what the Lord does; worship is what pleases Him; and servitude (ubudiyyah) is stronger than worship ('ibadah) because it remains in the hereafter unlike worship. The righteous person is one who fulfills the rights of Allah and the rights of people. When he said that out of kindness, the inhabitants of the highest kingdom and the heavens witnessed, and Jibril by revelation and inspiration said each of them: 'I bear witness' meaning I know and declare. He combined His most noble names with the most noble description of the created being, and the highest description necessitating prophethood for the station of gathering. The worshiper intends to utter these words meaning them, intending their literal meanings from himself as if he is greeting Allah, and sending salam upon the Prophet, upon himself, and upon the awliya' of Allah, contrary to what some said: that it is a narration of Allah's greeting, not an initiation of greeting from the worshiper. [Maraqi al-Falah, p. 284]
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the Tashahhud and the school's preference for Ibn Mas'ud's version. It lists that multiple companions transmitted their own tashahhud wordings: 'Umar, 'Ali, Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, 'A'ishah, Jabir, and others. The Hanafi school adopted the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, while al-Shafi'i adopted that of Ibn 'Abbas. The commentary then explains the meaning of each word: 'at-tahiyyat' are the noblest greetings indicating sovereignty; 'as-salawat' are bodily acts of worship; 'at-tayyibat' are financial acts of worship. These three correspond to the three parts of Allah's response: 'as-salam', the meaning of salawat, and 'al-barakah'. The commentary emphasizes that the worshiper is directly greeting Allah and the Prophet, not merely narrating a divine greeting. This is a point of dispute with some scholars. The Hanafi position is that the worshiper initiates the salam.

Key Terms
التحيات (al-tahiyyat): Plural of tahiyyah, meaning greetings or salutations. In the Tashahhud, it refers to the noblest words indicating sovereignty and greatness, encompassing all verbal worship.
الصلوات (al-salawat): In this context, bodily acts of worship such as prayer itself.
الطيبات (al-tayyibat): Financial acts of worship, e.g., charity.
السلام (al-salam): The greeting of Islam, meaning security and peace.
العبودية (al-'ubudiyyah): A continuous state of servitude to Allah, which remains in the hereafter unlike 'ibadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which companion's Tashahhud is recited in prayer?
A) Ibn 'Abbas
B) Ibn Mas'ud
C) 'Umar
D) 'A'ishah

Key Takeaway
Hanafis follow the Tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, emphasizing direct address to Allah and differentiating from the Shafi'i version by omitting 'al-mubarakatu' and reciting 'abduhu wa rasuluh'.

Recitation in Later Rak'ahs and Concluding the Prayer
Ruling on recitation in later rak'ahs and conclusion of prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that only al-Fatiha is recited in the third and fourth rak'ahs and describe the steps to conclude the prayer: sitting, tashahhud, salawat, dua, and taslim.

Core Idea
In the last two rak'ahs, only al-Fatiha; then sit, tashahhud, salawat, dua, taslim.

This passage from Nur al-Idah presents the Hanafi ruling on what to recite in the later rak'ahs of a multi-rak'ah prayer and the proper way to conclude. In the third and fourth rak'ahs (or third of Maghrib), the worshiper recites only Surah al-Fatiha, without an additional surah. After completing these rak'ahs, the final sitting includes Tashahhud, sending blessings on the Prophet, a supplication, and finally the taslim to both sides. This lesson will help you internalize these steps and understand why the Hanafi school limits recitation in the latter rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Determine which rak'ahs are being discussed. 'After the first two' refers to the third and fourth rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer, or the third rak'ah of Maghrib.
In two-rak'ah prayers like Fajr, there is no later rak'ah.
2
State the recitation ruling
The Hanafi ruling: only Surah al-Fatiha is recited in these later rak'ahs. No additional surah is added.
This is contrary to practices in other schools where a surah is recited in every rak'ah.
3
List the concluding sequence
After the last rak'ah: sit, recite Tashahhud, send salawat on the Prophet, make dua, then say taslim to the right and left with 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah'.
The order is fixed; the wording of taslim is as given.
4
Note the difference from the first sitting
The first sitting (after two rak'ahs) includes only Tashahhud; the final sitting adds salawat, dua, and taslim.
The first sitting is shorter and does not conclude the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقرأ الفاتحة فقط فيما بعد الأوليين، ثم جلس وقرأ التشهد، ثم صلى على سيدنا النبي ثم دعا بما يشبه القرآن كما في القعدة الأولى المتقدم ذكره ثم يسلم يمينا ويسارا، فيقول: 'السلام عليكم ورحمة الله'. والسنة، أي ألفاظه معه كما ناويا من تقدم. مفعول ناويا في سنن الصلاة
And he recites only al-Fatiha in what is after the first two rak'ahs. Then he sits and recites the Tashahhud. Then he sends blessings upon our master the Prophet, then he makes dua similar to the Quran? as in the first sitting mentioned earlier. Then he says taslim to the right and left, saying: 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah.' And the sunnah, i.e., its words with him as intended from before. The object of niyyah in the Sunan of prayer.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on recitation in the third and fourth rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer (or the third of Maghrib). According to the Hanafi school, only al-Fatiha is recited, not an additional surah. After completing these rak'ahs, the worshiper sits for the final Tashahhud, sends blessings on the Prophet (salat 'ala an-Nabi), and makes a supplication (dua) that resembles the Quran (meaning it is permissible to use Quranic phrases in dua, but not to recite Quran as part of the dua). Finally, he says taslim to the right and then to the left, saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah.' The note about niyyah indicates that the recitation of taslim is a sunnah and its words are established. This concludes the prayer.

Key Terms
الأوليين (al-uwalayayn): The first two rak'ahs of a prayer. 'After the first two' means the third and fourth rak'ahs.
التسليم (al-taslim): Saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to the right and then to the left to exit the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third and fourth rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, what does the Hanafi school prescribe to recite?
A) Only al-Fatiha
B) Al-Fatiha and a surah
C) Only a surah
D) Subhanallah three times

Key Takeaway
In the final two rak'ahs of a prayer, the Hanafi school prescribes reciting only al-Fatiha, and the prayer concludes with tashahhud, salawat, dua, and taslim to both sides.

The Tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud: Wording, Meaning, and Hanafi Preference
Explains the wording, meaning, and superiority of Ibn Mas'ud's tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact wording of the Hanafi tashahhud and explain why the Hanafi school adopts the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
Hanafis adopt the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud as the authentic testification of faith in prayer.

The tashahhud is a central element of prayer, yet its wording varies among madhhabs. This lesson unpacks the exact wording used in the Hanafi school, tracing its origin to Ibn Mas'ud and contrasting it with the Shafi'i version. You will also explore the deeper meanings of each phrase and the theological significance that the worshiper originates this greeting, not merely narrates it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi tashahhud wording
Read the passage and write down the exact Arabic of the tashahhud as adopted by the Hanafi school. Note the words: التحيات لله والصلوات والطيبات...
This wording is attributed to Ibn Mas'ud.
2
Understand the meaning of each key term
The passage explains التحيات as verbal worship, الصلوات as physical worship, and الطيبات as financial worship. Understand how each corresponds to Allah's response with السلام, and البركات.
These terms encompass all forms of worship.
3
Compare with the Shafi'i wording
The passage gives the Shafi'i wording: التحيات المباركات... Notice the difference in the opening phrase.
The Shafi'i tashahhud is attributed to Ibn 'Abbas.
4
Recognize the theological nuance: narration vs. initiation
The passage refutes the idea that the worshiper is merely narrating what happened on the Night Journey. Instead, the worshiper is initiating the greeting directly to Allah and the Prophet.
This affects the intention (niyyah) during recitation.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
In the first sitting, recite only the tashahhud (without blessings). In the second sitting, add blessings and du'a. The passage also describes the finger movement.
The finger is raised at 'لا إله' and lowered at 'إلا الله'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقرأ تشهد ابن مسعود له ، وأشار بالمسبحة في الشهادة يرفعها عند النفي، ويضعها عند الإثبات، ولا يزيد على التشهد في القعود الأول، وهو: التحيات لله والصلوات والطيبات، السلام عليك أيها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته، السلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين، أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، وأشهد أن محمدا عبده ورسوله ، وقرأ الفاتحة فقط فيما بعد الأوليين، ثم جلس وقرأ التشهد، ثم صلى على سيدنا النبي ثم دعا بما يشبه القرآن كما في القعدة الأولى المتقدم ذكره ثم يسلم يمينا ويسارا، فيقول: "السلام عليكم ورحمة الله" والسنة، أي ألفاظه معه كما ناويا من تقدم. مفعول ناويا في سنن الصلاة الله بن ابن مسعود : اعلم أن العمر الله تشهدا، ولعلي هه تشهدا، ولعبد الله بن عباس لما تشهدا، ولعبد مسعود همه تشهدا، ولعائشة تشهدا، ولجابر همه تشهدا، ولغيرهم أيضا تشهدا وعلماؤنا أخذوا بتشهد ابن مسعود لله، والشافعي بتشهد ابن عباس ما، وهو: "التحيات المباركات الصلوات الطيبات الله، سلام عليك أيها ورحمة الله وبركاته، سلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين، وأشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، وأشهد أن محمدا رسول الله"، وبين الفريقان وجوها لتفصيل ما ذهبا إليه، ومحله المطولات العناية بتصرف وزيادة: ٢٧٢/١] التحيات: التحيات جمع تحية من حيا فلان فلاناً إذا دعا له عند ملاقاته كقولهم: حياك الله أي أبقاك الله، والمراد هنا أعز الألفاظ التي تدل على الملك والعظمة، وكل عبادة قولية الله تعالى والمراد بالصلوات هنا العبادات البدنية النبي و الله ونحوها، والطيبات: العبادات المالية الله تعالى وهي الصادرة منه ليلة الإسراء، فلما قال ذلك النبي بإلهام من تعالى، ردّ الله عليه وحياه بقوله: "السلام" إلخ"، فقابل التحيات بالسلام الذي هو تحية الإسلام، وقابل الصلوات معناها، وقابل الطيبات بالبركات المناسبة للمال؛ لكونها للنمو والكثرة. من بالرحمة التي هي فلما أفاض سبحانه بإنعامه على النبي بالثلاثة مقابل الثلاثة والنبي الله أكرم خلق الله وأجودهم، عطف بإحسانه ذلك الفيض لإخوانه الأنبياء والملائكة وصالحي المؤمنين من الإنس والجن، فقال: "السلام علينا إلخ"، فعمهم بها كما قال : "إنكم إذا قلتموها أصابت كل عبد صالح في السماء والأرض" ، وليس أشرف من العبودية في صفات المخلوقين، وهي الرضا بما يفعل الرب، والعبادة ما يرضيه والعبودية أقوى من العبادة؛ لبقائها في العقبى بخلاف العبادة، والصالح: القائم بحقوق الله تعالى وحقوق العباد، فلما أن قال ذلك إحساناً منه شهد أهل الملكوت الأعلى والسموات جبريل بوحي وإلهام أن قال كل منهم: "أشهد إلخ " ، أي أعلم وأبين، وجمع بين أشرف أسمائه وبين أشرف وصف للمخلوق وأرقى وصف مستلزم للنبوة لمقام الجمع، فيقصد المصلي إنشاء هذه الألفاظ مرادة له قاصداً معناها الموضوعة له من عنده كأنه يحيي الله سبحانه وتعالى، ويسلم على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعلى نفسه، وعلى أولياء الله تعالى خلافا لما قاله بعضهم: إنه حكاية سلام الله لا ابتداء سلام من المصلي. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٨٤]
And he recited the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, and he pointed with the index finger during the testimony, raising it at the negation and lowering it at the affirmation. He does not add anything to the tashahhud in the first sitting. It is: 'All greetings, prayers, and good things are for Allah. Peace be upon you, O Prophet, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings. Peace be upon us and upon the righteous servants of Allah. I bear witness that there is no deity except Allah, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger.' And he recites only al-Fatihah in the two rak'ahs after the first two, then he sits and recites the tashahhud, then sends blessings upon our master the Prophet, then makes a supplication that resembles the Qur'an as mentioned earlier in the first sitting, then he says the taslim to the right and left, saying: 'Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah.' And the Sunnah is its wording with him, as intended by the one who preceded. [Explanation:] Know that there are tashahhud narrated from 'Umar, 'Ali, Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, 'A'ishah, Jabir, and others. Our scholars took the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, while al-Shafi'i took the tashahhud of Ibn 'Abbas, which is: 'Blessed greetings, prayers, and good things are for Allah. Peace be upon you, O Prophet, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings. Peace be upon us and upon the righteous servants of Allah. I bear witness that there is no deity except Allah, and I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' There are differences between the two groups regarding the details of their positions, and the place for that is in the lengthy books. [Al-'Inayah with modifications and additions: 1/272] 'Al-Tahiyyat' is the plural of tahiyyah, from 'hayya' meaning to greet, as in 'hayyaka Allah' meaning may Allah keep you. The intended meaning here is the most honorable words that indicate sovereignty and greatness, and every verbal act of worship... The intended meaning of 'al-salawat' here is physical acts of worship... and 'al-tayyibat' are financial acts of worship... They were revealed on the Night of Isra'. When the Prophet said that by inspiration from Allah, Allah responded to him and greeted him with 'al-salam', etc. So He responded to the greetings with peace, which is the greeting of Islam; He responded to the prayers with their meaning; and He responded to the good things with blessings appropriate for wealth... Then when Allah bestowed His favor upon the Prophet with three things corresponding to the three, and the Prophet is the most generous of Allah's creation, he in turn extended that favor to his brothers the prophets, angels, and righteous believers among humans and jinn, saying: 'Peace be upon us, etc.' So he included them all, as the Prophet said: 'When you say it, it reaches every righteous servant in the heavens and the earth.' And there is nothing more honorable than servitude in the attributes of created beings, which is satisfaction with what the Lord does; and worship is what pleases Him; and servitude is stronger than worship because it remains in the Hereafter unlike worship. The righteous one is the one who fulfills the rights of Allah and the rights of people. When he said that out of benevolence, the inhabitants of the highest dominion and heavens, including Jibril, by revelation and inspiration, each of them said: 'I bear witness...' meaning I know and I make clear. He combined the most honorable of His names with the most honorable attribute of the created being and the highest attribute that implies prophethood for the station of gathering. So the worshiper intends to originate these words, intending their established meanings from himself, as if he is greeting Allah and sending peace upon the Prophet, himself, and the righteous servants of Allah, contrary to what some have said that it is a narration of Allah's peace not an initiation of peace from the worshiper. [Maraqi al-Falah: 284]
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the tashahhud (the testimony recited in the sitting position of prayer). It begins by stating that the Hanafi school adopts the tashahhud of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). The text describes the exact wording: 'Al-tahiyyatu lillahi...' and explains the physical act of raising the index finger at the negation ('la ilaha') and lowering it at the affirmation ('illa Allah'). It notes that in the first sitting, only this tashahhud is recited without adding blessings upon the Prophet. After explaining the ruling, the author contrasts the Hanafi choice with the Shafi'i choice of Ibn 'Abbas's tashahhud, giving the latter's wording. The commentary then delves into the linguistic and spiritual meanings of the words 'tahiyyat', 'salawat', and 'tayyibat', connecting them to the events of the Prophet's Night Journey and Allah's response. It emphasizes that the worshiper is initiating these words of greeting and praise, not merely narrating Allah's greeting, countering a differing opinion. The passage is rich in Hanafi theological and legal nuance.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The specific testimony of faith recited in the sitting position of prayer, particularly the wording attributed to Ibn Mas'ud (or other companions).
التحيات (al-tahiyyat): Plural of tahiyyah, meaning greetings; here referring to all forms of verbal worship and invocations that indicate sovereignty and greatness.
الصلوات (al-salawat): Physical acts of worship such as prayer and prostration.
الطيبات (al-tayyibat): Financial acts of worship such as charity and sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, whose tashahhud is adopted in prayer?
A) Ibn 'Abbas
B) Ibn Mas'ud
C) 'Umar
D) 'Ali

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, whose words are not a narration but an initiation of greeting by the worshiper, and its meaning comprehensively covers all forms of worship.

Salah — Prayer

Conditions for Valid Imamate (Leading Prayer)
Lists and explains the six conditions for valid imamate in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for valid imamate in Hanafi fiqh and identify which condition is violated in a given scenario.

Core Idea
For an imam to be valid, he must be Muslim, adult, sane, male, able to recite, and free from excuses.

In the Hanafi school, leading prayer (imamate) is governed by specific conditions that ensure the congregation's prayer is valid. This lesson unpacks the six conditions listed in Nur al-Idah, explaining each with its rationale and occasional internal disagreements. By the end, you will be able to assess whether a given imam meets the requirements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six conditions
From the passage, list the six required qualities: Islam, puberty, sanity, masculinity, ability to recite, and freedom from excuses. Understand that these apply when a man leads men; for women leading women, masculinity is not required.
The conditions are general; note the exceptions for women-only congregations.
2
Explain the rationale for each condition
Each condition has a legal basis: Islam ensures correct belief, puberty ensures the imam's prayer is obligatory, sanity ensures valid intention, masculinity preserves the dignity of leadership, recitation ability ensures correct Quran reading, and freedom from excuses ensures the imam can perform the prayer properly.
Focus on why each is necessary; the text gives explicit reasons for some, e.g., the argument against a boy leading an adult.
3
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a hypothetical imam (e.g., a sane, adult Muslim male with a chronic nosebleed), determine whether his imamate is valid for non-excused followers. Use the condition 'freedom from excuses' to rule it invalid.
Remember that the excused person can lead others with the same excuse.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The passage mentions that some Balkh scholars allowed an adult to be led by a boy in tarawih and nafl, but the mufta bihi position rejects this. Understand the reasoning: the boy's prayer is supererogatory, while the follower's is obligatory, leading to inequality.
This disagreement is resolved by later Hanafi authorities; the chosen view is invalidity without exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإمامة الأذان، والصلاة بالجماعة سنة للرجال الأحرار بلا عذر، وشروط صحة شائبة بالواجب في القوة لأن الجماعة تسقط بالعذر أفضل من الإمامة للرجال الأصحاء ستة أشياء: الإسلام والبلوغ والعقل والذكورة والقراءة والسلامة من الأعذار كالرُّعاف والفأفأة والتمتمة واللثغ وفقد شرط كطهارة وستر عورة. الإمامة: أي اتباع الإمام في جزء من صلاته [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح ٢٨٥] أفضل المواظبته الضيع التالي عليها، وكذا الخلفاء الراشدون بعده. فتح القدير سنة أطلق السنة وهي مقيدة بما عدا الجمعة والعيدين؛ فإنها فيهما شرط الجواز. للرجال: قيد بالرجال فلا تشترط كل الشروط لصحة جماعة النساء، بل يخرج منها الذكورة؛ فإن الأنثى تصح إمامتها لمثلها، وبأصحاء لإخراج ذوي الأعذار، فإن إمامتهم صحيحة لمماثليهم. حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۸۷] الأصحاء جمع صحيح كأحباء جمع حبيب. الإسلام وهو شرط عام، فلا تصح إمامة منكر البعث أو خلافة الصديق أو صحبته أو من يسب الشيخين، أو ينكر الشفاعة، أو ينكر الإسراء أو الرؤية أو عذاب القبر أو وجود الكرام الكاتبين أو نحو ذلك ممن يظهر يصح اقتداء الإسلام مع ظهور صفته المكفرة له . [ حاشية الطحطاوي، مراقي الفلاح: ٢٨٧] والبلوغ فلا يصح اقتداء بالغ لصبي مطلقا، سواء كان في فرض؛ لأن صلاة الصبي ولو نوى الفرض نفل، أو في نفل؛ لأن نفله لا يلزمه، ونفل المقتدي لازم مضمون عليه، فيلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف، وقال بعض مشايخ بلخ: يصح اقتداء البالغ بالصبي في التراويح والسنن المطلقة والنفل، والمختار: عدم الصحة بلا خلاف بين أصحابنا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٨٨] والعقل: فلا تصح إمامة سكران ومجنون يجنون مطبق مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۸] والذكورة فلا الرجل بالمرأة، وصلاتها في ذاتها صحيحة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٨٨] والسلامة من الأعذار: فلا يصح اقتداء غير المعذور بالمعذور كالرعاف الرعاف بالضم الدم يخرج من الأنف و كصبار الكثير الرعاف. أقرب الموارد والفأفأة فأفأ الرجل: كثر الفاء وتردد فيها في كلامه، قال المطرزي: الفافاً: الذي لا يقدر على إخراج الكلمة لسانه إلا بجهد يبتدئ في أول إخراجها بشبه الفاء، ثم يؤدي بعده من بالجهد حروف الكلمة على الصحة. أقرب الموارد) التمتمة تمتم الكلام تمتمه رده إلى التاء والميم أو سبقت كلمته إلى حنكه ،الأعلى وعن أبي زيد: التمتام: الذي يعجل في الكلام ولا يضحك. أقرب الموارد) واللثغ بالثاء المثلثة والتحريك وهو اللثغة بضم اللام وسكون الثاء: تحرك اللسان السين إلى الثاء، ومن الراء إلى الغين ونحوه مراقي الفلاح (۲۸۹] كطهارة إلخ فلا : يصح إمامة عادم طهارة لطاهر، وكذا إمامة ساتر العار.
Chapter of Imamate. The adhan and prayer in congregation are sunnah for free men without excuse, and conditions of validity are similar to wajib in strength because congregation is waived by excuse. Better than imamate for healthy men are six things: Islam, puberty, sanity, masculinity, ability to recite, and freedom from excuses such as nosebleed, stammering (fa'fa'ah), mumbling (tamtamah), lisping (luthgh), and loss of a condition like purification or covering the private parts. [Footnote:] Imamate means following the imam in part of his prayer. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi] The best is to adhere to the one who is regular in prayer, and likewise the rightly guided caliphs after him. [Fath al-Qadir] 'Sunnah' is used absolutely but is restricted to other than Friday and the two 'Eids; for those it is a condition of validity. 'For men': restricted to men, so not all conditions are required for the validity of a women's congregation; rather masculinity is excluded because a woman can validly lead her own gender. 'Healthy men' excludes those with excuses, as their imamate is valid for those similar to them. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 287] 'Al-Sihah' is plural of sahih (healthy) like ahba' plural of habib. Islam is a general condition, so the imamate of one who denies the Resurrection, the caliphate of Abu Bakr, his companionship, or insults the two shaykhs, or denies intercession, or denies the Night Journey, or the beatific vision, or the punishment of the grave, or the existence of the recording angels, or similar, is not valid if his Islam manifests as apostasy. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah: 287] Puberty: an adult cannot be led by a boy at all, whether in obligatory prayer (because the boy's prayer, even if he intends obligation, is supererogatory) or in supererogatory (because his supererogatory is not obligatory, while the follower's supererogatory is obligatory and guaranteed, so it necessitates building the strong upon the weak). Some scholars of Balkh said: an adult can be led by a boy in tarawih, absolute sunan, and supererogatory prayers. But the chosen view is that it is invalid without disagreement among our companions. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 288] Sanity: the imamate of an intoxicated person or a chronic madman is not valid. [Maraqi al-Falah: 288] Masculinity: a man cannot be led by a woman, though her prayer in itself is valid. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 288] Freedom from excuses: a non-excused person cannot be led by an excused one, such as nosebleed (nosebleed: blood from the nose) like a chronic nosebleeder. [Aqrab al-Mawarid] Fa'fa'ah: a man who repeats the letter fa frequently in his speech. Al-Mutarrizi said: 'al-fafa'' is one who cannot pronounce a word without difficulty, starting its articulation with something like fa, then manages the remaining letters with effort. [Aqrab al-Mawarid] Tamtamah: one who returns speech to ta' and mim, or his word precedes to his palate. Abu Zaid said: al-tamtam is one who hurries in speech and does not laugh. [Aqrab al-Mawarid] Luthgh (with thā' and vowel): it is the lisp that turns sin into thā' and ra' into ghayn and similar. [Maraqi al-Falah: 289] Like purification etc.: one lacking purification cannot lead one who has purification, and likewise one not covering his private parts.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the rules of imamate (leading prayer) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by stating that congregation (jama'ah) for prayer is sunnah for free men without excuse, though it is 'shadeedah bil-wajib' (close to obligatory in strength), as it is waived only by a valid excuse. The passage lists six conditions for being a valid imam: Islam, puberty, sanity, masculinity, ability to recite, and freedom from physical defects or excuses. Each is explained. Islam is a general condition; an apostate or heretic cannot lead. Puberty: an adult cannot follow a pre-pubescent boy because the boy's prayer is supererogatory, while the adult's is obligatory, so it would be illogical. Sanity: an intoxicated or insane person cannot lead. Masculinity: a woman cannot lead men but can lead women. Freedom from excuses: a person with a chronic nosebleed, stammer, mumble, or lisp cannot lead someone without such excuse, as the imam's recitation must be complete. The passage also clarifies that these conditions apply to leading men; for women leading women, masculinity is not required. The text cites commentators like al-Tahtawi and al-Shurunbulali's Maraqi al-Falah to elaborate details and occasional ikhtilaf (like the Balkh scholars' view on boys leading tarawih, which is rejected).

Key Terms
الإمامة (al-imamah): The act of leading prayer; defined as 'following the imam in a part of his prayer'.
الرعاف (al-ru'af): Nosebleed; an excuse that prevents one from being imam for non-excused followers.
الفأفأة (al-fa'fa'ah): A speech disorder involving repetition of the letter fa, making recitation difficult.
التمتمة (al-tamtamah): A speech disorder where speech is turned to ta and mim, or the word precedes to the palate, causing unclear articulation.
اللثغ (al-luthgh): Lisping, such as pronouncing sin as tha or ra as ghayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a pre-pubescent boy lead an adult man in an obligatory prayer?
A) Yes, if the boy has reached the age of discernment
B) Yes, for any prayer
C) No, not under any circumstance
D) Yes, but only for tarawih

Key Takeaway
The validity of imamate depends on six conditions; failure in any one, even if the imam is otherwise qualified, invalidates the congregation's prayer for non-excused followers.

Fourteen Conditions for Valid Iqtida' (Following the Imam)
Ruling with expansion: lists conditions with intra-Hanafi dispute on positioning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fourteen conditions for valid iqtida' and apply them to determine the validity of a follower's prayer.

Core Idea
Following the imam requires eight key conditions; missing any invalidates the prayer.

The validity of praying behind an imam (iqtida') depends on specific conditions. This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates fourteen such conditions, covering intention, positioning, and status of both imam and follower. Understanding these conditions ensures that your congregational prayer is sound. Let's break them down.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list of conditions
Read the Arabic text and locate the numbered conditions. They begin with 'نيّة المقتدي المتابعة' and continue through the passage. Note that some conditions are further elaborated with examples.
The passage mentions fourteen but lists eight main points with sub-cases.
2
Classify each condition as shart or man'i
Determine which conditions are shurut (prerequisites for validity) and which are mawani' (preventers). Most are shurut, e.g., intention must be present; a row of women separating is a man'i.
Shurut must exist; mawani' must be absent.
3
Examine the intention requirements
The passage discusses the follower's intention (niyya) – it must be mutaba'ah (to follow) concurrent with takbir. It also states that specifying the imam is not required and may be harmful.
A general intention suffices; specifying the imam risks invalidity if wrong.
4
Analyze the position of the imam
Two views are presented: the matn requires the imam to be ahead by his heel, but al-Tahtawi says alignment (muhadha) by the head is sufficient. Understand the dispute and the mufta bihi.
Consideration is by the head – if the follower's head is behind the imam's head, it is valid even if feet are ahead.
5
Apply the conditions to practical scenarios
Use the conditions to evaluate whether a given prayer arrangement is valid. For example, can a traveler lead a resident in zuhr after the time? The passage explains the rules.
Pay attention to the details: four-rak'ah prayers only, within time vs after time, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشروط صحة الإقتداء أربعة عشر شيئا نيّة المقتدي المتابعة مقارنة لتحريمته، ونية الرجل الإمامة شرط لصحة اقتداء النساء به، وتقدم الإمام بعقبه عن المأموم، وأن لا يكون أدنى حالاً من المأموم، وأن لا يكون الإمام مصليا فرضا غير فرضه، وأن الإمام لا يكون مقيماً لمسافر بعد الوقت في رباعية ولا مسبوقاً، وأن لا يفصل بين الإمام والمأموم صف من النساء، المتابعة: كأن ينوي معه الشروع في صلاته أو الاقتداء فيها، ولو نوى الاقتداء به لا غير، فالأصح أنه يجزئه، وتنصرف إلى صلاة الإمام، وإن لم يكن للمقتدي علم بها؛ لأنه جعل تبعا للإمام خلافاً لمن قال: لابد للمقتدي ثلاث نية أصل الصلاة ونية التعيين ونية الاقتداء، ونية المتابعة شرط في غير جمعة وعيد على المختار؛ لاختصاصها بالجماعة، فلا يحتاج فيها إلى نية الاقتداء، وأما نية الإمامة فليست بشرط في حق النساء، ولا يلزم للمقتدي تعيين الإمام بل الأفضل عدمه؛ لأنه لو عينه فبان خلافه فسدت صلاته. (زيلعي على الكنز) وتقدم الإمام إلخ : قال الشارح: حتى لو تقدم المقتدي مع تأخر عقبه من عقب الإمام لطول قدم المقتدي لا يضر، وقال الطحطاوي واعلم أن ما أفاده المصنف من اشتراط التقدم خلاف المذهب؛ لأنه لو حاذاه صح الاقتداء، والعبرة في المؤمي بالرأس حتى لو كان رأسه خلف رأس الإمام ورجلاه قدام رجليه صح، وعلى العكس لا يصح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: (۲۹۰] وأن لا يكون أدنى إلخ مثل أن يكون المقتدي مفترضا والإمام متنفلا، فإن قلت: فكيف اقتداء من يرى وجوب الوتر بمن يرى سنيته؟ قلنا لأنه ليس الإمام أدنى حالا من المأموم، فإن صلاتهما متحدة، وإنما الاختلاف في الاعتقاد غیر فرضه مثل أن يصلي المأموم صلاة الظهر خلف من يصلي صلاة العصر أو على العكس، أو مثل أن يصلي المأموم صلاة الظهر من يوم السبت والإمام صلاة الظهر من يوم الأحد، وفي "الظهيرية": صلى ركعتين من العصر فغربت الشمس فاقتدى به إنسان في الأخريين يجوز وإن كان هذا قضاء للمقتدي؛ لأن الصلاة واحدة. مقيما: شرط عدم كون الإمام مقيما والمأموم مسافرا؛ فإن اقتداء المقيم بالمسافر صحيح في الوقت وبعده؛ لأن صلاة المسافر في الحالين واحدة والقعدة فرض في حقه غير فرض في حق المقتدي وبناء الضعيف على القوي جائز وكونه بعد الوقت فإن الاقتداء إذا وُجد في الوقت، ثم خرج الوقت وهما في الصلاة، فإن الاقتداء صحيح، ويفترض الإتمام ولو كان الإمام المقيم كبر في الوقت واقتدى المسافر بعد خروجه لا يصح، وكونه في رباعية؛ لأن الثنائية والثلاثية لا تتغيران سفرا ولا حضرا.
And the conditions for validity of iqtida' (following) are fourteen things: the intention of the follower to follow (mutaba'ah) concurrent with his takbirat al-ihram, and the intention of the man to be imam is a condition for the validity of women following him, and that the imam be ahead by his heel from the ma'mum, and that he (the ma'mum) not be in a lower state than the ma'mum (sic), and that the imam not be praying a fard other than his fard, and that the imam not be a resident for a traveler after the time in a four-rak'ah prayer, nor a masbuq (latecomer), and that there not be a row of women separating between the imam and the ma'mum. Mutaba'ah: such that he intends with him the start of his prayer or the iqtida' in it, and if he only intends iqtida' without more, the soundest view is that it suffices, and it refers to the imam's prayer even if the follower has no knowledge of it because he is made a follower of the imam, contrary to those who say: the follower must have three intentions: intention of the original prayer, intention of specification, and intention of iqtida'. And intention of mutaba'ah is a condition in other than Friday and Eid on the chosen view, because they are specific to congregation, so iqtida' intention is not needed in them. As for intention of imamah, it is not a condition for women, and it is not necessary for the follower to specify the imam; rather it is better not to, because if he specifies and it turns out otherwise, his prayer is invalid. (Zayla'i on al-Kanz) And the imam being ahead, etc.: the commentator said: even if the follower is ahead while his heel lags behind the imam's heel due to the length of the follower's foot, it does not harm. And al-Tahtawi said: know that what the author stated about stipulating being ahead is contrary to the madhhab, because if he aligns with him (muhadha) the iqtida' is valid, and consideration in the mumi' (one who indicates) is by the head, so if his head is behind the imam's head and his feet are in front of his feet, it is valid, and the opposite is invalid. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 290] And that he not be lower, etc., like the follower being obligated (mufrad) and the imam being supererogatory (mutatawwi'), so if you say: how then is the iqtida' of one who considers witr wajib behind one who considers it sunnah? We say: because the imam is not in a lower state than the ma'mum, for their prayers are one, and the difference is only in belief. Other than his fard: like the ma'mum praying zuhr behind one praying asr, or vice versa, or like the ma'mum praying zuhr of Saturday and the imam praying zuhr of Sunday. And in al-Zahiriyya: he prayed two rak'ahs of asr and the sun set, so someone followed him in the last two rak'ahs; it is permissible even if this is qada' for the follower because the prayer is one. Resident: condition that the imam not be resident and the ma'mum traveler; for the iqtida' of a resident behind a traveler is valid within the time and after it, because the traveler's prayer in both cases is one, and the final sitting (qa'da) is fard for him but not fard for the follower, and building the weak on the strong is permissible. And being after the time: for iqtida' if it occurs within the time, then the time exits while they are in prayer, the iqtida' is valid, and it becomes obligatory to complete. And if the resident imam said takbir within the time and the traveler followed after the time, it is invalid. And being in a four-rak'ah prayer: because two- and three-rak'ah prayers do not change in travel or residence.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with expansion, enumerating fourteen conditions for the validity of iqtida' (the follower's act of following the imam). The conditions are: 1) The follower must have intention (niyya) of mutaba'ah (following) concurrent with his opening takbir. 2) If the follower is a woman, the man (imam) must intend to lead. 3) The imam must be ahead by his heel relative to the ma'mum. 4) The follower must not be in a higher state than the imam (e.g., follower praying fard behind imam praying nafl). 5) The imam must not be praying a different fard than the follower. 6) The imam must not be a resident for a traveler after the time in a four-rak'ah prayer. 7) The imam must not be a masbuq (one who joined late) leading others. 8) No row of women should separate the imam and ma'mum. The text explains each condition in detail. It discusses the intention: the recommended view is that a general intention of following suffices, and specifying the imam is discouraged because if the imam turns out to be someone else, the prayer becomes invalid. Regarding the imam being ahead, al-Tahtawi notes that the madhhab considers muhadha (alignment) sufficient, with consideration given to the head position. The condition of not being in a lower state includes examples: a follower praying fard cannot follow an imam praying nafl; however, one who believes witr is wajib can follow one who believes it is sunnah because the actual prayer is the same. The condition of not being a different fard is illustrated by praying zuhr behind asr. The condition regarding resident/traveler is explained: a resident can follow a traveler in a four-rak'ah prayer only within the time, and after the time it is invalid unless the takbir was done in time. The text also touches on the ruling for masbuq and women's rows.

Key Terms
المتابعة (al-mutaba'ah): The follower's intention to follow the imam in prayer
الإقتداء (al-iqtidā'): The act of following an imam in prayer
المسبوق (al-masbūq): One who joins the congregation late and misses some rak'ahs
المحاذاة (al-muḥādhāh): Alignment of the imam and ma'mum such that their heads are at the same level

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling if a follower intends to follow a specific imam but that imam turns out to be someone else?
A) The prayer is still valid because intention of following is sufficient.
B) The prayer becomes invalid because the follower specified the wrong person.
C) The follower must repeat the prayer.
D) The imam must redo his intention.

Key Takeaway
The validity of following an imam in Hanafi prayer depends on eight core conditions; among them, a general intention suffices, and the imam's physical alignment by the head is sufficient.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Intention and Status: First Four Conditions of Iqtida'
Enumeration of first four conditions for iqtida'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first four conditions for valid following (iqtida') and apply them to distinguish valid from invalid congregational prayer scenarios.

Core Idea
Valid following requires the follower's intention to follow, the imam's intention for women, the imam's precedence, and that the imam not be inferior in status.

The Hanafi school specifies fourteen conditions for the validity of following an imam in prayer. This lesson covers the first four: the follower's intention at the takbir, the imam's intention when leading women, the imam's slight precedence in position, and the requirement that the imam not be of a lower religious or legal status than the follower. These conditions ensure that the relationship of imamate is properly established from the outset.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is following (iqtida') an imam in congregational prayer. The ruling is that it is valid only when all conditions are met. Here, we focus on the first four conditions.
2
Examine the follower's intention
The follower must intend to follow (mutaba'ah) at the moment of his own takbirat al-ihram. This intention makes him a muqtadi. If he intends to pray alone, his prayer is valid but he is not following the imam.
The intention does not need to specify the prayer type (e.g., Zuhr); just the act of following suffices.
3
Examine the imam's intention for women followers
When women follow a male imam, the imam must intend to lead them. Without this intention, the women's following is invalid, but the imam's own prayer remains valid.
This condition applies only when women are present. Men following do not require the imam's explicit intention.
4
Analyze the spatial precedence
The imam must stand slightly ahead of the follower, at least by the length of his heel. If they are level or the follower is ahead, the following is invalid.
This ensures the imam's leadership is visually clear.
5
Consider status equality
The imam must not be in a state that is legally 'lower' than the follower, such as being in a state of minor impurity while the follower has wudu, or being a sinner while the follower is pious. If the imam is inferior, the following is invalid.
Hanafis define 'lower status' in terms of both apparent religious state (like wudu) and moral character (fasiq vs. 'adil). A fasiq (open sinner) should not lead a righteous person.

Source Text

أحكام الإمامة وشروط صحة الإقتداء أربعة عشر شيئا نيّة المقتدي المتابعة مقارنة لتحريمته، ونية الرجل الإمامة شرط لصحة اقتداء النساء به، وتقدم الإمام بعقبه عن المأموم، وأن لا يكون أدنى حالاً من المأموم، وأن لا يكون الإمام مصليا فرضا غير فرضه، وأن الإمام لا يكون مقيماً لمسافر بعد الوقت في رباعية ولا مسبوقاً، وأن لا يفصل بين الإمام والمأموم صف من النساء، وأن لا يفصل نهر يمر فيه الزورق، ولا طريق تمرّ فيه العجلة، ولا حائط يشتبه معه العلم بانتقالات الإمام، وأن لا يكون الإمام راكبا، والمقتدي راجلاً أو بالعكس، أو راكبا غير دابة إمامه، وأن لا يكون في سفينة والإمام في أخرى غير مقترنة بها، وأن لا يعلم المقتدي من حال إمامه مفسدا في زعم المأموم كخروج دم أو قيء لم يعد بعده وضوءه، وصح اقتداء متوضئ بمتيمم، وغاسل بماسح وقائم بقاعد وبأحدب، ومؤم بمثله، ومتنفل بمفترض، وإن ظهر بطلان صلاة إمامه أعاد، ويلزم الإمام إعلام القوم بإعادة صلاحتم بالقدر الممكن في المختار. ولو بكتاب أو رسول. هر فرق الشيخ بين النهر الصغير الغير الفاصل والكبير الفاصل بمرور الزورق، وهذا هو الصحيح في الفرق بينهما، وقيل: الصغير ما تحصى شركاؤه. العجلة: هي بالتحريك : آلة يجرها الثور، أي لا يكون بين الإمام والمأموم طريق إلخ. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۹۲] في الصحيح: خلافا لما في "الدر" و"البحر" وغيرهما من اشتراط عدم اختلاف المكان إمامه أفاد أنه إذا كان المأموم راكبا على دابة إمامه صح الاقتداء؛ لاتحاد المكان. كخروج دم مثلا لو صلى أحد خلف من يعتقد عدم الانتقاض بالخارج من غير السبيلين أو بالقيء، ويتيقن أنه وجد منه أحدهما و لم يتوضأ زعما منه عدم انتقاض الوضوء، لا يصح اقتداء من يعتقد الانتقاض، حتى لو غاب بعد ما شاهد منه ذلك بقدر ما يعيد الوضوء و لم يعلم حاله، فالصحيح جواز الاقتداء مع الكراهة. وصح اقتداء إلخ أي . صح الاقتداء إذا كان المقتدي متوضئا والإمام متيمما ، أو كان المقتدي غاسلا والإمام ماسحا على خف أو جبيرة، أو كان المقتدي قائما والإمام قاعدا أو كان المقتدي قائماً والإمام أحدب، أو كان الإمام والمقتدي يصليان بالإيماء، أو كان المقتدي متنفلا والإمام مفترضا. بماسح على خف أو جبيرة أو خرقة قرحة لا يسيل منها شيء [مراقي الفلاح ۲۹٥] وبأحدب: هو من خرج ظهره ودخل صدره وبطنه الإمام أي الذي تبين فساد صلاته. مراقي الفلاح في المختار: وفي "الدراية": لا يلزم الإمام الإعلام إذا كانوا قوما غير معينين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٩٧]
Rulings of Imamate and conditions for validity of following (iqtida') are fourteen things: intention of the follower (muqtadi) to follow (mutaba'ah) at the beginning of his takbirat al-ihram; and intention of the man for imamate is a condition for validity of women following him; and the precedence of the imam with his heel over the follower; and that the imam not be of a lower status than the follower; and that the imam not be praying a different obligatory prayer than his own; and that the imam not be a resident while the follower is a traveler after the time in a four-rak'ah prayer, nor a masbuq (one who missed part of the prayer); and that there be no row of women separating the imam and the follower; and that there be no river in which a small boat passes, nor a road on which a cart passes, nor a wall that obstructs knowledge of the imam's movements; and that the imam not be riding while the follower is on foot or vice versa, or riding an animal different from the imam's mount; and that he not be in a ship while the imam is in another ship not attached to it; and that the follower not know of a state of the imam that is invalidating in the follower's view, such as the emission of blood or vomit for which he has not renewed his ablution. And the following of a person with ablution behind one who performs tayammum is valid, and one who washes behind one who wipes, and one standing behind one sitting, and behind one with a hunched back, and one gesturing behind one like him, and one performing supererogatory prayer behind one performing obligatory prayer. And if the invalidity of the imam's prayer becomes apparent, he repeats; and the imam is obligated to inform the people of the repetition of their prayer to the extent possible in the preferred view, even by a book or a messenger. The shaykh distinguished between a small river that does not separate and a large one that separates by the passage of the boat, and this is the correct distinction between them; and it was said: the small river is one whose partners are counted. al-'Ajalah: it is, with tashkeed, a device pulled by an ox, meaning there should not be a road between the imam and the follower, etc. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 292] In al-Sahih: contrary to what is in al-Durr and al-Bahr and others regarding the condition that the place not differ; his saying 'imam' indicates that if the follower is riding on the animal of his imam, the following is valid due to unity of place. Like the emission of blood for example: if someone prays behind one who believes that the emission from other than the two passages or vomit does not break wudu, and he is certain that one of these occurred from him and he did not perform wudu, assuming that his wudu is not invalidated, then the following of one who believes it invalidates is not valid; until if he disappears after witnessing that from him for a period sufficient to renew wudu and his state is not known, then the correct view is that following is permissible with dislike. 'And the following is valid' etc., meaning: following is valid if the follower has wudu and the imam performs tayammum, or if the follower washes and the imam wipes over a khuff or a splint, or if the follower is standing and the imam is sitting, or if the follower is standing and the imam is hunched, or if the imam and follower pray with gestures, or if the follower is performing supererogatory prayer and the imam is performing obligatory prayer. 'Wiping over a khuff or a splint or a cloth over a wound from which nothing oozes' [Maraqi al-Falah 295]. 'And hunched (ahdab)': one whose back is curved and his chest and stomach protrude. 'Imam' meaning the one whose prayer is invalid. Maraqui al-Falah in al-Mukhtar: and in al-Diraya: the imam is not obligated to inform if the people are not a specific group. [Maraqi al-Falah: 297]
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and others enumerates the fourteen conditions for the validity of following an imam (iqtida') in congregational prayer. The conditions cover intention, spatial alignment, compatibility of prayers, absence of barriers, and knowledge of the imam's state. The text first lists all conditions concisely, then expands on each with scholarly commentary. Key points: the follower must intend to follow at the takbir; the imam must intend imamate for women followers; the imam must be slightly ahead; the imam must not be of inferior status; the prayers must match; a resident imam cannot lead a traveler in a 4-rak'at prayer after time; the follower must not be a masbuq; no row of women or impassable barriers between; the imam and follower must be on similar transport or both on foot; if the follower knows the imam's prayer is invalid in his view, following is invalid. The text also validates following in cases where the imam has a different wudu status (tayammum, wiping) or posture (sitting, hunched, gesturing), as long as the prayer itself is valid. If the imam's prayer is later found invalid, the follower must repeat; the imam should inform the congregation if possible. The commentary clarifies specific terms like 'small river' and 'cart-road' and discusses the ruling on following a person who does not consider certain actions to break wudu. This is a standard Hanafi treatment based on the principle that the follower is subordinate to the imam.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer by performing actions after him with intention.
المتابعة (al-mutaba'ah): The follower's intention to follow the imam, either at the start or during prayer.
أدنى حالاً (adna halan): Lower in religious or legal status, e.g., impure vs. pure, fasiq vs. righteous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The imam must be ahead by at least his heel.
C) The prayer must be an obligatory prayer.
D) The imam must be a scholar.

Key Takeaway
The first four conditions establish the basic relationship: the follower must intend to follow, the imam must intend to lead (if women follow), physical precedence is required, and the imam must not be inferior in status.

Conditions for Valid Iqtida' (Following the Imam)
Rulings on physical and practical conditions for valid congregational following

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid iqtida' and identify which scenarios are valid or invalid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Following the imam is valid if you can track his movements; physical separation is allowed as long as no confusion.

Congregational prayer requires the follower to synchronise with the imam. The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance on what physical and practical conditions enable valid iqtida'. This lesson unpacks those conditions, from barriers and transport to the follower's knowledge of the imam's state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general conditions
Iqtida' means following the imam in prayer. The text first lists barriers that prevent valid following: a river with boat traffic, a road with carts, a wall causing confusion. The key is that the follower must be able to track the imam's movements by sight or sound.
This is the overarching principle: visibility or audibility without confusion.
2
Examine the barrier conditions
A river is problematic only if it is large enough for a boat to pass. A road is problematic if carts pass. A wall is problematic if it causes confusion. If there is no confusion (e.g., the follower can see or hear clearly), following is valid.
The commentary distinguishes between small and large rivers; the sound position uses boat passage as the criterion.
3
Analyze riding and ship scenarios
If the imam is riding, the follower must be on the same mount; otherwise, following is invalid. Similarly, if both are in separate ships not connected, following is invalid. This is because unity of place is necessary when both are in motion.
Unity of place is required only in specific dynamic contexts, not in static buildings.
4
Understand the 'knowledge of invalidator' condition
If the follower knows that the imam has done something that invalidates wudu in the follower's own view (e.g., blood or vomit), and the imam did not renew wudu, the follower's prayer is invalid. If the follower is uncertain or the imam's state is unknown, it is permissible with dislike.
This condition depends on the follower's ijtihad regarding nullifiers of wudu.
5
List the valid iqtida' pairings
The text lists several valid combinations: a person with wudu following a mutayammim, one who washes following one who wipes, a standing person following a sitting or hunchbacked imam, one using gestures following another using gestures, and a supererogatory prayer following an obligatory one.
These pairings are permitted even though the imam and follower are in different states of purity or posture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة

1..

أحكام الإمامة

وأن لا يفصل نهر يمر فيه الزورق، ولا طريق تمرّ فيه العجلة، ولا حائط يشتبه معه بين الإمام والمأموم نوع من السفن الصغار أراد به الطريق النافذ

العلم بانتقالات الإمام، فإن لم يشتبه لسماع أو رؤية صح الاقتداء في الصحيح،

وأن لا يكون الإمام راكبا، والمقتدي راجلاً أو راكبا غير دابة إمامه، وأن لا يكون أو بالعكس

سفينة أخرى

في سفينة والإمام في أخرى غير مقترنة بها، وأن لا يعلم المقتدي من حال إمامه مفسدا في زعم المأموم كخروج دم أو قيء لم يعد بعده وضوءه، وصح مفعول لقوله: "يعلم" الجملة نعت لما قبلها

اقتداء

متوضئ بمتيمم، وغاسل بماسح وقائم بقاعد وبأحدب، ومؤم بمثله، ومتنفل اسم فاعل من الإيماء

بمفترض، وإن ظهر بطلان صلاة إمامه أعاد ، ويلزم الإمام إعلام القوم بإعادة

صلاتهم بالقدر الممكن في المختار.

ولو بكتاب أو رسول

هر فرق الشيخ بين النهر الصغير الغير الفاصل والكبير الفاصل بمرور الزورق، وهذا هو الصحيح في الفرق بينهما، وقيل: الصغير ما تحصى شركاؤه. العجلة: هي بالتحريك : آلة يجرها الثور، أي لا يكون بين الإمام والمأموم طريق إلخ. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۹۲] في الصحيح: خلافا لما في "الدر" و"البحر" وغيرهما من اشتراط عدم اختلاف المكان إمامه أفاد أنه إذا كان المأموم راكبا على دابة إمامه صح الاقتداء؛ لاتحاد المكان. کخروج دم مثلا لو صلى أحد خلف من يعتقد عدم الانتقاض بالخارج من غير السبيلين أو بالقيء، ويتيقن أنه وجد منه أحدهما و لم يتوضأ زعما منه عدم انتقاض الوضوء، لا يصح اقتداء من يعتقد الانتقاض، حتى لو غاب بعد ما شاهد منه ذلك بقدر ما يعيد الوضوء و لم يعلم حاله، فالصحيح جواز الاقتداء مع الكراهة.

Book of Prayer

Rulings of Imamate
And that there should not separate [them] a river in which a small boat passes, nor a road on which a cart passes, nor a wall that causes confusion between the imam and the ma'mum—[the river being] a type of small ship, intending [by 'road'] the through road.
Knowledge of the imam's movements [is required], and if it is not confusing due to hearing or sight, the following is valid according to the sound [position].
And that the imam should not be riding while the follower is walking, or riding an animal other than the imam's mount, or vice versa.
[And] another ship: [if] in a ship and the imam is in another not connected to it.
And that the follower should not know from the imam's state something that invalidates in the follower's opinion, such as blood or vomit after which he did not renew his ablution. ['and correct' is the object of 'knows'; the sentence is an adjective for what precedes].
Following [is valid] of a person who performed ablution [following] one who performed tayammum, and one who washed [following] one who wiped, and a standing person [following] a sitting one or a hunchbacked one, and one who prays with gestures [following] one like him, and one performing a supererogatory prayer [the active participle of 'gesturing'] following one performing an obligatory prayer. And if the invalidity of his imam's prayer becomes apparent, he repeats [his prayer], and the imam is obliged to inform the people of the repetition of their prayer as much as possible in the chosen [view]. Even if by a book or a messenger.
He [the commentator] distinguished between a small river that does not separate and a large one that separates due to the passage of a boat, and this is the correct distinction between them. It was said: the small one is that whose partners can be counted. 'al-Ajal' is, with fatha, an implement pulled by an ox, i.e., there should not be between the imam and the ma'mum a road, etc. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 292] In the sound [view], contrary to what is in al-Durr and al-Bahr and others of the condition of not differing in place. It benefits that if the ma'mum is riding on the imam's mount, following is valid due to unity of place. For example, blood: if one prays behind someone who believes that what comes out from other than the two passages or vomit does not break wudu, and he is certain that one of them occurred from him and he did not perform wudu, assuming that wudu is not broken, the following of one who believes it breaks is not valid. Even if he disappeared after witnessing that from him for the time sufficient to renew wudu and his state is unknown, the correct [view] is permissibility of following with dislike.
And correct
following
etc., i.e., following is valid if the follower performed wudu and the imam performed tayammum, or the follower washed and the imam wiped over a khuff or a splint, or the follower was standing and the imam was sitting, or the follower was standing and the imam was hunchbacked, or the imam and follower prayed with gestures, or the follower was performing a supererogatory prayer and the imam an obligatory one. [Following] one who wipes over a khuff or splint or a piece of cloth over a wound from which nothing flows [Maraqi al-Falah 295]. And 'ahdab' is one whose back is curved and chest and belly are sunken. The imam: i.e., the one whose prayer's invalidity became apparent. Maraqi al-Falah: In al-Mukhtar, and in al-Diraya: the imam is not obliged to inform if they are an unspecified group. [Maraqi al-Falah: 297]
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings from the Hanafi school on conditions for the validity of iqtida' (following the imam in congregational prayer). The text begins by listing physical barriers that prevent valid following: a river navigable by small boat, a road traversed by carts, or a wall that obscures the imam's movements. The key principle is that the follower must be able to track the imam's transitions (from standing to bowing, etc.) either by sight or sound. If there is no confusion, following is valid. The text then addresses scenarios where the imam is riding: if the follower is on foot or riding a different animal, the following is invalid unless the follower is on the same mount as the imam (united in place). Similarly, if both are in separate ships not connected, following is invalid. Another condition is that the follower must not know of a factor that invalidates prayer in his own view (e.g., blood or vomit from the imam that the imam ignored). If the follower knows, his following is invalid. However, if he merely suspects, it may be valid with dislike. The passage then presents a series of valid iqtida' pairings: a person with wudu following a mutayammim, one washing his limbs following one who wipes over khuff, a standing person following a sitting or hunchbacked imam, one using gestures following another using gestures, and a supererogatory prayer following an obligatory one. The text concludes with a ruling: if the imam's prayer becomes invalid, he must inform the congregation to repeat, unless they are an unspecified group (al-Diraya holds he is not obliged). The commentary resolves a dispute about the river barrier, preferring the distinction based on boat passage over counting partners. It also highlights an intra-Hanafi difference: al-Durr and al-Bahr require unity of place, but the sound position allows following if the follower is on the imam's mount.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Act of following the imam in congregational prayer, submitting to his leadership in actions.
مأموم (ma'mum): The person who follows the imam in prayer.
مفسد (mufsid): That which invalidates the prayer, such as hadath (impurity) or speaking.
صحيح (sahih): Sound; legally valid and fulfilling all conditions.
زورق (zawraq): A small boat; used in the text to define a large separating river.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following iqtida' scenarios is valid?
A) A standing person following a sitting imam
B) A person who performed tayammum following one who performed wudu
C) A follower walking on the ground while the imam rides a camel
D) A follower in a ship while the imam is in another ship that is not connected

Key Takeaway
Iqtida' is valid if the follower can track the imam's movements without confusion, with specific exceptions for riding and separate ships.

Owner and Mosque Imam Priority in Leading Prayer
Priority rules for imamate: house owner and mosque official over more virtuous individuals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the owner of a house and the appointed imam of a mosque have absolute priority to lead congregational prayer, and explain the underlying rationale of authority (sultan).

Core Idea
The owner and mosque imam lead even over the more learned because the home is his domain.

In congregational prayer, who deserves to lead? While knowledge and piety are generally preferred, the Hanafi school carves out two exceptions: the owner of the house and the mosque's official imam. This lesson unpacks that ruling, showing how ownership and appointment confer a right that overrides personal virtue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exceptions
Find the two categories that take precedence: the house owner (sahib manzil) and the mosque functionary (dhu wazifa, the appointed imam).
Also includes the owner of a gathering place.
2
State the ruling
Both have absolute priority over others, even if the others are more learned, recitative, pious, or virtuous.
They may lead or appoint someone else.
3
Understand the rationale
The owner's authority (sultan) over his property gives him the right to lead or delegate. The mosque imam's appointment by the waqf gives him similar authority.
The term 'sultan' implies full disposal.
4
Note the recommendation (istihbab)
It is recommended for the owner to permit a better person to lead, but this is not obligatory.
The owner may choose to lead himself even if less qualified.
5
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school generally prefers the most knowledgeable regardless of ownership or appointment. Recognize the ikhtilaf.
Both positions have evidence; Hanafi relies on owner's authority.

Section on the most entitled to imamate and arrangement of rows

If there is not among those present an owner of the house or a functionary [appointed by waqf]...
[Commentary] 'with them' by rental or borrowing
'the congregation'
'fear' – any fear, absolute, includes fear for oneself, one's property, loss of property, or departure of a caravan if he occupies himself with congregational prayer. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 297] Muhammad I'zaz 'Ali... [repetition of previous section's commentary]...
'If there is not among them an owner of a house or a functionary' – he negated that there is among them a house owner or a functionary, i.e., the one appointed by the waqf for imamate, because these two are given priority absolutely, whether these mentioned virtues are present or not. So the owner of the house, the gathering, and the imam of the mosque are more entitled to lead than others, even if the other is more learned, more recitative, more pious, and more virtuous. If he wishes, he may lead; if he wishes, he may appoint whom he wants, even if the one he appoints is less than the rest of the attendees because he is the authority; he acts in it as he wishes. It is recommended for the house owner to permit one who is better. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 299]
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This section deals with who has priority to lead the congregational prayer when there is no pre-existing arrangement. The passage states that if there is no house owner or appointed functionary, then the general rules of priority based on knowledge and piety apply. However, the commentary clarifies that if a house owner or a mosque's appointed imam is present, they have absolute priority over others, regardless of their knowledge or piety. The house owner has the authority to either lead himself or appoint someone else, even if that person is less qualified than others present. This is because the house is his domain ('sultan'). It is recommended, though, that he defer to a more virtuous person. The remaining part of the text is a repetition of the previous section's commentary on excuses, which seems to be an OCR error.

Key Terms
صاحب منزل (sahib manzil): Owner of the house where prayer is being held, who has priority to lead.
صاحب وظيفة (sahib wazifa): The appointed imam of the mosque, designated by the waqf, who has priority to lead.
سلطانه (sultanuhu): His authority; the owner's dominion over his property.

In Hanafi fiqh, the house owner and mosque imam have absolute priority in leading prayer based on their authority over the premises, overriding personal virtue.
