The Eighteen Valid Excuses for Missing Congregational Prayer
Lists 18 valid excuses and emphasizes reward preservation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eighteen excuses for missing congregational prayer and explain that a valid excuse preserves the reward of jama'ah.

Core Idea
Eighteen specific hardships exempt a Hanafi from jama'ah—and he still obtains the full reward.

In Hanafi fiqh, attending congregational prayer (jama'ah) is a confirmed obligation (wajib), not a personal duty (fard). This means the school allows a broader range of valid excuses. The classical text Nur al-Idah lists exactly eighteen excuses. Understanding them ensures you know when you may pray alone without sin—and when you still earn the reward of the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the legal basis
Recall that jama'ah is wajib, not fard, in the Hanafi school. This leniency allows these excuses. The principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj) underlies the list.
2
Categorize the eighteen excuses
Group them into natural phenomena (rain, cold, darkness, wind), physical disabilities (blindness, paralysis, amputation, illness, bedridden, chronic disability, old age), external circumstances (fear, imprisonment, deep mud), and other (food craving, travel, caring for sick, studying fiqh).
The list is exhaustive for the author.
3
Note the key reward rule
The text states: 'If one misses jama'ah due to a permissible excuse, he obtains its reward.' This means the excuse does not just forgive the absence—it makes the single prayer equal in reward to the congregational one.
This is a mercy from Allah.
4
Memorize the list using grouping
Use an acrostic or visual chart. For example: R (rain), C (cold), F (fear), D (darkness), I (imprisonment), B (blindness), P (paralysis), A (amputation), I (illness), B (bedridden), M (mud), C (chronic disability), O (old age), S (studying fiqh), F (food craving), T (travel), S (sick care), W (wind at night).
Practice active recall.
5
Apply the condition for imprisonment
The commentary restricts 'imprisonment' to the insolvent (mu'sir). A solvent person who is imprisoned for debt is not excused because he could pay.
This shows that each excuse has its own conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مسقطات الجماعة] مسقطات الجماعة يسقط حضور الجماعة بواحد من ثمانية عشر شيئاً: مطر، وبرد، وخوف، وظلمة، وحبس، وعمى، وفلج، وقطع يد ورجل، وسقام، وإقعاد، ووحل، وزمانة، وشيخوخة، وتكرار فقه بجماعة تفوته، وحضور طعام تتوقه نفسه، وإرادة سفر، وقيامه بمريض، وشدة ريح شديدة ليلا لا نهارا. وإذا انقطع عن الجماعة لعذر من أعذارها المبيحة للتخلف يحصل له ثوابها. وخوف أي خوف ظالم أطلقه فشمل إذا خاف على نفسه أو ماله أو ضياع ماله أو ذهاب قافلة لو اشتغل بالصلاة جماعة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۹۷] وحبس أي إذا حبس معسر لوفاء دين عليه أو حبسه ظالم بغير حق عليه يسقط منه حضور الجماعة، قيد بالمعسر؛ لأن الموسر لا يعذر في الترك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٩٧] وفلج: فلج الرجل أصابه داء الفالج، وهو داء يحدث في أحد شقي البدن طولا، فيبطل إحساسه وحركته. (أقرب الموارد) وإقعاد: أقعد الرجل على المجهول: أصابه داء في جسده، فلا يستطيع المشي. (أقرب الموارد) ووحل: الوحل محركة الطين الرقيق ترتطم فيه الدواب والجمع أو حال ووحول. (أقرب الموارد) وزمانة: العامة هي وعدم بعض الأعضاء، وتعطل القوى. (أقرب الموارد) وشيخوخة أي كونه شيخا كبيرا لا يستطيع المشي. (حاشية الطحطاوي) وتكرار فقه إلخ: أي يكرر كتب فقه مع القوم الذين لو حضروا الجماعة يفوتونه، وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يداوم على ترك الجماعة ويفيد أن المتكرر وحده لا يعطى هذا الحكم، وفيه نظر. بجماعة تفوته الأولى حذفه؛ لأن الموضوع الأعذار التي تفوت الجماعة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٩٨] وإرادة: أراد به تهيؤ وقت السفر بأن صار مشغول البال بمصالحه. بمريض: أي إذا كان المصلي قائما بمريض يستضر بغيبة يباح له ترك الجماعة.
Section on Exemptions from Congregational Prayer. Exemptions from Congregational Prayer. Attendance of congregational prayer is waived by one of eighteen things: rain, extreme cold, fear, darkness, imprisonment, blindness, paralysis, amputation of hand and foot, illness, being bedridden, deep mud, chronic disability, advanced old age, reviewing fiqh with a group whose prayer he would miss, presence of food that he craves, intention to travel, being occupied with a sick person, and severe wind at night but not during the day. And if one misses the congregational prayer due to any of the permissible excuses, he obtains its reward. Explanation: Fear: any fear of a tyrant, general, includes fear for his life, property, loss of property, or loss of a caravan if he were to engage in congregational prayer. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 297] Imprisonment: if an insolvent debtor is imprisoned for debt repayment or a tyrant imprisons him unjustly, attendance of congregation is waived. It is restricted to the insolvent because the solvent is not excused. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 297] Paralysis: a man afflicted with paralysis, a disease that occurs in one side of the body longitudinally, nullifying its sensation and movement. (Aqrab al-Mawarid) Bedridden: a man becomes bedridden (passive verb): he is afflicted with a disease in his body such that he cannot walk. (Aqrab al-Mawarid) Deep mud: deep mud (with vowel movements) fine mud in which animals sink; plural is awhal or wuhul. (Aqrab al-Mawarid) Chronic disability: it is the loss of some limbs and the failure of powers. (Aqrab al-Mawarid) Advanced old age: meaning being a very old man unable to walk. (Hashiyah al-Tahtawi) Reviewing fiqh, etc.: i.e., he reviews books of fiqh with a group whom he would miss if he attended the congregation. It is restricted to when he does not persistently abandon the congregation. It indicates that the mere reviewer does not get this ruling, and there is consideration in that. "B-jamā'atin tafūtuhu" the first "al-ula" is deleted because the topic is excuses that cause missing the congregation. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 298] Intention: what is meant is that the time for travel becomes ready such that he becomes occupied with its preparations. For a sick person: i.e., if the person praying is caring for a sick person who would be harmed by his absence, it is permissible for him to leave the congregation.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Nur al-Idah listing the eighteen valid excuses that exempt a person from attending the congregational (jama'ah) prayer in Hanafi fiqh. The author first enumerates them concisely: rain, extreme cold, fear, darkness, imprisonment, blindness, paralysis, amputation of hand and foot, illness, being bedridden (unable to walk), deep mud, chronic disability, advanced old age, studying fiqh with a group whose prayer would be missed, presence of desired food, intention to travel, caring for a sick person, and severe wind at night (not day). Then the commentator (from Hashiyah al-Tahtawi and others) elaborates on each. For example, 'fear' includes any fear from a tyrant, whether for life, property, or caravan. 'Imprisonment' only excuses the insolvent (mu'sir) who cannot pay, not the solvent. 'Paralysis' and 'bedridden' are physical incapacities. 'Deep mud' refers to fine mud that hinders movement. 'Chronic disability' is loss of limbs. 'Old age' is inability to walk. 'Reviewing fiqh' is allowed only if he is not persistently missing the congregation. The text also notes that if someone misses jama'ah due to these excuses, he still obtains the reward of communal prayer. The key principle is that these are genuine hardships that make attendance difficult; the list is exhaustive for the author. The Hanafi school considers jama'ah a confirmed obligation (wajib) but not fard, hence these excuses are derived from the principle of hardship removal.

Key Terms
مسقطات الجماعة (musqitat al-jama'ah): The legal excuses that remove the obligation of attending congregational prayer.
تخلف (takhalluf): Being absent from congregational prayer due to an excuse.
فقه (fiqh): In this context, studying or reviewing fiqh books with others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Priority for Leading Prayer and Disliked Imams
Sets the order of priority for imamah and discusses disliked imams with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi priority order for imamah and identify when the imamate of a slave, blind person, bedouin, or illegitimate child is disliked and when it is permissible.

Core Idea
Knowledge leads the prayer; ignorance in an imam is disliked, but piety removes it.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes a hierarchical order for who should lead the prayer when no designated imam or ruler is present. It also addresses four categories of people whose imamate is generally disliked, but explains that the dislike is conditional on ignorance. Understanding these rulings helps in organizing congregational prayer with proper adab.

Guided Path
1
List the priority order
Identify the ten qualities in order: knowledgeable, best reciter, most pious, oldest, best character, best face, noblest lineage, best voice, cleanest garment. Note that this applies only when no house owner, official imam, or ruler is present.
The ruler takes precedence over everyone due to general authority.
2
Understand the role of majority choice
If the congregation disagrees on who should lead, the majority's choice prevails. If they choose someone other than the most entitled, they act wrongfully but the prayer is valid.
The prayer is not invalidated by appointing a less entitled imam.
3
Examine the four disliked imams
For each of the four (slave, blind, bedouin, illegitimate child), note the reason for dislike and the condition that removes it. The dislike is based on presumed ignorance, not inherent status.
If they are knowledgeable and pious, there is no dislike.
4
Analyze the proof for ruler precedence
The hadith of Ibn Umar praying behind al-Hajjaj is cited to show that even a sinful ruler has precedence due to his general authority. This demonstrates that authority overrides other criteria.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, indicating its authenticity.

فصل في الأحق بالإمامة وترتيب الصفوف إذا لم يكن بين الحاضرين صاحب منزل ولا وظيفة. أي معهم بالإجارة أو بالعارية ولا ذو سلطان، فالأعلم أحق بالإمامة، ثم الأقرأ ثم الأورع، ثم الأسن، ثم الأحسن خلقا ثم الأحسن وجها، ثم الأشرف نسبا، ثم الأحسن صوتا، ثم الأنظف ثوبا، فإن استووا يقرع، أو الخيار للقوم فإن اختلفوا فالعبرة بما اختاره الأكثر، وإن قدموا غير الأولى فقد أساؤوا، لكن لا يأثمون، وكره إمامة العبد والأعمى والأعرابي وولد الزنا. ولا ذو سلطان أفاد أن ذا سلطان إذا كان معهم فهو أولى من الجميع حتى من ساكن المنزل وصاحب الوظيفة؛ لأن ولايته عامة، وروى البخاري أن ابن عمر كان يصلى خلف الحجاج، وكفى به فاسقا، قال في 'النهاية': هذا في الزمن الماضي؛ لأن الولاة كانوا علماء وغالبهم كانوا صلحاء، وأما في زماننا فأكثر الولاة وجهلة. [حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة ۲۹۹] فالأعلم أحق إلخ أي الذي يعلم بأحكام الصلاة صحة وفسادا ويحفظ ما به سنة القراءة، وأما حفظ مقدار الفرض فمعلوم أنه من شروط الصحة وهذه شروط كمال، ويجتنب الفواحش الظاهرة وإن كان غير متبحر في بقية العلوم. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٩٩] الأقرأ وهو يحتمل لشيئين: أحدهما: أن يكون المراد به أحفظهم للقرآن، وهو المتبادر، الثاني: أحسنهم تلاوة للقرآن باعتبار تجويد قراءته وترتيلها، وقد اقتصر العلامة تلميذ المحقق ابن الهمام في 'شرح زاد الفقير' عليه. [البحر الرائق: ٦٥٤/١] الأورع: أي الأكثر اجتنابا للشبهات والفرق بين الورع والتقوى: أن الورع اجتناب الشبهات، والتقوى اجتناب المحرمات [البحر الرائق: ٦٥٤/١] خلقا بضمتين، أي ألفة بين الناس [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۰۰] فإن اختلفوا إلخ أي إن اختلف المصلون في تقديم الإمام، فقال بعضهم: يقدم فلان وأشار بعضهم إلى آخر وهكذا فالاعتبار لمن اختاره أكثر القوم. وإن قدموا إلخ أي وإن قدم القوم من هو غير الأحق فيهم، فالقوم مسيؤون وكره إمامة إلخ: اعلم أن كراهة إمامة العبد معللة بعدم علمه وتقواه، فظهر أن الكراهة في إمامة العبد لا لذاتهم، بل لأنهم لاشتغالهم بخدمة المولى لا يتفرغون للعلم، فيغلب عليهم الجهل ويندر فيهم تقوى، فلو انتفى ذلك بأن كان عالماً تقياً فلا كراهة. وكراهة إمامة الأعمى معللة بعدم اهتدائه إلى القبلة، وصون ثيابه عن الدنس. والأعرابي: من يسكن البادية عربيا كان أو عجميّاً، وأما من يسكن المدن فهو عربي، وكراهة إمامة الأعراب لغلبة الجهل عليهم، يحكى أن أعرابيا اقتدى بإمام فقرأ الإمام آية (الأعراب أشد كفرا ونفاقا) [التوبة: ٩٧] إلخ فضربه الأعرابي وشجّ رأسه، ثم اقتدى به بعد مدة، فرآه الإمام فقرأ آية (ومن الأعراب من يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر) [التوبة: ٩٩] فقال الأعرابي الآن نفعك العصا. وكراهة إمامة ولد الزنا معللة بأنه ليس له أب يربيه ويؤدبه ويعلمه، فيغلب عليه الجهل، فإذا كان هو أفضل القوم فلا كراهة وأراد بولد الزنا الذي لا علم عنده ولا تقوى، فبالجملة.
Section on Who is Most Entitled to Lead the Prayer and Arrangement of Rows. If there is no house owner or official imam among those present, meaning with them by rent or loan, and no ruler, then the most knowledgeable is most entitled to lead the prayer, then the most proficient in recitation, then the most pious, then the oldest, then the best in character, then the best in face, then the noblest in lineage, then the best in voice, then the cleanest in garment. If they are equal, a lottery is held or the choice is left to the people. If they differ, weight is given to the choice of the majority. If they appoint someone other than the most worthy, they act wrongfully but do not sin. And the imamate of a slave, a blind person, a bedouin, and an illegitimate child is disliked. The phrase 'and no ruler' indicates that if a ruler is with them, he is more entitled than all, even than the house occupant and the official imam, because his authority is general. Al-Bukhari reported that Ibn Umar used to pray behind al-Hajjaj, and it suffices that he was a sinner. He said in al-Nihayah: This was in the past because rulers were scholars and most were righteous. But in our time, most rulers are ignorant. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi with addition 299] 'The most knowledgeable is most entitled' etc.: i.e., one who knows the rulings of prayer, its validity and invalidity, and preserves what is necessary for the Sunnah of recitation. As for preserving the obligatory amount, it is known that this is a condition of validity, and these are conditions of perfection. He avoids manifest sins even if he is not a master of other sciences. [Maraqi al-Falah: 299] 'The most proficient in recitation': this can mean two things: one is the one who memorizes the Quran most, which is the apparent meaning; the second is the one who recites the Quran best in terms of tajweed and tarteel. The student of the researcher Ibn al-Humam in Sharh Zad al-Faqir adopted the latter. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/654] 'The most pious': i.e., the one who avoids doubtful matters most. The difference between wara' and taqwa is that wara' is avoidance of doubtful matters, and taqwa is avoidance of forbidden matters. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/654] 'Best in character' (khuluqan with double damma): i.e., affability among people. [Maraqi al-Falah: 300] 'If they differ' etc.: i.e., if the worshipers differ in presenting the imam, some saying to present Fulan and others pointing to another, then the weight is for the choice of the majority. 'And if they appoint' etc.: i.e., if the people appoint someone who is not the most worthy, they act wrongfully. And the dislike of imamate of a slave, blind, bedouin, and illegitimate child: know that the dislike of the imamate of a slave is due to his lack of knowledge and piety. So it appears that the dislike for the imamate of a slave is not for their essence, but because being occupied with the service of the master prevents them from pursuing knowledge, so ignorance prevails among them and piety is rare. Therefore, if that is not the case, such as if he is knowledgeable and pious, then there is no dislike. The dislike of the imamate of a blind person is due to his inability to find the direction of the qibla and keep his garments clean from filth. The bedouin: one who lives in the desert, whether Arab or non-Arab. As for one who lives in cities, he is an Arab. The dislike of the imamate of bedouins is due to the prevalence of ignorance among them. It is narrated that a bedouin followed an imam who recited the verse (The bedouins are more severe in disbelief and hypocrisy) [al-Tawbah: 97] etc., and the bedouin struck him and split his head. Then after a while he followed him again, and the imam recited the verse (And among the bedouins are those who believe in Allah and the Last Day) [al-Tawbah: 99], so the bedouin said: Now the stick has benefited you. The dislike of the imamate of an illegitimate child is because he has no father to raise him, discipline him, and teach him, so ignorance prevails upon him. If he is the best of the people, then there is no dislike. And by 'illegitimate child' he means one who has no knowledge and no piety. In summary.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah addresses two main issues: the order of priority for leading the prayer (imamah) and the ruling on certain disliked imams. The text first states that when there is no house owner (sahib al-manzil) or official imam (sahib al-wazifa) or ruler (dhu sultan) present, the priority order is: the most knowledgeable (a'lam), then the best reciter (aqra'), then the most pious (awra'), then the oldest (asinn), then the best character, then the best face, then the noblest lineage, then the best voice, then the cleanest garment. The commentator explains that 'knowledgeable' means one who knows the rulings of prayer and the sunnah recitation, not necessarily scholarly in other fields. 'Aqra' can mean most memorization of Quran or best recitation; the preferred view is best recitation. 'Awra' is one who avoids doubtful matters, distinguishing wara' from taqwa. The commentary also clarifies that if the worshippers differ, the majority's choice prevails, and if they appoint someone other than the most entitled, they are blameworthy but the prayer is valid. The passage then discusses four disliked imams: a slave, a blind person, a bedouin, and an illegitimate child. The reason for dislike is given: slaves are usually uneducated, blind persons may struggle with qibla and cleanliness, bedouins are often ignorant (as illustrated by a story), and illegitimate children often lack parental education. However, the commentary emphasizes that if any of these individuals are actually knowledgeable and pious, the dislike is removed. The proof for the ruler's precedence comes from the hadith that Ibn Umar prayed behind the tyrant al-Hajjaj, indicating that even a sinful ruler takes precedence due to his general authority.

Key Terms
الأعلم (al-a'lam): The most knowledgeable in the rulings of prayer and its conditions.
الأقرأ (al-aqra'): Two interpretations: best memorizer of Quran or best reciter in tajweed.
الأورع (al-awra'): The most pious, avoiding doubtful matters (shubuhat).
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): Illegitimate child born out of wedlock.
الأعرابي (al-a'rabi): Bedouin; one who lives in the desert, whether Arab or non-Arab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, the imamate of which of the following is disliked only if the person is ignorant?
A) A ruler
B) A slave
C) A Hanafi scholar
D) A person with a beard

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi priority for imamah is based on knowledge first, and dislike of certain imams is conditional on ignorance.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

The Ranking of the Most Entitled Imam
Ranking of imams and principle of validity vs. dislike

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ranking of imams for leading prayer and apply it to determine the most entitled person in a given scenario.

Core Idea
The most knowledgeable in prayer rules leads first, not the most senior in age.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes the hierarchy of who deserves to lead the prayer. It begins with the authority of the ruler (sultan) and then proceeds through knowledge, recitation, piety, and other qualities. The proof is drawn from the practice of the Companions, including Ibn Umar praying behind al-Hajjaj, demonstrating that even a sinful ruler takes precedence to avoid social discord.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first criterion: authority (sultan)
The sultan (ruler) is given top priority even if sinful, to maintain unity and avoid fitna.
This is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar praying behind al-Hajjaj.
2
List the remaining criteria in order
After the sultan, the most knowledgeable in prayer rulings, then the best reciter, then the most pious (wara'), then the oldest, then the best in character, then best in appearance, then noblest lineage, then best voice, then cleanest clothes.
Knowledge (al-a'lam) is given precedence over recitation (al-aqra').
3
Determine resolution when candidates are equal
If two or more are equal in all criteria, either lots are drawn or the congregation chooses. If the congregation differs, the majority opinion is followed.
This avoids prolonged disputes.
4
Recognize the ruling when a less qualified is appointed
If the congregation intentionally appoints someone less entitled, they have done wrong (asau) and it is makruh tahrimi, but the prayer is still valid.
The validity of the prayer depends on basic eligibility, not optimality.
5
Understand the underlying principle: validity vs. dislike
The passage explains that validity is based on performing the arkan with proper conditions, while dislike is based on the potential reduction in congregational attendance.
Thus, a less-than-ideal imam does not invalidate the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
۱۰۲
الأحق بالأمامة .
ولا ذو سلطان، فالأعلم أحق بالإمامة، ثم الأقرأ ثم الأورع، ثم الأسن، ثم
الأحسن خلقا ثم الأحسن وجها، ثم الأشرف نسبا ، ثم الأحسن صوتا، ثم الأنظف
ثوبا، فإن استووا يقرع ، أو الخيار للقوم فإن اختلفوا فالعبرة بما اختاره الأكثر، وإن
قدموا غير الأولى فقد أساؤوا، وكره إمامة.
العبد والأعمى والأعرابي وولد الزنا والجاهل والفاسق والمبتدع، وتطويل الصلاة، وجماعة العراة ،والنساء فإن فعلن يقف الإمام وسطهن كالعراة، ويقف
الواحد عن يمين الإمام والأكثر خلفه ويصف الرجال، ثم الصبيان، ثم الخناثي
ثم النساء.
هذا الكلام بيان لشيئين الصحة والكراهة، أما الصحة فمبنية على وجود الأهلية للصلاة أداء الأركان، مع وهما موجودان من غير نقص في الشرائط، وأما الكراهة فمبنية على قلة رغبة الناس في الاقتداء بهؤلاء، فيؤدي إلى تقليل الجماعة المطلوب تكثيرها تكثيراً للأجر.
العبد: فلو اجتمع المعتق والحر الأصلي واستويا في العلم والقراءة، فالحر الأصلي أولى. [فتح القدير: ٣٠٣/١] المبتدع وهو صاحب البدعة، وهي كما في "المغرب" اسم من ابتدع، ثم غلبت على ما هو زيادة في الدين أو نقصان منه. وعرفها الشمني بأنها ما أحدث على خلاف الحق المتلقى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من علم أو عمل أو حال بنوع شبهة واستحسان، وجعل دينا قويما وصراطا مستقيما وأطلق في المبتدع فشمل كل مبتدع هو من أهل قبلتنا، وقيده في "المحيط" و"الخلاصة" و"المجتبى" وغيرها بأن لا تكون بدعة تكفره، فإن كانت تكفره فالصلاة خلفه لا تجوز [البحر الرائق: ٦٥٨/١] وتطويل الصلاة أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان القوم يحصون أو لا، رضوا بالتطويل أو لا ؛ لإطلاق الحديث، وأطلق في التطويل فشمل إطالة القراءة أو الركوع أو السجود أو الأدعية البحر الرائق: ٦٦٢/١] والنساء: أي وكره تحريما جماعة النساء بواحدة منهن، ولو أمهن رجل فلا كراهة إلا أن يكون في بيت ليس معهن فيه رجل أو محرم من الإمام أو زوجته، فإن كان واحد ممن ذكر معهنَّ فلا كراهة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٠٤] فإن فعلن إلخ أي فإن صلت النساء بالجماعة يجب أن يقف الإمام وسطهنَّ مع تقدم عقبها، فلو تقدمت كالرجل أثمت، وصحت الصلاة والوسط بالتحريك ما بين طرفي الشيء، وبالسكون لما يبين بعضه عن بعض كجلست وسط الدار بالسكون. فإن قلت لم ترك المصنف بالله التأنيث في لفظ الإمام؟ قلت: الإمام من يؤتم به ذكرا كان أو أنثى. يمين الإمام ويكره أن يقف عن يساره. مراقي الفلاح ثم الخناثي جمع الخنثى، من الرجال والنساء. أقرب الموارد، مراقي الفلاح (۳۰۸ ثم النساء: إن حضرن، وإلا فهن ممنوعات عن حضور الجماعات. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٠٨]
The Book of Prayer: 102. The Most Entitled to Lead. And no one with authority, so the most knowledgeable is most entitled to lead, then the best reciter, then the most pious, then the oldest, then the best in character, then the best in face, then the noblest in lineage, then the best in voice, then the cleanest in garment. If they are equal, lots are drawn, or the choice is for the people. If they differ, consideration is given to what the majority chooses. If they appoint other than the most entitled, they have done wrong, and it is disliked to lead: the slave, the blind man, the bedouin, the child of fornication, the ignorant, the sinful, the innovator, and prolonging the prayer, and the congregation of the naked, and women. If they do so, the imam stands in their middle like the naked. The single person stands to the right of the imam, and the majority behind him. The men are arranged, then boys, then the hermaphrodites, then women. This speech is an explanation of two things: validity and dislike. As for validity, it is based on the existence of eligibility for prayer by performing pillars, and they are present without deficiency in conditions. As for dislike, it is based on the lack of people's desire to follow these, leading to reduction of the congregation which is desired to be increased for reward. The slave: if a freed slave and a freeborn person meet and are equal in knowledge and recitation, the freeborn is more entitled. [Fath al-Qadir 1:303] The innovator: he is the one of innovation, which is as in al-Mughrib: a noun from ibtada'a, then it became prevalent for what is an addition to religion or a reduction. Al-Shumunni defined it as what is introduced contrary to the truth received from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, from knowledge or action or state, by kind of doubt and approval, and made a straight religion and path. It is general for every innovator who is of our qibla. It is restricted in al-Muhit, al-Khulasah, al-Mujtaba and others to not be an innovation that renders him an unbeliever; if it does, prayer behind him is not permissible. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1:658] Prolonging the prayer: he made it absolute, including whether the people count or not, whether they are pleased or not, due to the generality of the hadith. He made prolonging absolute, including prolonging the recitation, bowing, prostration, and supplications. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1:662] Women: i.e., it is prohibitively disliked for women to form a congregation with one of them as imam. If a man leads them, there is no dislike unless they are in a house where there is no other man or a mahram of the imam or his wife. If one of those mentioned is with them, there is no dislike. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 304] 'If they do so' etc.: i.e., if women pray in congregation, the imam must stand in their middle with her heel advanced. If she stands forward like a man, she sins, but the prayer is valid. al-Wast (middle) with fatha means between two ends; with sukun means what is between parts, like 'I sat in the middle of the house' with sukun. If you ask: why did the author (may Allah have mercy on him) not use the feminine for the word imam? I say: the imam is one who is followed, male or female. To the right of the imam, and it is disliked to stand to his left. [Maraqi al-Falah] Then the hermaphrodites: plural of khuntha, from men and women. [Aqrab al-Mawarid, Maraqi al-Falah (308)] Then women: if they attend, otherwise they are prohibited from attending congregations. [Maraqi al-Falah: 308]
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah regarding who is most entitled to lead the prayer (imamah). It covers both the ranking of preferred imams and the categories of imams whose leadership is disliked. The commentary draws from classical Hanafi sources like al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Fath al-Qadir, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, and Maraqi al-Falah. The author explains that the most entitled is the one with authority (sultan), then the most knowledgeable in rulings of prayer, then the best reciter (either most memorizer of Quran or best in tajweed), then the most pious (avoiding doubtful matters), then the oldest, then best character, then best appearance, then noblest lineage, then best voice, then cleanest clothes. If equal, lots are drawn or the congregation chooses. If they choose someone less entitled, they are blameworthy but the prayer is valid. The disliked imams include the slave, blind, bedouin, child of fornication, ignorant, sinful, innovator, and one who prolongs prayer. The reasoning for dislike is not due to inherent defect but because these individuals often lack knowledge and piety, leading to reduced congregational attendance. However, if such a person is actually knowledgeable and pious, the dislike disappears. For the slave, the freeborn is preferred if equal. For the innovator, only innovations that do not amount to disbelief are disliked; if the innovation is kufr, prayer behind him is invalid. Prolonging prayer is disliked even if the congregation consents. Women leading women in congregation is prohibitively disliked; if a man leads them, it is allowed unless no mahram is present. For women's congregation, the female imam stands in the middle of the row, slightly advanced. The passage also mentions the arrangement of rows: single person on the right, then men, boys, hermaphrodites, then women.

Key Terms
الأقرأ (al-aqra'): Either the one who memorizes most of the Quran or the one who recites best with tajweed and tartil.
الورع (al-wara'): Avoiding doubtful matters (shubuhat); distinct from taqwa which is avoiding clear prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ranking, if a sultan (ruler) is present but ignorant of fiqh, and a scholar is present, who should lead the prayer?
A) The ruler, because authority takes precedence.
B) The scholar, because knowledge is more important.
C) They should draw lots.
D) The congregation should vote.

Key Takeaway
The most entitled imam is the sultan, then the most knowledgeable, then the best reciter, then the most pious, etc.; choosing a lesser imam is sinful but the prayer is valid.

Salah — Prayer

Disliked Imams and the Rationale for Dislike
Listing of disliked imams and explanation of dislike rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the categories of imams whose leadership is disliked (makruh tahrimi) in the Hanafi school and explain the distinction between validity and dislike.

Core Idea
Prayer behind a disliked imam is valid but sinful for the congregation if a better qualified imam is available.

The passage continues by listing specific imams whose leadership is disliked: the slave, blind, bedouin, child of fornication, ignorant, sinful, innovator, and one who prolongs prayer. It also discusses the congregation of the naked and women. The commentary explains that the dislike is not due to any defect in the prayer itself, but because these imams typically deter people from joining the congregation, reducing the reward for the community.

Guided Path
1
List the nine disliked imams mentioned
The text enumerates: slave, blind, bedouin, child of fornication, ignorant, sinful, innovator, one who prolongs prayer, and the congregation of the naked.
The list is not exhaustive; other similar categories may be analogized.
2
Understand the reason for dislike
The commentary states that dislike is based on the lack of people's desire to follow such imams, leading to a reduction in congregational attendance.
If the imam is knowledgeable and pious despite being a slave or blind, the dislike is removed.
3
Examine the exception for the innovator (mubtadi')
If the innovation amounts to disbelief (kufr), prayer behind him is invalid. Otherwise, it is disliked.
The text cites al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that only non-kufr innovations are disliked.
4
Analyze prolongation of prayer (tatwil)
Prolonging the prayer is disliked even if the congregation consents, based on the generality of the hadith.
The prolongation includes extending recitation, bowing, prostration, or supplications.
5
Distinguish between validity and dislike
The prayer is valid if the imam meets basic conditions (Muslim, sane, can perform pillars). The dislike is separate and relates to the optimal choice.
Thus, fasting behind a blind imam is valid but makruh if a better imam is available.

العبد والأعمى والأعرابي وولد الزنا والجاهل والفاسق والمبتدع، وتطويل الصلاة، وجماعة العراة ،والنساء فإن فعلن يقف الإمام وسطهن كالعراة، ويقف

هذا الكلام بيان لشيئين الصحة والكراهة، أما الصحة فمبنية على وجود الأهلية للصلاة أداء الأركان، مع وهما موجودان من غير نقص في الشرائط، وأما الكراهة فمبنية على قلة رغبة الناس في الاقتداء بهؤلاء، فيؤدي إلى تقليل الجماعة المطلوب تكثيرها تكثيراً للأجر.
العبد: فلو اجتمع المعتق والحر الأصلي واستويا في العلم والقراءة، فالحر الأصلي أولى. [فتح القدير: ٣٠٣/١] المبتدع وهو صاحب البدعة، وهي كما في "المغرب" اسم من ابتدع، ثم غلبت على ما هو زيادة في الدين أو نقصان منه. وعرفها الشمني بأنها ما أحدث على خلاف الحق المتلقى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من علم أو عمل أو حال بنوع شبهة واستحسان، وجعل دينا قويما وصراطا مستقيما وأطلق في المبتدع فشمل كل مبتدع هو من أهل قبلتنا، وقيده في "المحيط" و"الخلاصة" و"المجتبى" وغيرها بأن لا تكون بدعة تكفره، فإن كانت تكفره فالصلاة خلفه لا تجوز [البحر الرائق: ٦٥٨/١] وتطويل الصلاة أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان القوم يحصون أو لا، رضوا بالتطويل أو لا ؛ لإطلاق الحديث، وأطلق في التطويل فشمل إطالة القراءة أو الركوع أو السجود أو الأدعية البحر الرائق: ٦٦٢/١] والنساء: أي وكره تحريما جماعة النساء بواحدة منهن، ولو أمهن رجل فلا كراهة إلا أن يكون في بيت ليس معهن فيه رجل أو محرم من الإمام أو زوجته، فإن كان واحد ممن ذكر معهنَّ فلا كراهة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٠٤] فإن فعلن إلخ أي فإن صلت النساء بالجماعة يجب أن يقف الإمام وسطهنَّ مع تقدم عقبها، فلو تقدمت كالرجل أثمت، وصحت الصلاة والوسط بالتحريك ما بين طرفي الشيء، وبالسكون لما يبين بعضه عن بعض كجلست وسط الدار بالسكون. فإن قلت لم ترك المصنف بالله التأنيث في لفظ الإمام؟ قلت: الإمام من يؤتم به ذكرا كان أو أنثى. يمين الإمام ويكره أن يقف عن يساره. مراقي الفلاح ثم الخناثي جمع الخنثى، من الرجال والنساء. أقرب الموارد، مراقي الفلاح (۳۰۸ ثم النساء: إن حضرن، وإلا فهن ممنوعات عن حضور الجماعات. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٠٨]
The Book of Prayer: 102. The Most Entitled to Lead. And no one with authority, so the most knowledgeable is most entitled to lead, then the best reciter, then the most pious, then the oldest, then the best in character, then the best in face, then the noblest in lineage, then the best in voice, then the cleanest in garment. If they are equal, lots are drawn, or the choice is for the people. If they differ, consideration is given to what the majority chooses. If they appoint other than the most entitled, they have done wrong, and it is disliked to lead: the slave, the blind man, the bedouin, the child of fornication, the ignorant, the sinful, the innovator, and prolonging the prayer, and the congregation of the naked, and women. If they do so, the imam stands in their middle like the naked. The single person stands to the right of the imam, and the majority behind him. The men are arranged, then boys, then the hermaphrodites, then women. This speech is an explanation of two things: validity and dislike. As for validity, it is based on the existence of eligibility for prayer by performing pillars, and they are present without deficiency in conditions. As for dislike, it is based on the lack of people's desire to follow these, leading to reduction of the congregation which is desired to be increased for reward. The slave: if a freed slave and a freeborn person meet and are equal in knowledge and recitation, the freeborn is more entitled. [Fath al-Qadir 1:303] The innovator: he is the one of innovation, which is as in al-Mughrib: a noun from ibtada'a, then it became prevalent for what is an addition to religion or a reduction. Al-Shumunni defined it as what is introduced contrary to the truth received from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, from knowledge or action or state, by kind of doubt and approval, and made a straight religion and path. It is general for every innovator who is of our qibla. It is restricted in al-Muhit, al-Khulasah, al-Mujtaba and others to not be an innovation that renders him an unbeliever; if it does, prayer behind him is not permissible. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1:658] Prolonging the prayer: he made it absolute, including whether the people count or not, whether they are pleased or not, due to the generality of the hadith. He made prolonging absolute, including prolonging the recitation, bowing, prostration, and supplications. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1:662] Women: i.e., it is prohibitively disliked for women to form a congregation with one of them as imam. If a man leads them, there is no dislike unless they are in a house where there is no other man or a mahram of the imam or his wife. If one of those mentioned is with them, there is no dislike. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 304] 'If they do so' etc.: i.e., if women pray in congregation, the imam must stand in their middle with her heel advanced. If she stands forward like a man, she sins, but the prayer is valid. al-Wast (middle) with fatha means between two ends; with sukun means what is between parts, like 'I sat in the middle of the house' with sukun. If you ask: why did the author (may Allah have mercy on him) not use the feminine for the word imam? I say: the imam is one who is followed, male or female. To the right of the imam, and it is disliked to stand to his left. [Maraqi al-Falah] Then the hermaphrodites: plural of khuntha, from men and women. [Aqrab al-Mawarid, Maraqi al-Falah (308)] Then women: if they attend, otherwise they are prohibited from attending congregations. [Maraqi al-Falah: 308]
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah regarding who is most entitled to lead the prayer (imamah). It covers both the ranking of preferred imams and the categories of imams whose leadership is disliked. The commentary draws from classical Hanafi sources like al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Fath al-Qadir, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, and Maraqi al-Falah. The author explains that the most entitled is the one with authority (sultan), then the most knowledgeable in rulings of prayer, then the best reciter (either most memorizer of Quran or best in tajweed), then the most pious (avoiding doubtful matters), then the oldest, then best character, then best appearance, then noblest lineage, then best voice, then cleanest clothes. If equal, lots are drawn or the congregation chooses. If they choose someone less entitled, they are blameworthy but the prayer is valid. The disliked imams include the slave, blind, bedouin, child of fornication, ignorant, sinful, innovator, and one who prolongs prayer. The reasoning for dislike is not due to inherent defect but because these individuals often lack knowledge and piety, leading to reduced congregational attendance. However, if such a person is actually knowledgeable and pious, the dislike disappears. For the slave, the freeborn is preferred if equal. For the innovator, only innovations that do not amount to disbelief are disliked; if the innovation is kufr, prayer behind him is invalid. Prolonging prayer is disliked even if the congregation consents. Women leading women in congregation is prohibitively disliked; if a man leads them, it is allowed unless no mahram is present. For women's congregation, the female imam stands in the middle of the row, slightly advanced. The passage also mentions the arrangement of rows: single person on the right, then men, boys, hermaphrodites, then women.

Key Terms
المبتدع (al-mubtadi'): One who introduces an innovation (bid'ah) in religion contrary to the sunnah, but not amounting to disbelief.
كراهة تحريما (karahah tahrimee): A prohibition-level dislike; sin if done, but still valid with compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if an imam prolongs the prayer despite the congregation's satisfaction, what is the ruling?
A) It is permissible as long as they consent.
B) It is disliked (makruh tahrimi) even if they consent.
C) It is invalid because it changes the prayer.
D) It is recommended to prolong.

Key Takeaway
The listed imams are disliked only when they lack knowledge and piety; if qualified, the dislike is removed, and the prayer is valid in all cases.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings on Imamah: Validity and Dislike
Lists imams whose prayer is valid but disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between validity and dislike in imamah, and identify which types of imams make the prayer valid but disliked according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Prayer behind a slave, blind, Bedouin, illegitimate, ignorant, sinner, or innovator is valid but disliked, because it reduces the congregation's reward.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lists specific imams whose prayer is valid yet disliked. The commentary immediately clarifies that we are dealing with two separate aspects: validity (sihha) and dislike (karaha). Validity is affirmed because these individuals possess basic eligibility for prayer—they can perform the pillars—and the conditions are met. Dislike, however, is based on the principle that following such imams reduces people's desire to join the congregation, thereby diminishing the reward that comes with larger gatherings. Understanding this distinction is essential for applying the rulings correctly in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list of imams
Read the matn list: slave, blind, Bedouin, illegitimate child, ignorant, sinner, innovator, and also prolonging prayer, naked congregation, and women's congregation. These are the types whose imamah is discussed.
The commentary later adds details about each, including the critical exception for kufr innovation.
2
Distinguish validity from dislike
The commentary explains that validity is based on existence of eligibility (ahliyya) and performing pillars, while dislike is based on reducing the congregation's size and reward. Recognise that both coexist; validity is not affected by the dislike.
This is a key Hanafi principle: the act can be valid yet disliked.
3
Apply the levels of dislike
Identify that most cases are makruh tanzih (lightly disliked), but women's congregation led by a woman is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). Note that if a man leads women, there is no dislike unless no other man or mahram is present.
The distinction between tanzih and tahrimi affects the degree of sin and recommendation to avoid.
4
Note the kufr innovation exception
The commentary restricts the innovator (mubtadi') to those whose innovation is not kufr. If the innovation is kufr, prayer behind such an imam is invalid. This is a crucial boundary.
This exception shows that the dislike is not absolute; it depends on the nature of the innovation.

The Book of Prayer. 103. The Most Entitled to Imamah: The slave, the blind, the Bedouin, the illegitimate child, the ignorant, the sinner, the innovator, and prolonging prayer, and the congregation of the naked, and women. If they do it, the imam stands in their middle like the naked. And one person stands to the right of the imam and the majority behind him. And the men are arranged, then the boys, then the hermaphrodites, whether male or a discerning boy, then the women. This speech is an explanation of two things: validity and dislike. As for validity, it is based on the existence of eligibility for prayer by performing the pillars, and both exist with no deficiency in conditions. As for dislike, it is based on the lack of people's desire to follow these people, which leads to reducing the congregation whose increase is desired for increase of reward. The slave: if a freed slave and a freeborn person gather and are equal in knowledge and recitation, the freeborn is more entitled. [Fath al-Qadir 1/303] The innovator: he is the one who commits innovation, and it is, as in al-Mughrib, a noun derived from ibtada'a, then it became prevalent for what is an addition to the religion or a reduction from it. Al-Shumunni defined it as something invented contrary to the truth received from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in knowledge, action, or state, by way of some doubt and approval, and made into a strong religion and a straight path. The word innovator is general, including every innovator who is of our qibla, but it is restricted in al-Muhit, al-Khulasa, al-Mujtaba, etc., that the innovation must not be a kufr innovation. If it is a kufr innovation, then prayer behind him is not permissible. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/658] And prolonging prayer: it is general, including whether the people count or not, whether they are pleased with prolongation or not, due to the generality of the hadith. And prolongation is general, including prolongation of recitation, bowing, prostration, or supplications. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/662] And women: i.e., the congregation of women led by one of them is makruh tahrimi. If a man leads them, then there is no dislike unless it is in a house where there is no man or mahram of the imam or his wife with them. If there is one of those mentioned with them, then no dislike. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 304] 'If they do it, etc.' i.e., if women pray in congregation, the imam must stand in their middle with her heel advanced. If she stands forward like a man, she sins, but the prayer is valid. al-Wasat (with fatha) means between the two ends of something, and with sukun means what separates some from others, like 'I sat in the middle of the house' with sukun. If you say: why did the author omit the feminine ending in the word 'imam'? I say: al-imam is one who is followed, whether male or female. The right of the imam: it is disliked to stand to his left. [Maraqi al-Falah] Then the hermaphrodites: plural of khuntha, from males and females. [Aqrab al-Mawarid, Maraqi al-Falah 308] Then women: if they attend, otherwise they are prevented from attending congregations. [Maraqi al-Falah 308]
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Nur al-Idah, expanded by the sharh. It addresses the issue of who is most entitled to lead prayer, but the focus is on imams whose prayer is valid yet disliked. The matn lists specific individuals: a slave, a blind person, a Bedouin, an illegitimate child, an ignorant person, a sinner, an innovator, and also mentions prolonging prayer, the congregation of naked people, and women's congregation. The commentary immediately clarifies that this passage pertains to two aspects: validity (sihha) and dislike (karaha). Validity is affirmed because these individuals possess the requisite eligibility (ahliyya) for prayer—they can perform the pillars—and the conditions are met. Dislike, however, is based on the principle that following such imams reduces people's desire to join the congregation, thereby diminishing the reward associated with large congregations, which is encouraged to be multiplied. The commentary then elaborates on each item. For the slave, it gives a rule of preference: if a freed slave (mu'taq) and a freeborn person (hurr asli) are equal in knowledge and recitation, the freeborn is more entitled. For the innovator (mubtadi'), it provides a detailed definition from al-Mughrib and al-Shumunni, and crucially distinguishes between innovations that do not constitute kufr and those that do. If the innovation is kufr, prayer behind such an imam is not permissible (la tujuz); otherwise, it is valid but disliked. Prolonging prayer (tatwil al-salat) is disliked regardless of whether the followers count or approve, based on the general import of hadith, and includes prolonging any part of the prayer. Women's congregation led by a woman is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). If a man leads them, there is no dislike unless there is no other man or mahram present. The commentary also addresses the positioning of the imam (in the middle for women) and the arrangement of rows: men first, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women. It ends by noting that women are generally prevented from attending congregational prayers unless they do attend, and even then, certain rules apply. The overall ruling is that the prayer is valid, but it is better to avoid such imams to encourage larger congregations.

Key Terms
المبتدع (al-mubtadi'): One who introduces an innovation in religion that contradicts the transmitted truth, but not necessarily kufr.
كراهة تحريما (karahah tahrīman): Prohibitive dislike, closer to haram but not as severe; requires leaving the disliked act.
الجماعة (al-jamā'ah): Congregational prayer; its increase is desired for multiplying reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a woman leading women in congregational prayer?
A) It is valid and recommended
B) It is valid but makruh tahrimi
C) It is invalid and sinful
D) It is valid and there is no dislike

Key Takeaway
Prayer behind an imam who is a slave, blind, Bedouin, illegitimate, ignorant, sinner, or non-kufr innovator is valid but disliked to avoid reducing congregational reward.

Three Types of Followers in Congregational Prayer
Definition and rulings of follower types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mudrik, lahiq, and masbuq, and state the rulings for each regarding tashahhud, tasbih, and making up missed rak'ahs.

Core Idea
The follower is either mudrik, lahiq, or masbuq; each has distinct obligations after the imam finishes.

This passage from Nur al-Idah categorizes followers into three types and clarifies their responsibilities after the imam finishes. Understanding these categories is essential for correctly performing congregational prayer and for making up missed parts without invalidating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The text divides the follower (muqtadi) into mudrik, lahiq, and masbuq. Mudrik performed all rak'ahs with the imam; lahiq entered with the imam but missed parts due to an excuse; masbuq joined late and missed one or more rak'ahs.
These categories are unique to Hanafi fiqh and affect how the follower makes up missed parts.
2
Understand the ruling for each type regarding tashahhud and tasbih
If the imam says salam before the mudrik or lahiq finishes tashahhud, the follower completes it (wajib). If the imam raises his head before the follower completes three tasbihs in ruku/sujud, the follower must follow immediately.
Completing tashahhud is obligatory; but following the imam in actions (like raising from ruku) takes precedence over completing optional tasbihs.
3
Learn the rules for making up missed parts
The lahiq makes up missed parts without recitation (surah) and does not perform sajdah sahw for the imam's forgetfulness. The masbuq makes up the first part of his prayer with recitation and the last part with tashahhud.
The order of making up for a lahiq who is also masbuq is important: first pray what was missed without recitation, then with recitation.
4
Recognize the dispute with Zufar on order of making up
According to Abu Hanifa, the follower must pray the missed parts in order: first what was missed without recitation, then with recitation. Zufar allows reversing this order. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's.
Reversing the order is considered sinful (ithm) but the prayer is valid.
5
Apply the rules to a scenario
For example, if a follower joins late (masbuq) and the imam forgetfully adds an extra sajdah, the follower should not follow; instead, he completes his own prayer alone after the imam.
The follower must not follow the imam in forgetful additions (like an extra rak'ah or sajdah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بعدم جواز
قيدها : أي الركعة الزائدة بسجدة . مراقي (الفلاح سلم ولا ينتظر بخروجه إلى غير صلاته. (مراقي الفلاح)
The Book of Prayer. 104. What the follower does after his imam finishes. Chapter on what the follower does after his imam finishes, of obligatory and other. If the imam says salam before the follower finishes the tashahhud, he completes it. If the imam raises his head before the follower's three tasbihs in ruku or sujud, he follows him. If the imam adds a sajdah or stands after the last sitting forgetfully, the follower does not follow him. And if he ties it (the added rak'ah) with a sajdah, he says salam alone. And he glorifies to alert his imam. The follower: Know that the follower is of three types: mudrik, lahiq, and masbuq. Mudrik: one who prays all the rak'ahs with the imam. Lahiq: one who entered with him but missed all or some due to sleep, heedlessness, crowding, preceding hadath, or a resident behind a traveler. His ruling is like a real follower, so he does not recite or perform sahw in what he makes up, his fard does not change to four by intention of residence, he begins with making up what he missed, then follows his imam if possible so that he may then say salam with him, otherwise he follows, and he does not engage in making up until the imam finishes his prayer, and he does not prostrate with the imam for the imam's sahw, but stands for making up then prostrates for that after completion, and he does not sit for the second if the imam does not sit, and he does not follow him. If he is also masbuq and stands for making up, he prays first what he slept on, for example, without recitation, then prays what he missed with recitation. And if he reverses it, according to us it is contrary to Zufar, and he sins for abandoning the order as in al-Fath and others. Masbuq: one whom the imam preceded in all or some of the prayer. His ruling is that he makes up the first of his prayer in terms of recitation and the last in terms of sitting. He is alone in what he makes up except in four, he may not be followed nor follow, and he performs the takbirs of tashriq by consensus. If he says takbir intending to start the prayer, he becomes a fresh starter. If he stands to make up what he was preceded in and his imam prostrates for sahw, he follows him in it if he has not tied the rak'ah with a sajdah. If he does not follow him, he prostrates at the end of his prayer. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 309] And other: it is connected to his saying 'what he does' meaning and what he does not do, like if the imam raises his head before the follower's three tasbihs; then he does not complete them, and other possibilities. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 309] He completes it because completing tashahhud is obligatory, and after that he says salam because he is in the state of prayer, and combining them is possible. It is restricted by 'before the follower finishes' because after he finishes he says salam with the imam, and by 'from the tashahhud' to indicate that if there remain prayers and supplications, he leaves them and says salam with the imam, because leaving the sunnah is like leaving the obligatory. If the imam stands for the third and the follower has not completed tashahhud, he completes it, and if he does not complete it, it is permissible. He follows him: this is the correct position of the school. Some say: he completes them three because the scholars said three by reducing them from three. [Maraqi al-Falah 310] Sahin is the state of each of the implied subjects in his saying 'added' and 'stood'. He tied it: i.e., the extra rak'ah with a sajdah. [Maraqi al-Falah] He says salam and does not wait with his exit for something outside his prayer. [Maraqi al-Falah]
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling that categorizes the follower (muqtadi) into three types and explains their respective rulings. It begins with a chapter on what the follower does after the imam finishes, covering obligatory and other actions. Specific scenarios are given: if the imam says salam before the follower finishes tashahhud, the follower completes it and then says salam; if the imam raises his head before the follower completes three tasbihs, the follower follows; if the imam forgetfully adds a sajdah or stands after the final sitting, the follower does not follow; if the imam ties the extra rak'ah to a sajdah, the follower says salam alone. The follower may also glorify to alert his imam. The commentary then defines the three types: Mudrik: one who completes all rak'ahs with the imam. Lahiq: one who entered with the imam but missed some parts due to sleep, forgetfulness, crowding, a preceding minor impurity (hadath), or a resident behind a traveler. The lahiq's ruling is like a real follower: he does not recite in what he makes up, does not perform sahw, his fard obligation remains as is, he must make up what he missed after the imam finishes, he follows the imam when possible, and he does not prostrate with the imam for the imam's sahw. If the lahiq is also masbuq (i.e., he missed some rak'ahs), he must first pray what he missed without recitation, then what he was preceded in with recitation; reversing this order is sinful according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Zufar. Masbuq: one whom the imam preceded in all or some rak'ahs. The masbuq's ruling is that he makes up the first part of his prayer in terms of recitation (i.e., the opening of his own prayer) and the last part in terms of sitting. He is considered alone (munfarid) in what he makes up, except in four matters where he cannot be followed nor follow. He must perform the takbirs of tashriq if applicable. If he intends to start a new prayer, he becomes a fresh starter. If he stands to make up and the imam prostrates for sahw, he follows if he has not yet tied his rak'ah with a sajdah; otherwise, he prostrates at the end of his own prayer. The commentary ends with additional notes from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah, emphasizing that completing tashahhud is obligatory and the follower must prioritize following the imam unless it contradicts an obligation.

Key Terms
المدرك (al-mudrik): One who performed all rak'ahs with the imam from start to finish.
اللاحق (al-lāḥiq): One who entered with the imam but missed some or all parts due to specific reasons like sleep or hadath.
المسبوق (al-masbūq): One who missed one or more rak'ahs with the imam and joins later.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The sitting of recitation (attahiyyat) in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a follower do if the imam says salam before the follower has completed the tashahhud?
A) Immediately say salam with the imam
B) Complete the tashahhud and then say salam
C) Continue reciting and then follow the imam
D) Make up the tashahhud after the imam finishes

Key Takeaway
The follower in congregational prayer is either mudrik, lahiq, or masbuq; each has specific duties after the imam finishes, and the follower must not follow the imam in forgetful additions.

The Three Types of Followers in Salah
Definitions and rulings for mudrik, lahiq, and masbuq in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the three types of followers in Hanafi salah and state the key rulings for each, including the order of makeup for a masbuq who was also lahiq.

Core Idea
The lahiq makes up without recitation; the masbuq makes up with recitation; reversing the order is sinful.

In congregational prayer, followers are categorized based on when they joined and whether they missed parts due to valid excuses. Understanding these categories is essential for correctly performing makeup prayers after the imam completes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
From the first line of the passage, list the three types of followers: mudrik, lahiq, and masbuq.
These are the only three categories; no other exists.
2
Define each type
For each type, extract the defining characteristic: mudrik attends all rak'ahs with imam; lahiq enters early but misses some due to a valid excuse (e.g., sleep); masbuq enters late and misses part without an excuse.
The excuse distinguishes lahiq from masbuq.
3
Extract the ruling for each
For lahiq: no recitation or sahw in makeup, must wait until imam finishes, and does not follow imam's sahw. For masbuq: recites in the first part of makeup, sits in the last part, and follows imam in sahw if the rak'ah is not yet tied.
The lahiq remains a true follower (mu'tamm) during makeup.
4
Handle the combined case
If someone is both lahiq and masbuq (e.g., slept then was preceded), he must first make up the lahiq part without recitation, then the masbuq part with recitation. Reversing this order is sinful according to the Hanafi majority, contrary to Zufar.
The dispute with Zufar is noted in the text; the relied-upon position is that reversal incurs sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقتدي: اعلم أن المقتدي ثلاثة أقسام مدرك ولاحق، ومسبوق، فالمدرك: من صلى الركعات كلها مع الإمام. واللاحق هو من دخل معه وفاته كلها أو بعضها بأن عرض له نوم أو غفلة أو زحمة أو سبق حدث أو كان مقيما خلف مسافر وحكمه كمؤتم حقيقة، فلا يأتي فيما يقضي بقراءة ولا سهو ولا يتغير فرضه أربعا بنية الإقامة، ويبدأ بقضاء ما فاته، ثم يتبع إمامه إن أمكنه أن که بعد ذلك فيسلم معه وإلا تابعه، ولا يشتغل بالقضاء حتى يفرغ الإمام من صلاته ولا يسجد مع الإمام بسهو الإمام، بل يقوم للقضاء ثم يسجد عن ذلك بعد الختم، ولا يقعد عن الثانية إذا لم يقعد الإمام، ولا يقتدي به. صح يدر فإن كان مسبوقا أيضا فقام للقضاء، فإنه يصلي أولا ما نام فيه مثلا بلا قراءة ثم يصلي ما سبق به بها، ولو عكس عندنا خلافا لزفر، وأثم لترك الترتيب كما في "الفتح" وغيره والمسبوق هو من سبقه الإمام بكلها أو بعضها، وحكمه أنه يقضي أول صلاته في حق القراءة، وآخرها في حق القعدة، وهو منفرد فيما يقضيه إلا في أربع لا يجوز اقتداؤه، ولا الاقتداء به، ويأتي بتكبيرات التشريق إجماعا، ولو كبر ينوي الاستيناف للصلاة يصير مستأنفا، ولو قام لقضاء ما سبق به وسجد إمامه لسهو تابعه فيه إن لم يقيد الركعة بسجدة، فإن لم يتابعه سجد في آخر صلاته.
The follower: Know that the follower is three types: mudrik, lahiq, and masbuq. The mudrik is the one who performed all the rak'ahs with the imam. The lahiq is the one who entered with him but missed all or some due to sleep, heedlessness, crowding, preceding hadath, or being a resident behind a traveller; his ruling is truly that of a mu'tamm (follower), so he does not recite or perform sahw in what he makes up, his fard does not change to four by intention of residence, he begins by making up what he missed, then follows his imam if possible so that he says salam with him, otherwise he follows him, and he does not busy himself with making up until the imam finishes his prayer, and he does not prostrate with the imam for the imam's sahw, but stands for making up then prostrates for that after completing, and he does not sit for the second if the imam did not sit, and he does not follow him. 'Sah' (correct) 'yadir'? If he was also masbuq and stood to make up, he first prays what he slept in, for example, without recitation, then prays what he was preceded in with recitation; if he reverses, in our view contrary to Zufar, he sins for leaving order as in al-Fath and others. The masbuq is the one the imam preceded him in all or some; his ruling is that he makes up the first part of his prayer in terms of recitation and the last part in terms of sitting, and he is alone in what he makes up except in four (cases): he is not allowed to be followed, nor to follow another; he says the takbirs of tashriq by consensus; if he says takbir intending to restart prayer, he becomes a restarting one; if he stands to make up what he was preceded in and his imam prostrates for sahw, he follows him in it if he has not tied the rak'ah with a prostration, otherwise he prostrates at the end of his prayer.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage defines the three types of followers in congregational prayer. The mudrik is the normal follower who completes the whole prayer with the imam. The lahiq is one who joined the imam but missed part due to a valid excuse (sleep, forgetfulness, crowd, etc.). His ruling is like a regular follower in his makeup: no recitation, no sahw, and he must make up missed parts after the imam finishes, then follow. The masbuq is one who missed part without excuse; he makes up his prayer with recitation and sitting accordingly, and is considered alone in makeup except in four matters. The passage also mentions that if a masbuq reverses the order, he sins. Zufar disagreed. The masbuq follows the imam in sahw prostration if he hasn't tied the rak'ah, otherwise prostrates later.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): A follower who performed all rak'ahs with the imam from start to end.
لاحق (lahiq): A follower who joined the imam early but missed some part due to a valid excuse like sleep or forgetfulness.
مسبوق (masbuq): A follower who joined the imam late and missed part without a valid excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He makes up missed parts immediately.
B) He waits until the imam finishes to start his makeup.
C) He recites fatihah silently while waiting.
D) He leaves the congregation.

Key Takeaway
The three categories of followers have distinct rules for makeup: the lahiq does not recite, the masbuq does, and in combined cases, order matters and reversal is sinful.

Rulings for the Follower After the Imam Finishes
Rulings on follower's actions when imam finishes prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for a follower after the imam finishes, identify when to follow and when not to, and explain the rationale behind completing the tashahhud.

Core Idea
The follower completes wajib acts (tashahhud) but follows the imam in sunan; he does not follow in forgetful extra acts.

When praying in congregation, the follower (muqtadi) must sometimes follow the imam immediately and other times complete his own recitation. This lesson clarifies the specific scenarios after the imam finishes. Understanding these distinctions ensures the follower's prayer remains valid and avoids common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the follower's action
Determine what the follower is doing when the imam finishes: completing tashahhud, saying tasbihat, or reacting to an imam's extra rak'ah.
The passage covers multiple scenarios.
2
Classify the obligation level
Determine whether the action is wajib (e.g., tashahhud) or sunnah (e.g., tasbihat). This decides whether to follow the imam or complete the action.
Hanafis consider tashahhud wajib, not a rukn.
3
Apply the follow-or-complete rule
If the action is wajib, complete it even if the imam moves on. If it is sunnah, follow the imam immediately.
4
Recognize exceptions for the imam's forgetful actions
If the imam adds a sajdah or stands from the final sitting forgetfully, the follower does not follow. He waits or says salam alone if the imam ties the extra rak'ah with a prostration.
‘Forgetfully’ (sahwan) is the key condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يفعله المقتدي بعد فراغ إمامه من واجب وغيره لوسلم الإمام قبل فراغ المقتدي من التشهد يتمه، ولو رفع الإمام رأسه قبل تسبيح المقتدي ثلاثا في الركوع أو السجود يتابعه، ولو زاد الإمام سجدة أو قام بعد القعود الأخير ساهيا لا يتبعه المؤتم، وإن قيدها سلم وحده، وسبح ليتنبه إمامه. يتمه لأن إتمام التشهد من الواجبات وبعد ذلك يسلم؛ لأنه في تحريمة الصلاة، والجمع بالإتيان بهما ممكن قيد بقوله قبل فراغ المقتدي؛ لأنه بعد فراغه يسلم مع الإمام وبقوله: "من التشهد" لإفادة أنها إن بقيت الصلوات والدعوات يتركها ويسلم مع الإمام؛ لأن ترك السنة ترك الواجب، ولو قام الإمام إلى الثالثة ولم يتم المقتدي التشهد أتمه، وإن لم يتمه جاز. يتابعه هذا على الصحيح من المذهب، ومنهم من قال: يتمها ثلاثا؛ لأن أهل العلم من قال الثلاث بتنقيصها عن الثلاث. ساهيا حال من كل من المستترين في قوله: "زاد" و"قام". قيدها: أي الركعة الزائدة بسجدة. سلم ولا ينتظر بخروجه إلى غير صلاته. وإن قام الإمام قبل القعود الأخير ساهيا انتظره المأموم، فإن سلم المقتدي قبل أن يقيد إمامه الزائدة بسجدة فسد فرضه وكره سلام المقتدي بعد تشهد الإمام قبل سلامه. الركعة تحريما.
Chapter on what the follower does after his imam finishes of obligatory and other matters: If the imam says salam before the follower completes the tashahhud, he completes it. If the imam raises his head before the follower completes three tasbihat in bowing or prostration, he follows him. If the imam adds a prostration or stands after the final sitting forgetfully, the follower does not follow him. And if he ties it (the extra rak'ah) with a sajdah, he says salam alone, and he says subhanallah to alert his imam. He completes it because completing tashahhud is obligatory, and after that he says salam because he is still in the tahrimah of prayer, and combining both is possible. It is restricted by his saying 'before the follower finishes' because after he finishes, he says salam with the imam, and by his saying 'from the tashahhud' to indicate that if remaining prayers and supplications (remain), he leaves them and says salam with the imam, because leaving a sunnah is leaving an obligatory act. If the imam stands for the third and the follower has not completed the tashahhud, he completes it, and if he does not complete it, it is permissible. He follows him; this is the correct view of the school. Some said he completes three because the people of knowledge said three is diminished from three. 'Forgetfully' is a condition for each of the implied subjects in his words 'added' and 'stood'. 'Tied it' means the extra rak'ah with a prostration. He says salam and does not wait, exiting to his other prayer. And if the imam stands before the final sitting forgetfully, the follower waits for him. If the follower says salam before his imam ties the extra rak'ah with a prostration, his obligatory prayer is invalidated, and it is prohibitively disliked for the follower to say salam after the imam's tashahhud before his salam.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage states rulings for the follower (muqtadi) after the imam finishes. The follower must complete the tashahhud if the imam says salam before he finishes, because tashahhud is wajib. He follows the imam in raising the head before completing three tasbihat, but does not follow if the imam adds a sajdah or stands forgetfully from the final sitting. If the imam ties an extra rak'ah with a prostration, the follower says salam alone. The commentary explains that the follower completes tashahhud because it is obligatory, and then says salam, as he is still in prayer. If the follower does not complete it, he must follow the imam after completing. The ruling about the imam standing before the final sitting requires the follower to wait; if the follower says salam beforehand, his prayer is invalid.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The person who prays behind an imam as a follower.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of 'Attahiyyat' during the sitting in prayer.
قيدها (qayyadaha): Connecting the extra rak'ah with a prostration (sajdah) to complete it.
تسبيح (tasbih): The glorification of Allah, e.g., 'Subhana rabbiyal 'azim' in ruku.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a follower do if the imam says salam before the follower completes the tashahhud?
A) Immediately say salam with the imam.
B) Complete the tashahhud and then say salam.
C) Skip the tashahhud and say salam.
D) Repeat the tashahhud after the imam.

Key Takeaway
The follower completes wajib acts like tashahhud but follows the imam in sunan; he does not follow the imam in forgetful extra acts, and saying salam prematurely can invalidate his prayer.

Post-Prayer Supplications and Sunan
Rulings on recommended acts after obligatory prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts after obligatory prayer in the Hanafi school and explain the preferred timing for post-prayer adhkar.

Core Idea
It is best to perform post-prayer adhkar after the sunnah prayer, not between fard and sunnah.

After completing an obligatory prayer, various sunan and adhkar are recommended. However, there is a scholarly discussion on the best timing: should these be recited immediately after the fard or after the sunnah prayer that follows? This passage from Nur al-Idah provides the Hanafi ruling on this matter, clarifying the preferred practice and addressing common actions that may affect the reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts after fard
List the sunan: standing for sunnah immediately, imam turning to his left, reciting specific du'a and adhkar after the sunnah.
2
Understand the ikhtilaf on timing
Some scholars (al-Halwani) permit awrad between fard and sunnah; the preferred view delays them until after the sunnah.
3
Apply the preferred Hanafi view
Follow the sequence: fard, brief du'a, sunnah, then adhkar (Ayat al-Kursi, mu'awwidhat, tasbih 33 each).
4
Know the effect of disruptions
Talking, eating, or drinking between fard and sunnah does not invalidate the fard but decreases the reward of the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأذكار الواردة بعد الفرض: القيام إلى السنة متصلا بالفرض مسنون، وعن شمس الأئمة الحلواني: لا بأس بقراءة الأوراد بين الفريضة والسنة، ويستحب للإمام بعد سلامه أن يتحول إلى يساره لتطوع بعد الفرض، وأن يستقبل بعده الناس ويستغفرون الله ويقرؤون آية الكرسي والمعوذات، ويسبحون الله ثلاثا وثلاثين ويحمدونه كذلك، ويكبرونه كذلك. متصلاً: لكنه يستحب الفصل بينهما كما كان عليه إذا سلم يمكث قدر ما يقول: اللهم أنت السلام، ومنك السلام، وإليك يعود السلام، تباركت يا ذا الجلال والإكرام، ثم يقوم إلى السنة. لا بأس بقراءة إلخ: فالأولى تأخير الأوراد عن السنة فهذا ينفي الكراهة، ويخالفه ما قال في "الاختيار": كل صلاة بعدها سنة يكره القعود بعدها والدعاء، بل يشتغل بالسنة كي لا يفصل بين السنة والمكتوبة، ثم قال الكمال: ولم يثبت عنه الفصل بالأذكار التي يواظب عليها في المساجد في عصرنا من قراءة آية الكرسي والتسبيحات وأخواتها ثلاثا وثلاثين وغيرها، وقوله تسبحون، وتكبرون، وتحمدون كل صلاة إلخ لا يقتضي وصلها بالفرض، بل كونها عقب السنة من غير اشتغال بما ليس من توابع الصلاة، فصح كونها دبرها. وإذا تكلم بكلام كثير أو أكل أو شرب بين الفرض والسنة لا تبطل، وهو الأصح، بل نقص ثوابها. أن يتحول إلخ أي: يتحول إلى يمين القبلة، وهو الجانب المقابل إلى جهة يساره أي يسار المستقبل؛ لأن يمين المقابل جهة يسار المستقبل، فيتحول إليه. أن يستقبل إلخ: أي ويستحب أن يستقبل بعد التطوع عقب الفرض، وإن لم يكن بعده نافلة يستقبل الناس إن لم يكن في مقابلة مصل. والمعوذات فيه تغليب والمراد الصمدية والمعوذتان. ثلاثا وثلاثين فإن قلت: هل الشرط في تحصيل السنة والفضل الموعود به أن يقول الذكر المنصوص عليه بالعدد متتابعا أم لا، وفي مجلس واحد أم لا؟ قلت: وكل ذلك ليس بشرط، لكن الأفضل أن يأتي به متتابعا في الوقت الذي عين فيه.
Chapter on the supplications reported after the obligatory prayer: Standing for the sunnah (supererogatory) immediately after the fard is sunnah. From Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani: There is no harm in reciting the awrad (adhkar) between the fard and sunnah. It is recommended for the imam after his salam to turn to his left for voluntary prayer after the fard, and to face the people afterwards, and they ask forgiveness of Allah and recite Ayat al-Kursi and al-Mu'awwidhat, and say subhanallah 33 times, alhamdulillah 33 times, and Allahu akbar 33 times. Immediately: But it is recommended to separate between them as was his practice: when he said salam, he would pause for the time it takes to say: 'Allahumma anta al-salam wa minka al-salam wa ilayka ya'ud al-salam, tabarakta ya dha al-jalali wa al-ikram', then stand for the sunnah. 'There is no harm' etc: So it is better to delay the awrad after the sunnah; this negates dislike. It contradicts what is said in al-Ikhtiyar: every prayer after which there is a sunnah, it is disliked to sit and make du'a after it; rather one should occupy oneself with the sunnah so as not to separate between the sunnah and the obligatory. Then al-Kamal said: It is not proven from him (the Prophet) to separate with the adhkar that are regularly practiced in our time in mosques of reciting Ayat al-Kursi, tasbihat, and their likes 33 times etc. And his saying 'you glorify, magnify, praise after every prayer' does not require connecting them to the fard, but rather they are after the sunnah without occupying with what is not from the accessories of prayer, so it is correct that they are its (the fard's) after. If one talks a lot or eats or drinks between the fard and sunnah, it does not invalidate (the prayer), and this is the more correct view, but it decreases its reward. 'Turn' etc means: he turns to the right of the qibla, which is the side opposite to his left, i.e., the left of the one facing (the qibla); because the right of the opposite is the left of the one facing, so he turns to it. 'Face' etc means: and it is recommended that he faces after the voluntary prayer following the fard, and if there is no nafl after it, he faces the people if he is not in front of a person praying. 'al-Mu'awwidhat' here is a generalization; the intended are al-Samadiyyah (al-Ikhlas) and al-Mu'awwidhatan (al-Falaq and al-Nas). 'Thirty-three': If you ask: Is the condition for attaining the sunnah and the promised reward that one recites the prescribed dhikr with the number consecutively or not, and in one sitting or not? I say: All that is not a condition, but it is better to recite it consecutively at the time specified.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage discusses the adhkar after the obligatory prayer. It states that standing for the sunnah immediately after fard is sunnah. There is a difference of opinion: some say reciting awrad between fard and sunnah is permissible, while others recommend separating them with the specific du'a mentioned. The commentary resolves that it is better to delay the awrad until after the sunnah to avoid separating between fard and sunnah, but it is not disliked to do them between. It also states that talking or eating between fard and sunnah does not invalidate the fard, but decreases reward. The imam turning to his left (i.e., right of qibla) is recommended. Reciting Ayat al-Kursi and the three surahs (Ikhlas, Falaq, Nas) and tasbih 33 times after the sunnah is recommended. It clarifies that the dhikr does not have to be consecutive or in one sitting to get the reward.

Key Terms
الأوراد (al-awrad): Non-obligatory supplications and recitations, specifically those after prayer.
المعوذات (al-mu'awwidhat): The three surahs: al-Ikhlas, al-Falaq, and al-Nas, used for seeking protection.
التسبيحات (al-tasbihat): The phrases subhanallah, alhamdulillah, Allahu akbar repeated 33 times each.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, when should the post-fard adhkar (like tasbih) be recited?
A) Immediately after the fard prayer before standing for sunnah.
B) After the sunnah prayer that follows the fard.
C) During the fard prayer itself.
D) At any time during the day.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi practice is to perform the post-prayer adhkar after the sunnah prayer, not between the fard and sunnah.
