Ruling on Follower's Salaam When Imam Forgets Final Sitting
Ruling on imam's inadvertent standing and follower's salaam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two rulings for a follower's salaam when the imam forgets the final sitting and apply them to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
Salaam before imam's sujud al-sahw invalidates; after tashahhud but before imam's salaam is disliked.

In congregational prayer, the imam may forget the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) and stand up inadvertently. What should the follower do? This lesson unpacks the ruling from Nur al-Idah, clarifying when the follower's salaam breaks the prayer and when it is merely discouraged. Understanding these nuances preserves the validity of your congregational prayer and prevents common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the imam's error
The imam stands up before performing the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) due to forgetfulness. The follower must recognize this error and know the correct response.
The final sitting is wajib in the Hanafi school.
2
Determine the follower's required action
The follower must wait for the imam to realise his mistake and return to the sitting position. The follower should not act prematurely.
3
Analyze the consequence of premature salaam
If the follower gives salaam before the imam performs the two prostrations of forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw), his fard prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
The imam's sujud al-sahw is essential to complete the prayer after forgetfulness.
4
Analyze the consequence of late salaam
If the follower gives salaam after the imam's tashahhud but before the imam's own salaam, the prayer is valid but it is disliked (makruh).
Disliked because it violates the ideal of following the imam until the end.
5
Distinguish the two scenarios
The key difference is whether the follower's salaam occurs before or after the imam's sujud al-sahw. Early salaam severs the connection before the imam completes the prayer; late salaam still occurs within the imam's prayer but prematurely.
This distinction is crucial for correct practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قام الإمام قبل القعود الأخير ساهيا انتظره المأموم، فإن سلم المقتدي قبل أن يقيد إمامه الزائدة بسجدة فسد فرضه وكره سلام المقتدي بعد تشهد الإمام قبل سلامه.
And if the imam stands up before the final sitting inadvertently, the follower waits for him. So if the follower gives salaam before the imam performs the extra prostration, his fard is invalidated, and it is disliked for the follower to give salaam after the imam's tashahhud before his salaam.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Nur al-Idah regarding the imam's forgetfulness in prayer. The scenario: the imam, by mistake, stands up for the next rak'ah before completing the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah). The follower must wait for the imam to remember and return. If the follower, impatient, gives salaam before the imam performs the sujud al-sahw (the two extra prostrations), then the follower's fard prayer becomes invalid (fasid) because he separated from the imam prematurely. However, if the follower waits until after the imam's tashahhud but gives salaam before the imam does, that action is makruh (disliked) but does not invalidate the prayer. The ruling emphasizes the necessity of following the imam until the end.

Key Terms
القعود الأخير (al-qu'ud al-akhir): The final sitting of the prayer, after the last sujud, where tashahhud and salam occur.
سجدة (sajdah): Here refers to the two prostrations of sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the follower gives salaam before the imam performs sujud al-sahw for forgetting the final sitting?
A) The follower's prayer is valid but makruh.
B) The follower's prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
C) The follower must repeat the rak'ah.
D) The imam's prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
A follower must wait for the imam to complete sujud al-sahw; premature salaam invalidates, while salaam after tashahhud but before imam's salaam is disliked.

Post-Fard Adhkar: Timing, Content, and Etiquette
Detailed rulings on post-fard remembrances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (mustahabb) practices after the obligatory prayer according to the Hanafi school and evaluate the preferred timing of adhkar.

Core Idea
Delay the adhkar until after the sunnah — that is the preferred Hanafi practice.

After completing the fard prayer, there are several sunnah and mustahabb acts that enhance one's worship. However, there is a difference among Hanafi scholars about when to recite the adhkar. This passage from Nur al-Idah with commentary clarifies that while reciting between fard and sunnah is permissible, the preferred and more established practice is to delay them until after the sunnah. It also details the specific remembrances, the imam's movements, and the etiquette of du'a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on standing immediately for sunnah
Understand that it is sunnah to stand directly for the sunnah prayer after the fard. Note the dispute about performing adhkar in between.
The text says 'القيام إلى السنة متصلا بالفرض مسنون'.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of adhkar
Recognize that Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani allows reciting between fard and sunnah, while al-Ikhtiyar considers it disliked. Identify the preferred view from al-Kamal: delay adhkar after sunnah.
The text concludes 'فالأولى تأخير الأوراد عن السنة'.
3
Extract the recommended practices for imam and congregation
Describe the imam's actions: after salaam, turn left (right side of qibla) for sunnah; after sunnah, face the congregation. Then the congregation recites Ayat al-Kursi, mu'awwidhat, tasbihat, tahlil, and du'a.
4
Apply the rules on conditions and etiquette
Note that the prescribed number (33) need not be consecutive or in one sitting. Recognize disliked acts: raising eyes to sky during du'a, restricting du'a to specific prayer/time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأذكار الواردة بعد الفرض

الإمام

القيام إلى السنة متصلا بالفرض مسنون، وعن شمس الأئمة الحلواني: لا بأس بقراءة الأوراد بين الفريضة والسنة، ويستحب للإمام بعد سلامه أن يتحول إلى يساره لتطوع بعد الفرض، وأن يستقبل بعده الناس ويستغفرون الله ويقرؤون آية الكرسي والمعوذات، ويسبحون الله ثلاثاً وثلاثين ويحمدونه كذلك، ويكبرونه كذلك. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣١١] لا بأس بقراءة إلخ: فالأولى تأخير الأوراد عن السنة فهذا ينفي الكراهة، ويخالفه ما قال في "الاختيار": كل صلاة بعدها سنة يكره القعود بعدها والدعاء، بل يشتغل بالسنة كي لا يفصل بين السنة والمكتوبة، ثم قال الكمال: ولم يثبت عنه الفصل بالأذكار التي يواظب عليها في المساجد في عصرنا من قراءة آية الكرسي والتسبيحات وأخواتها ثلاثا وثلاثين وغيرها، وقوله الله الفقراء المهاجرين [؟]: تسبحون، وتكبرون، وتحمدون كل صلاة إلخ" لا يقتضي وصلها بالفرض، بل كونها عقب السنة من غير اشتغال بما ليس من توابع الصلاة، فصح كونها دبرها. وإذا تكلم بكلام كثير أو أكل أو شرب بين الفرض والسنة لا تبطل، وهو الأصح، بل نقص ثوابها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣١٢] أن يتحول إلخ أي: يتحول إلى يمين القبلة، وهو الجانب المقابل إلى جهة يساره أي يسار المستقبل؛ لأن يمين المقابل جهة يسار المستقبل، فيتحول إليه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣١٣] أن يستقبل إلخ: أي ويستحب أن يستقبل بعد التطوع عقب الفرض، وإن لم يكن بعده نافلة يستقبل الناس إن لم يكن في مقابلة مصل. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣١٤] والمعوذات فيه تغليب والمراد الصمدية والمعوذتان. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ثلاثا وثلاثين] فإن قلت: هل الشرط في تحصيل السنة والفضل الموعود به أن يقول الذكر المنصوص عليه بالعدد متتابعا أم لا، وفي مجلس واحد أم لا؟ قلت: وكل ذلك ليس بشرط، لكن الأفضل أن يأتي به متتابعا في الوقت الذي عين فيه. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣١٦] ثم يقولون: لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له، له الملك وله الحمد، وهو على كل شيء قدير، ثم يدعون لأنفسهم وللمسلمين رافعي أيديهم، ثم يمسحون بها وجوههم بالأدعية المأثورة في آخره. ويكره أن يرفع بصره إلى السماء؛ لما فيه من ترك الأدب وتوهم الجهة، وقد نهى النبي . كما في شرح الحصن الحصين"، وأن يخص صلاة أو وقتا بدعاء؛ لأنه يقسي القلب. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣١٦] رافعي أصله: رافعين وسقوط النون للإضافة.
Section on the remembrances transmitted after the obligatory prayer. The imam: Standing up for the sunnah immediately after the fard is sunnah. And from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani: There is no harm in reciting the litanies between the fard and the sunnah. And it is recommended for the imam after his salaam to turn to his left for supererogatory prayer after the fard, and that he should then face the people and they ask forgiveness of Allah and recite Ayat al-Kursi and the Mu'awwidhat, and glorify Allah thirty-three times and praise Him likewise and exalt Him likewise. [Marqi al-Falah: 311] 'There is no harm in reciting etc.': So the preferable is to delay the litanies until after the sunnah; this negates dislike. And it contradicts what was said in al-Ikhtiyar: Every prayer after which there is a sunnah, it is disliked to sit after it and supplicate; rather one should occupy oneself with the sunnah so as not to separate between the sunnah and the obligatory. Then al-Kamal said: And it is not established from him (the Prophet) the separation with the remembrances that are constantly performed in our time in the mosques, such as reciting Ayat al-Kursi, the tasbihat and their sisters thirty-three times and others. And his statement 'the poor emigrants [؟]: you glorify, exalt, and praise after every prayer etc.' does not necessitate connecting them with the fard, but rather that they be after the sunnah without engaging in what is not from the appendages of prayer, so it is correct that they are its aftermath. And if one speaks much speech or eats or drinks between the fard and the sunnah, it does not invalidate, and that is the most correct, but it reduces its reward. [Marqi al-Falah: 312] 'That he turns etc.': Meaning he turns to the right side of the qibla, which is the side opposite to his left, i.e., the left of the one facing the qibla; because the right of the opposite is the left of the one facing the qibla, so he turns to it. [Marqi al-Falah: 313] 'That he faces etc.': Meaning it is recommended that he faces after the supererogatory after the fard, and if there is no supererogatory after it, he faces the people if there is no one in front of him praying. [Marqi al-Falah: 314] And 'the Mu'awwidhat' includes a generalization; what is meant is al-Samadiyyah and the two Mu'awwidhat. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: thirty-three] If you say: Is the condition for achieving the sunnah and the promised reward that one says the prescribed remembrance with the number consecutively or not, and in one sitting or not? I say: All that is not a condition, but it is best to do it consecutively at the time specified. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 316] Then they say: There is no god but Allah alone, no partner for Him, to Him belongs the kingdom and to Him belongs all praise, and He is over all things powerful. Then they supplicate for themselves and for the Muslims, raising their hands, then they wipe their faces with their hands with the transmitted supplications at the end. And it is disliked to raise his gaze to the sky because it contains abandonment of manners and imagining direction, and the Prophet prohibited it, as in Sharh al-Husn al-Hasin; and that he specifies a prayer or time with a supplication because it hardens the heart. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 316] 'Rafi'i' originally is 'Rafi'in' and the nun is dropped due to addition.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah with commentary discusses the recommended (mustahabb) practices after the obligatory prayer. It begins with the ruling: standing up immediately for the sunnah prayer (the two rak'ahs of sunnah of fajr, or the sunnah after zuhr, etc.) is sunnah. There is a difference of opinion: Imam al-Halwani said there is no harm in reciting adhkar (litanies) between the fard and sunnah, while the author of al-Ikhtiyar held it disliked to sit and make du'a, preferring to go straight to the sunnah. Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam notes that the practice of reciting Ayat al-Kursi, tasbih, tahmid, takbir 33 times each after fard is not established as being done between fard and sunnah; rather they are done after the sunnah. The preferred view is to delay the adhkar until after the sunnah. If one speaks, eats, or drinks between fard and sunnah, the sunnah is not invalidated but its reward is reduced. The text then explains the mustahabb actions for the imam: after salaam, he turns to his left (i.e., to the right side of the qibla) to perform the sunnah. After the sunnah, he faces the congregation. The congregation then recites Ayat al-Kursi, al-Mu'awwidhat (including al-Ikhlas and the two Mu'awwidhat), and the tasbihat. The prescribed number (33 each) need not be done consecutively or in one sitting; it is best but not required. Finally, they say the tahlil (la ilaha illa Allah) and make du'a raising hands, then wipe their faces. It is disliked to raise eyes to the sky during du'a or to restrict a supplication to a specific prayer or time without basis.

Key Terms
الأوراد (al-awrad): Litanies or set remembrances including Ayat al-Kursi, mu'awwidhat, tasbihat, etc.
المعوذات (al-mu'awwidhat): Surahs al-Falaq and an-Nas, and by some, also al-Ikhlas (the 'generalizing' usage).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, when should the tasbihat (subhanallah 33 times etc.) be recited?
A) Immediately after the fard prayer, before the sunnah.
B) After the sunnah prayer.
C) At any time after fard, even if not consecutively.
D) Only after the sunnah and in one sitting.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi practice is to recite the post-fard adhkar after the sunnah prayer, not between fard and sunnah.

Verbal Invalidators in Prayer: Speech, Supplication, Greeting, and Reply
Enumeration and commentary on four verbal invalidators with intra- and inter-madhhab nuances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four verbal invalidators of prayer according to the Hanafi school and apply the ruling that any speech, even forgetful or mistaken, invalidates prayer, with a nuanced exception for greeting without a present addressee.

Core Idea
Any word in prayer invalidates; greeting only invalidates absolutely if someone is present.

What spoken acts break your prayer? The Hanafi school holds that any deliberate, forgetful, or mistaken utterance invalidates, but with key nuances on supplication and greeting. This lesson unpacks four specific invalidators and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four invalidators
From the text, list the four verbal acts that invalidate prayer: any word (al-kalimah), supplication resembling human speech (al-du'a), greeting with intention (al-salam), and replying to greeting (radd al-salam).
The author also notes that these are among sixty-eight total invalidators, an approximate number.
2
Understand the scope of 'word'
Note that any utterance, whether meaningful (like 'Zaid is standing') or meaningless (like 'Ya'), spoken intentionally, forgetfully (sahw), or mistakenly (khata) invalidates prayer. This includes cases where the person was unaware they were in prayer.
The text distinguishes sahw (forgetfulness that can be recalled), nisyan (requires re-learning), and khata (error not noticed even with prompting). All invalidate.
3
Analyze the supplication dispute
The rule for supplication (dua) is treated separately from 'word' because of a madhhab difference. Hanafis rule that dua resembling requests that could be made to humans (e.g., 'O Allah, feed me') invalidates prayer. Imam al-Shafi'i does not. Understand the practical consequence: a Hanafi cannot make such dua in prayer.
Dua for matters impossible from humans (e.g., forgiveness, paradise) is permissible and does not invalidate.
4
Reconcile the greeting inconsistency
The text states greeting invalidates absolutely, but the Hidayah says forgetful greeting is dhikr. The author reconciles: if the addressee is present, greeting invalidates even forgetfully; if no addressee, only intentional greeting invalidates. Learn the condition: presence of addressee determines the ruling.
This is an example of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf resolved by distinguishing the scenario.
5
Apply the reply ruling
Replying to a greeting verbally or by handshake invalidates, whether intentional, forgetful, or mistaken. However, replying with the hand alone (e.g., waving) does not invalidate. This is because reply is pure speech, not dhikr.
The text cites al-Shumni to confirm this position.

The Book of Prayer: What invalidates prayer. Chapter of what invalidates prayer. There are sixty-eight things: the word (even if forgetfully or mistakenly), supplication resembling our speech, greeting with intention of salutation even if forgetfully, and replying to the greeting with his tongue or by handshake. If he replies with his hand, it does not invalidate. Its number is completed. What invalidates: fasad and butlan are the same in worship, but different in transactions: what is lawful in its essence not in its description, like a sale with a condition not required by the contract, is fasid; what is not lawful in its essence nor description, like selling carrion and blood, is batil. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah: 320] Sixty-eight is an approximate statement, not definitive, so it is not necessary that the word: it includes whether it is meaningful like 'Zaid is standing' or not, like 'Ya', even if uttered forgetfully thinking he is not in prayer, or uttered mistakenly as if he meant to say 'O people' but said 'O Yazid', whether he was ignorant of its being invalidating or knowledgeable in the chosen view. Forgetfully: Know that the difference between sahw and nisyan is that if the image present in the mind can be observed at any time, it is called dhuhul and sahw; if it cannot be observed except after new acquisition, it is called nisyan. And between sahw and khata: sahw is what its owner becomes aware of, and khata is what he does not become aware of by being alerted or becomes aware after exertion. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi adapted: 321] 'and supplication etc.': He singled it out even though it is included in 'the word' because al-Shafi'i does not invalidate prayer by supplication. Supplication resembling our speech is what can be requested from humans, like 'O Allah, feed me' or 'fulfill my debt and provide for me so-and-so' according to the sahih, and what is impossible to request from humans is not our speech, like well-being, forgiveness, and provision, whether for himself or others, even for his brother according to the sahih. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq adapted: 7/1] 'and greeting with intention etc.': He made it absolute, encompassing intentional and forgetful, and if he says 'Peace' only without saying 'upon you'. In al-Hidayah there is something contradicting it, for it says: 'contrary to greeting forgetfully' because it is from dhikr, so it is considered dhikr in the state of forgetfulness and speech in the state of intent. I have not seen anyone reconciling the two statements, and it has become apparent to me that what is meant by greeting that invalidates absolutely is when the addressee is present, then there is no difference between intentional and forgetful, i.e., forgetfulness of being in prayer; and what is meant by greeting that invalidates only in the state of intent is when there is no addressee present, as they said: he greeted at the end of two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer forgetfully, then his prayer does not invalidate. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq: 14/2] 'and replying to the greeting': al-Shumni said because replying to the greeting invalidates, whether intentional or forgetful, because replying to the greeting is not from dhikr, but rather speech and address, and speech invalidates absolutely. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq: 14/2] with his tongue, intentionally, forgetfully, or mistakenly. (Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi)
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on what invalidates prayer. It lists sixty-eight invalidators, but the author clarifies this is an approximate number. The first invalidator is any word (الكلمة), whether meaningful or not, even if uttered forgetfully (سهواً) or mistakenly (خطأً). A note defines sahw (forgetfulness one can recall with attention) versus nisyan (forgetfulness requiring re-learning) and khata (error one does not notice without prompting). The second invalidator is supplication (الدعاء) that resembles human speech, i.e., requests that could be asked of humans, such as 'O Allah, feed me'. The author singles this out because Imam al-Shafi'i does not consider such dua invalidating, but the Hanafi position is that it does. The third invalidator is greeting (السلام) with the intention of salutation, whether intentional or forgetful. However, the Hidayah states that if done forgetfully it is considered dhikr and does not invalidate. The author reconciles by distinguishing whether there is a present addressee: if there is, it invalidates even forgetfully; if not, it invalidates only intentionally. The fourth invalidator is replying to the greeting (رد السلام) with the tongue or handshake; replying only with the hand does not invalidate. Replying verbally invalidates even if forgetful, as it is pure speech.

Key Terms
الكلمة (al-kalimah): Any utterance, whether meaningful or not, including particles like 'Ya', that invalidates prayer if spoken intentionally, forgetfully, or mistakenly.
الدعاء (al-du'a): Supplication in prayer that resembles human speech, i.e., requesting things that can be asked of humans, which invalidates prayer according to Hanafis.
السلام (al-salam): The greeting 'as-salamu alaykum' said with the intention of salutation, which invalidates prayer if addressed to a present person even forgetfully, but only if intentional if no one is present.
رد السلام (radd al-salam): Verbally responding to a greeting, which invalidates prayer whether intentional, forgetful, or mistaken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does saying 'O Allah, feed me' (اللهم أطعمني) during prayer invalidate the prayer?
A) Yes, because it is a request that can be asked of humans, thus resembling speech.
B) No, because it is a dua and du'a is permissible in prayer.
C) Yes, but only if said intentionally.
D) No, because it is a request from Allah, not from humans.

Key Takeaway
Any spoken word, intentional or accidental, invalidates prayer; greeting has a nuance based on the presence of an addressee, and replying always invalidates.

Defining Excessive Action (Amal Kathir) in the Hanafi School
Defining excessive action and its threshold in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of excessive action (amal kathir) in prayer and apply the perceptual test to distinguish between invalidating and permissible actions.

Core Idea
Excessive action in prayer is defined by what an observer would be certain is not prayer, not by a fixed number of movements.

The validity of prayer depends on maintaining its state of devotion and stillness. However, not every movement outside the prescribed actions breaks the prayer. This passage from the Hanafi tradition clarifies the critical distinction between 'excessive' and 'little' action, using a simple perceptual test rather than an arbitrary count. Understanding this criterion helps avoid unnecessary invalidation and ensures the prayer remains sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal concept being defined
The passage defines 'amal kathir' (excessive action) as an invalidator of prayer. Determine the concept's role: it is a mufsid (nullifier).
The hukm (ruling) is that if amal kathir occurs, the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
2
Extract the operative criterion
The relied-upon criterion is external perception: if an observer would have no doubt that the person is not praying, the action is excessive. If there is doubt, it is considered little (qalil) and does not invalidate.
The text says: 'على الأصح' (according to the most correct view).
3
Note the alternative definition
An alternative view (قيل) defines excessive action as three consecutive movements (الحركات الثلاث المتواليات). Less than that is little.
This is a minority opinion within the Hanafi school, not the relied-upon view.
4
Determine the relied-upon view (mufta bihi)
The perceptual test is preferred. The authority weight is from zahir al-riwayah, and scholars like al-Marghinani adopt it.
The mufta bihi position is the perceptual test, not the three-movement rule.
5
Apply the distinction to a scenario
Given an action during prayer, assess whether an observer would be certain the person is not praying. If yes, the action is kathir and invalidates. If ambiguous, it is qalil and does not invalidate.
This test is subjective but relies on a hypothetical reasonable observer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعمل الكثير والفاصل بين القليل والكثير أن الكثير هو الذي لا يشك الناظر لفاعله أنه ليس في الصلاة، وإن اشتبه فهو قليل على الأصح، وقيل في تفسيره غير هذا كالحركات الثلاث المتواليات كثير، ودونها قليل. مراقي الفلاح: ۳۲۲
And excessive action: the distinction between little and much is that much is what the observer does not doubt that its doer is not in prayer, and if it is ambiguous then it is little according to the most correct view. And it was said in its explanation other than this: such as three consecutive movements is much, and less than that is little. (Maraqi al-Falah: 322)
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage defines the invalidator of 'excessive action' (amal kathir) in prayer. The relied-upon criterion is external perception: if any onlooker would definitely conclude that the person is not praying, the action is excessive. If it is doubtful, the action is considered little (qalil) and does not invalidate. An alternative view, mentioned but not preferred, sets a fixed number: three consecutive movements constitute excess, fewer are little. The Hanafi school generally adopts the perceptual test.

Key Terms
العمل الكثير (al-‘amal al-kathīr): Action in prayer that is so much that any observer would be certain the person is not praying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what is the criterion for 'excessive action' that invalidates prayer?
A) Three or more consecutive movements
B) Any voluntary movement
C) The observer does not doubt that the doer is not in prayer
D) Moving two limbs three times

Key Takeaway
Excessive action in prayer is determined by external perception, not by counting movements; the Hanafi school adopts the criterion that an observer would have no doubt that the person is not praying.

Turning the Chest Away from the Qibla: The General Rule and Its Exceptions
Ruling on turning the chest away from qibla and its exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general ruling on turning the chest away from the qibla and identify the two exceptional situations where it does not invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Turning the chest from the qibla invalidates prayer unless necessitated by wudu after hadath or by the fear prayer.

The rule that turning the chest invalidates prayer is not absolute. Necessity creates exceptions. This passage from Nur al-Idah highlights two such cases: when one must leave for wudu after breaking wudu, and when one must face the enemy in the fear prayer. These exceptions show the balance between ritual precision and practical need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage begins with a general statement that turning the chest is a mufsid. What is the default ruling?
2
Recognize the restriction
The phrase 'أطلقه وهو مقيد' indicates the ruling is not absolute; it is restricted by conditions.
3
List the two exceptions
Find the two situations mentioned: (1) prior hadath leading to wudu, (2) turning in fear prayer to guard against the enemy.
4
Understand the common principle
Both exceptions involve necessity (darurah or hajah). The prayer is not invalidated because the turning is for a required act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتحويل الصدر إلخ أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يسبقه حدث أو بغير صلاة الخوف، أما إذا سبقه حدث فخرج للوضوء وحوّل صدره عن القبلة أو حوّل صدره لاصطفاف حراسته بإزاء العدو لا تفسد صلاته.
And turning the chest etc. - he mentioned it absolutely, but it is restricted: if a hadath (event that breaks wudu) preceded him, he goes out for wudu and turns his chest away from the qibla, or turns his chest to line up for guarding against the enemy, his prayer does not become invalid.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This explains the invalidator of turning the chest (sadr) away from the qibla. The rule is conditional: normally it invalidates, but two exceptions are mentioned: (1) if the person had an event that invalidates wudu (hadath), he must leave for wudu and accidentally or necessarily turns his chest - prayer is not invalidated because he is fulfilling an obligation. (2) In the prayer of fear (salat al-khawf), if a warrior turns his chest to face the enemy for protection, his prayer remains valid. This shows the Hanafi concern for contextual necessity.

Key Terms
تحويل الصدر (tahwīl al-ṣadr): Turning the chest away from the qibla direction during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which situation does turning the chest away from the qibla not invalidate the prayer?
A) When the person is forgetful
B) When the person has a hadath and goes for wudu
C) When the person is praying alone
D) When the person moves to a cleaner spot

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes that necessity can override the default invalidation of turning the chest, specifically in cases of prior hadath and fear prayer.

Invalidators of Prayer: Eating, Drinking, and Vocal Expressions
Rulings on eating, drinking, clearing throat, and vocal expressions of displeasure in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which consumptive and vocal actions invalidate the prayer and identify the exceptions that excuse them.

Core Idea
Eating, drinking, and vocal complaints invalidate prayer unless excused or purely for dhikr.

In this lesson, we examine specific actions that nullify prayer. The Hanafi school is precise: not all sounds or movements break the prayer; intention and necessity matter. You will learn to distinguish between invalidating and permissible actions based on cause and purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action
What is the person doing? Is it eating, drinking, a vocal sound, or a response?
Look for specific terms: tanahnuh, tafif, anin, ta'awwuh, crying, tashmit.
2
Determine if it is a clear invalidator
Does it fall under the categories listed? For example, eating from outside the mouth always invalidates; eating between teeth only if size of chickpea.
Some actions have quantitative thresholds or contextual conditions.
3
Check for valid excuse or intention
If clearing throat, was it for recitation? If crying, was it from piety? If a response, was it intended as dhikr or address?
Excuses remove invalidation; intention determines the nature of the utterance.
4
Apply the ruling
If no excuse and it is a listed action, the prayer becomes invalid. If excused, it is valid.
Be mindful of subtle distinctions, like crying from pain vs. from fear of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأكل شيء من خارج فمه ولوقـل وصولي كسم [؟]، وأكل ما بين أسنانه وهو قدر الحمصة وشربه، والتنحنح بلا عذر، والتأفيف، والأنين، والتأوه، وارتفاع بكائه من وجع أو مصيبة، لا من ذكر جنة أو نار، وتشميت عاطس إلخ . والتنحنح : هو أن يقول 'أح' بالفتح أو الضم. البحر الرائق بزيادة: ٩/٢] بلا عذر وإن كان لعذر كمنعه البلغم من القراءة لا يفسد [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٢٤] ومنه التنحنح لإصلاح الصوت وتحسينه، أو ليهتدي خطأه، أو للإعلام بأنه في الصلاة على الصحيح كما في 'الفتح'. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٤] والتأفيف: التأفيف أن يقول: 'أف' أو 'تف' لنفخ التراب أو التضجر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٤] وهو 'أه' بسكون الهاء مقصوراً بوزن 'دع' يقال: إن الرجل يئن بالكسر أنينا وأنانا بالضم صوت فهو آن كفاعل وهي آنة حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٣٢٤] والتأوه وهو أن يقول: 'أوه'، وفيها لغات كثيرة تمدّ، لا تمدُّ مع تشديد الواو المفتوحة وسكون الهاء وكسرها. مراقي الفلاح: ٣٢٤ وارتفاع هو أن تحصل به حروف مسموعة. (مراقي الفلاح) من وجع إلخ وقوله : 'لا' من ذكر جنة أو نار' عائد إلى الكل أيضا فالحاصل أنها إن كانت من ذكر الجنة أو النار فهو دال على زيادة الخشوع، ولو صرح بهما فقال: 'اللهم إني أسألك الجنة وأعوذ بك من النار'، لم تفسد صلاته، وإن كان من وجع أو مصيبة فهو دال على إظهارهما، فكأنه قال: إني مصاب والدلالة تعمل عمل الصريح إذا لم يكن هناك يخالفها. البحر الرائق بحذف: ٨/٢] وتشميت عاطس إلخ هو بالشين المعجمة أفصح من السين المهملة: الدعاء بالخير، وهو من إضافة المصدر إلى مفعوله، أي خطاب المصلي للعاطس قيدنا بالخطاب من المصلي؛ لأنه لو قاله العاطس لنفسه لا تفسد؛ لأنه بمنزلة قوله: يرحمني و به لا تفسد، ولو قال: 'الحمد لله فمن العاطس نفسه لا تفسد، وكذا من غيره إن أراد الثواب اتفاقا، كما تفسد اتفاقا إذا أراد به تعليم العاطس أن يقول ذلك، ولو أراد به الجواب للعاطس لا تفسد [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٥، مراقي الفلاح]
And eating something from outside his mouth... and eating what is between his teeth of the size of a chickpea and drinking it, and clearing the throat without excuse, and saying 'uff', and moaning (anin), and saying 'awh', and elevation of his crying from pain or calamity, not from mention of paradise or hell, and responding to a sneezer... And clearing the throat: it is saying 'ah' with fatha or damma. Without excuse, but if for an excuse like preventing phlegm from reading, it does not invalidate... And it includes clearing throat for correcting voice, or to guide his mistake, or to indicate he is in prayer according to the correct view. And 'tafif': to say 'uff' or 'tuff' for blowing dust or expressing annoyance. And 'anin': it is 'ah' with sukun on ha, shortened... And 'ta'awwuh': to say 'awh', with many variant pronunciations. And elevation of crying: it produces audible letters. From pain etc: if from mention of paradise or hell it indicates increased khushu', and even if expressed explicitly it does not invalidate. If from pain or calamity it indicates showing them, as if he says 'I am afflicted', and indication acts like explicit statement. And responding to a sneezer: with shin is more eloquent, meaning supplication for good. It is from adding the masdar to its object, i.e., the address of the worshiper to the sneezer. We restrict it to address from the worshiper because if the sneezer says it for himself it does not invalidate, as it is like saying 'may He have mercy on me'. And if he says 'alhamdulillah' from the sneezer himself it does not invalidate, similarly from someone else if he intends reward by agreement, and it invalidates by agreement if he intends to teach the sneezer to say that, but if he intends to respond to the sneezer it does not invalidate.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage lists several vocal and consumptive actions that invalidate prayer. Eating anything from outside the mouth invalidates even if little, but eating what is between the teeth of a chickpea-size or drinking it also invalidates. Clearing the throat (tanahnuh) without a valid excuse (like phlegm hindering recitation) invalidates; with excuse it does not. Saying 'uff' (tafif) out of displeasure, moaning (anin), and saying 'awh' (ta'awwuh) all invalidate. Crying aloud from pain or worldly calamity invalidates because it indicates complaining, but crying out of fear of Allah or longing for paradise shows khushu' and does not invalidate. Responding to a sneezer (tashmit) by saying 'yarhamukallah' invalidates because it is addressing another person. However, if the sneezer himself says 'alhamdulillah' it does not invalidate as it is dhikr. The nuances show that intention matters: if one intends to teach or respond, it may invalidate; if one intends mere dhikr or reward, it does not. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between actions that are purely worship and those that resemble worldly conversation.

Key Terms
التنحنح (al-tanahnuh): Clearing the throat by saying 'ah' audibly.
التأفيف (al-ta'fīf): Saying 'uff' to express annoyance or to blow dust.
الأنين (al-anīn): Moaning: saying 'ah' with sukun on ha, a low sound of pain.
التأوه (al-ta'awwuh): Saying 'awh' as a sigh of distress.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following invalidates the prayer according to this passage?
A) Clearing throat to prevent phlegm from blocking recitation
B) Saying 'uff' when annoyed by a fly
C) Crying out of longing for Paradise
D) Saying 'alhamdulillah' after sneeze as dhikr

Key Takeaway
Intentions and excuses distinguish valid dhikr from invalidating speech and consumption in prayer.

Events That End a Concession and Invalidate Prayer
Lists five cases where a concession ends and the prayer becomes invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify five specific events that remove a legal concession during prayer and state that each invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
When the excuse ends, prayer built on it collapses.

Prayer may be performed with a concession due to a valid excuse, such as tayammum for lack of water or wiping over khuffs. If the reason for the concession disappears during the prayer—for example, seeing water or the wipe period ending—the basis of the prayer is lost. This lesson covers five such events and the Hanafi ruling on each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concession
Recognize which legal concession is being used: tayammum, masḥ ʿalā al-khuffayn, permission for the unlettered, covering for the naked, or gesture prayer for the incapacitated.
2
Pinpoint the ending event
For each concession, note the specific event that removes it: seeing water, completion of the wipe period, learning a verse, finding a cover, or regaining ability to bow.
3
Apply the invalidation ruling
Once the concession ends, the prayer becomes invalid (fāsid). Exception: ṭayammum – if the worshiper is a follower whose imam has not seen water, his prayer remains valid.
4
Note the practical condition
For the naked person finding a cover, the cover must be obligatory to wear (owned or permitted, sufficiently pure). Similarly, the wipe period differs for resident and traveller.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورؤية متيمم ماءا، وتمام مدة ماسح الحُقِّ ونزعه، وتعلم الأمي آية ووجدان العاري ساترا، وقدرة المؤمي على الركوع والسجود، وتذكر فائتة لذي ترتيب واستخلاف من لا يصلح إماماً، ... ورؤية متيمم ماءاً أراد به ماء قدر على استعماله مراقي الفلاح فشمل ما إذا كان مقتديا أو إماما، أما إذا كان إماما فظاهر، وأما إذا كان مقتديا فهو مقيد بما إذا لم ير الماء إمامه. وتمام: أي يفسد صلاة المصلي إذا تمت مدة مسح خفه وهو في الصلاة؛ لزوال طهارة الرجلين. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٧] مدة ماسح إلخ وهي للمقيم يوم وليلة، وللمسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٧] ساتراً: أطلقه وهو مقيد بساتر يلزمه الصلاة فيه بأن كان مالكاً له أو أبيح له، وهو طاهر أو نجس وعنده ما يطهره به أو لا، إلا أن ربعه طاهر، فخرج نجس الكل وما لم يبحه مالكه. [ مراقي الفلاح ۳۲۷ ، حاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف] وتذكر فائتة إلخ أي إذا تذكر مصل ذو ترتيب أن عليه فائتة قبل هذه فسدت صلاته، وهذا الفساد فساد موقوف، فإن صلى خمسا متذكرا الفائتة وقضاها قبل خروج وقت الخامسة بطل وصف ما صلاه قبلها وصار نفلا، وإن لم يقضها حتى خرج وقت الخامسة ،صحت وارتفع فسادها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٢٨] واستخلاف إلخ أي صلى قارئ بهم ثم سبقه حدث وسط الصلاة فاستخلف ذلك القارئ أميا من المقتدين فسدت صلاته وصلواتهم.
And a mutayammim seeing water, and the completion of the period of a mas'h on khuffs and its removal, and an unlettered person learning a verse, and a naked person finding a cover, and the ability of one who prays by gestures (?) to bow and prostrate, and remembering an obligatory prayer missed by one who observes order, and appointing as successor one unfit to be imam. And seeing water: a mutayammim seeing water he is able to use. It includes whether he is a follower or imam, but if he is a follower, it is restricted to when his imam does not see water. And completion: the prayer of the worshiper is invalidated if the period of wiping on his khuffs completes while he is in prayer, due to the loss of purity of feet. The period for a resident is one day and night, for a traveler three days and nights. And finding a cover: unrestricted but restricted to a cover that it is obligatory to pray in, i.e., if he owns it or it is permissible for him, pure or impure but he has something to purify it, unless a quarter is pure, so excluded is entirely impure or unowned. And remembering an obligatory prayer: if a worshiper who observes order remembers that he has a missed obligatory prayer before this one, his prayer is invalidated. This invalidation is suspended: if he prays five (prayers) remembering the missed prayer and makes it up before the end of the time of the fifth, the description of what he prayed before becomes void and becomes nafl; if he does not make it up until the time of the fifth expires, it becomes valid and the invalidation is lifted. And appointing as successor: a qari (one who recites well) leads them, then is overtaken by hadath in the middle of prayer, and he appoints as successor an unlettered person from the followers, his prayer and their prayers are invalidated.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage covers situations where the reason for a legal concession ceases to exist during prayer, thus invalidating it. 1) A mutayammim sees water: his tayammum becomes null and prayer invalidates, unless he is a follower and his imam does not see water (he continues). 2) If the period for wiping over khuffs ends while in prayer, the prayer invalidates because foot purity is lost. 3) An unlettered person (unable to recite) learns a verse during prayer: he is no longer entitled to the concession of limited recitation, so prayer invalidates. 4) A naked person finds a cover: he is now obligated to cover, so prayer invalidates. 5) Someone praying with gestures due to inability becomes able to bow and prostrate: he must restart with proper actions. 6) If one remembers a missed prayer while praying a current prayer, the current prayer becomes invalid (but the invalidation is suspended depending on whether he makes up the missed prayer before the time of the current prayer ends—if he does, the current prayer becomes nafl; if not, it is valid). 7) If the imam (a qari) appoints an unlettered person as successor due to hadath, the prayer invalidates because the successor cannot lead properly. These cases illustrate that prayer is built on valid excuses; once the excuse ends, the prayer cannot continue.

Key Terms
ذو ترتيب (dhū tartīb): One who is obligated to perform prayers in order because the amount of missed prayers is less than six.
فساد موقوف (fasād mawqūf): Suspended invalidation: the ruling depends on a future action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A naked person finds a cover that is one-quarter pure and the rest is impure, but he owns no other cover. Is he obligated to wear it during prayer?
A) Yes, because at least a quarter is pure, so the cover is obligatory.
B) No, because the majority is impure.
C) Yes, but only if he can purify the impure part.
D) No, because any impurity in the cover makes it impermissible.

Key Takeaway
When a concession necessary for a valid prayer disappears, the prayer becomes invalid—except for the follower seeing water while his imam does not.

Suspended Invalidation and Succession by an Unqualified Imam
Explains suspended invalidation for remembering missed prayer and invalidation from unqualified successor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of suspended invalidation (fasād mawqūf) and state the ruling when an imam appoints an unlettered successor.

Core Idea
Remembering a missed prayer during a current prayer creates suspended invalidation—it becomes nafl if made up in time.

Among the events that invalidate prayer are two that involve obligations beyond the immediate prayer. The first is when a person who must pray in order remembers a missed prayer while praying; this creates a suspended invalidation. The second is when an imam who is a competent reciter appoints an unlettered person to lead after his hadath. This lesson unpacks these two rulings.

Guided Path
1
Define dhū tartīb
A person who has missed fewer than six prayers must perform them in order. During a current prayer, if such a person remembers a missed prayer, the current prayer becomes subject to invalidation.
If missed prayers are six or more, order is not required, so this ruling does not apply.
2
Understand suspended invalidation
The current prayer is not immediately invalid. Its status depends on action: if the missed prayer is made up before the time of the current prayer ends, the current prayer becomes nafl. If not, it is valid as the obligatory prayer.
The 'time of the current prayer ends' refers to the end of its time, not the prayer itself. The text says 'before the time of the fifth prayer ends' – meaning before the time of the next prayer in sequence? Actually, the example in the commentary mentions 'five prayers'? The text says: 'if he prays five prayers remembering the missed prayer and makes it up before the time of the fifth ends...' This is a specific calculation: if he prays five current prayers while remembering the missed one, and makes up the missed prayer before the time of the fifth of those current prayers ends, then the earlier ones become nafl. This is detailed in the source.
3
Apply the imam succession case
If an imam who is a competent reciter (qāriʾ) is invalidated by hadath and appoints an unlettered person (ummī) as his successor, the prayer of both the imam and the followers is invalidated because the successor is not qualified.
The unlettered person cannot lead because recitation of Qur'an is a condition, and an ummī cannot fulfill it for others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٧] مدة ماسح إلخ وهي للمقيم يوم وليلة، وللمسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٧] ساتراً: أطلقه وهو مقيد بساتر يلزمه الصلاة فيه بأن كان مالكاً له أو أبيح له، وهو طاهر أو نجس وعنده ما يطهره به أو لا، إلا أن ربعه طاهر، فخرج نجس الكل وما لم يبحه مالكه. An imam who recites well (qāriʾ) leads the prayer, but during the prayer he becomes impure and appoints a man who cannot recite Qur'an (ummī) as successor. What is the ruling on the prayer of the followers?
A) The prayer becomes invalid for both imam and followers.

Invalidators of Prayer: Speech, Conditions, and Alignment
List of actions and events that invalidate prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the actions and events that invalidate the prayer (salah) according to the Hanafi school and apply the rule that any intentional human reply invalidates.

Core Idea
Any intentional speech intended as a reply to another person invalidates the prayer, even if it is Quran or dhikr.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lists the invalidators of prayer. These are actions, speech, and changes of state that nullify the salah if they occur. Understanding these is crucial to preserve the validity of one's prayer. The commentary explains each item in detail, clarifying the principles behind the rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify speech invalidators
The first group includes any speech that is a reply to another person: 'Yarhamukallah', answering a question about other gods, istirja', saying 'Alhamdulillah' upon good news, expressing wonder, or any Quranic phrase used as a reply.
Even if the phrase is Quranic, if it is intended as a reply, it invalidates.
2
Understand invalidators due to loss of excuse
When an excuse for a concession (rukhsah) is removed during prayer, the prayer becomes invalid. Examples: a mutayammim seeing water, the duration of masah expiring, an ummi learning a verse, a naked person finding clothing, a person with an excuse gaining ability to bow, and remembering a missed prayer (if sequence is required).
The removal of the excuse means the original requirement becomes due.
3
Recognize invalidators from time or state changes
Certain external events invalidate if they occur during prayer: sunrise during Fajr, zenith during Eid prayer, entry of Asr during Jumu'ah, cast falling off after healing, hadath, fainting, insanity, janaba, and exposure of awrah.
For hadath and exposure due to compulsion, the prayer may be built upon under certain conditions.
4
Analyze the alignment (muhadhat) rule
Alignment of a desirable woman with a man in prayer invalidates the prayer if specific conditions are met: both are praying the same act, share the same tahrimah, in one place without barrier, and the man intends her imamate.
The woman must be desirable (even if old) and alignment is by shin and ankle.
5
Apply the principle consistently
The key principle is that any intentional speech or action that is a human reply, or any change that removes a condition of validity, nullifies the prayer. Memorize the list but understand the underlying rule.
Note the exceptions: compulsion may allow building, and fainting/insanity invalidate entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يفسد الصلاة
بـ"يرحمك الله"، وجواب مستفهم عن ند بـ"لا إله إلا الله"، وخبر سوء بالاسترجاع وسارّ بـ "الحمد لله"، وعجب بـ "لا إله إلا الله" أو سبحان الله، وكل شيء قصد به الجواب كيا يحيى خذ الكتاب"، ورؤية متيمم ماءا، وتمام مدة ماسح الحُقِّ ونزعه، وتعلم الأمي آية ووجدان العاري ساترا، وقدرة المؤمي على الركوع والسجود، وتذكر فائتة لذي ترتيب واستخلاف من لا يصلح إماماً، ... كامي ومعذور
وجواب مستفهم إلخ بأن قيل : أمع الله إله آخر؟ فقال: لا إله إلا الله. [حاشية الشلبي ٣٩٤/١] بالاسترجاع: استرجع زيد قال : إنا لله وإنا إليه راجعون، أي أخبر أحد مصلياً بخبر يحزنه مثل موت ابنه، فقال وهو في الصلاة: "إنا لله وإنا إليه راجعون فسدت صلاته وسار أي أخبر أحد مصليا بخبر يسره مثل ولادة ابنه، فقال: "الحمد لله" فسدت صلاته وعجب إلخ أي يفسد الصلاة جوابه الخبر يعجبه بقوله: "لا إله إلا الله"، أو "سبحان الله " . وكل شيء إلخ: عمّمه فشمل ما إذا كان من القرآن أو من غيره، فلو ذكر الشهادتين عند ذكر المؤذن لهما أو سمع ذكر الله ، فقال : جل جلاله، أو ذكر النبي فصلى عليه، أو قال عند ختم الإمام القراءة: صدق الله العظيم أو صدق رسوله أو سمع الشيطان فلعنه أو ناداه رجل بأن يجهر بالتكبير ففعل فسدت [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٦] كـ"يا يحيى": مثلاً طلب رجل اسمه يحيى من رجل وهو يصلي كتابا، فقال المصلي: يا يحيى! خذ الكتاب. ماءاً أراد به ماء قدر على استعماله مراقي الفلاح فشمل ما إذا كان مقتديا أو إماما، أما إذا ورؤية متيمم كان إماما فظاهر، وأما إذا كان مقتديا فهو مقيد بما إذا لم ير الماء إمامه. وتمام: أي يفسد صلاة المصلي إذا تمت مدة مسح خفه وهو في الصلاة؛ لزوال طهارة الرجلين. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٧] مدة ماسح إلخ وهي للمقيم يوم وليلة، وللمسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٧] ساتراً: أطلقه وهو مقيد بساتر يلزمه الصلاة فيه بأن كان مالكاً له أو أبيح له، وهو طاهر أو نجس وعنده ما يطهره به أو لا، إلا أن ربعه طاهر، فخرج نجس الكل وما لم يبحه مالكه. [ مراقي الفلاح ۳۲۷ ، حاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف] وتذكر فائتة إلخ أي إذا تذكر مصل ذو ترتيب أن عليه فائتة قبل هذه فسدت صلاته، وهذا الفساد فساد موقوف، فإن صلى خمسا متذكرا الفائتة وقضاها قبل خروج وقت الخامسة بطل وصف ما صلاه قبلها وصار نفلا، وإن لم يقضها حتى خرج وقت الخامسة ،صحت وارتفع فسادها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٢٨] واستخلاف إلخ أي صلى قارئ بهم ثم سبقه حدث وسط الصلاة فاستخلف ذلك القارئ أميا من المقتدين فسدت صلاته وصلواتهم.
وطلوع الشمس في الفجر، وزوالها في العيدين، ودخول وقت العصر في الجمعة، وسقوط الجبيرة عن برء وزوال عذر المعذور، والحدث عمداً أو بصنع غيره، والإغماء، والجنون، والجنابة بنظر أو احتلام ومحاذاة المشتهاة في صلاة مطلقة مشتركة تحريمة في مكان متحد بلا حائل ونوى إمامتها وظهور عورة من سبقه الحدث ولو اضطر إليه، ككشف المرأة ذراعها، وصلية
وطلوع الشمس إلخ : مثلاً شرع رجل في صلاة الفجر وطلعت الشمس في أثنائها فسدت صلاته. وزوالها إلخ: مثلاً شرع قوم في صلاة الفطر أو العيد فزالت الشمس وهم في صلاتهم فسدت صلاتهم. وسقوط الجبيرة إلخ أي كان الرجل ماسحا على جبيرة، فشرع في الصلاة فسقطت بعد برء فسدت صلاته، ولو سقطت لا عن برء لا تفسد عمدا أفاد أن الصلاة لا تفسد بسبق الحدث؛ لأن المسبوق به يبني بالشروط المعلومة في البناء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٩]
أو احتلام إن قيل لا حاجة إلى ذكر إضافة البطلان إلى الاحتلام لسبق بطلانها بالنوم؟ فالجواب أن هذا محمول على ما إذا نام في صلاته على وجه لا يبطلها فاحتلم [حاشية الطحطاوي بتغيير : ٣٢٩] ومحاذاة: أي محاذاة الرجل المشتهاة بساقها وكعبها في الأصح ولو محرماً له أو زوجة اشتهت ولو ماضياً كعجوز شوهاء، والتفسير الصحيح للمحاذاة هو أن تقوم المرأة بجنب الرجل أو قدامه من غير حائل، إنما قيد بالرجل إشارة إلى اشتراط كونه مكلفاً، وإلا فلا فساد، وقيد بـ"المشتهاة" احترازاً عن محاذاة الأمرد فإنها لا تفسد، وشدّ من أفسد بها، وأطلق فيها فعمت الحرة والأجنبية والزوجة والعجوز الشوهاء. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ۳۳۱، مراقي الفلاح بتصرف]
في صلاة إلخ الجار والمجرور في محل نصب على الحال أي حال كونهما في صلاة، فخرج محاذاة المجنونة، فإنها غير مفسدة؛ لعدم انعقاد صلاتها. [حاشية الطحطاوي (۳۲۹] مطلقة : فلا تبطل صلاة الجنازة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٢٩] مشتركة تحريمة: باقتدائهما بإمام أو اقتداؤها به مراقي الفلاح (۳۲۹] في مكان إلخ: فلو اختلف المكان بأن كانت المرأة على مكان عال بحيث لا يحاذي شيء منه شيئا منها لا تفسد [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٣٠] ونوى إمامتها فإن لم ينوها لا تكون في الصلاة فانتفت المحاذاة. [ مراقي الفلاح: ٣٣١] وهذا القيد مستغنى قيد الاشتراك؛ إذ لا اشتراك إلا بنية الإمام إمامتها؛ لأنه إذا لم ينو إمامتها لا يصح اقتداؤها. حاشية الطحطاوي: ۳۳۱] ولو اضطر إلخ وفي "الخانية " : إذا اضطر إلى الكشف يبني، وإلا لا، وبه جزم في التنوير وشرحه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٣١] عنه لعلمه
What invalidates the prayer: (responding to a sneeze with) 'May Allah have mercy on you', and answering a questioner about a rival with 'There is no god but Allah', and bad news by saying 'Inna lillah wa inna ilayhi raji'un' and good news by saying 'Alhamdulillah', and wonder by saying 'There is no god but Allah' or 'Subhanallah', and everything intended as a reply like 'O Yahya, take the book', and a mutayammim seeing water, and completion of the duration of the masah over the khuff and removing it, and the ummi learning a verse and the naked person finding a covering, and the one with an excuse being able to bow and prostrate, and the one with a valid sequence remembering a missed prayer, and appointing an imam who is not fit, ... and the complete and excused [person]. And answering a questioner etc. when it is said: 'Is there another god with Allah?' and he says: 'There is no god but Allah.' [Hashiyat al-Shalabi 1/394] By 'istirja': Zaid said: 'Inna lillah wa inna ilayhi raji'un', meaning one informs a praying person of sad news like the death of his son, and he says during prayer: 'Inna lillah wa inna ilayhi raji'un', his prayer is invalidated. And 'saar' i.e. one informs a praying person of joyful news like the birth of his son, and he says: 'Alhamdulillah', his prayer is invalidated. And 'ajab' etc. i.e. the prayer is invalidated by his answer to news that amazes him by saying: 'There is no god but Allah' or 'Subhanallah'. And 'wa kullu shay' etc.: he generalizes, so it includes whether it is from the Quran or otherwise. For example, if he mentions the two testimonies when the mu'adhdhin mentions them, or hears the mention of Allah and says 'Jalla jalaluh', or mentions the Prophet and sends blessings upon him, or says upon the imam's completion of the recitation 'Sadaqa Allahu al-'Azeem' or 'Sadaqa Rasuluh', or hears the devil and curses him, or a man calls him to say the takbir loudly and he does so, it is invalidated [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 326]. Like 'O Yahya': for example, a man named Yahya requests a book from a praying man, and the praying person says: O Yahya, take the book. 'Ma'an' meaning water that he has ability to use. 'Maraqi al-Falah' includes whether he is a follower or imam. As for when he is imam, it is apparent; as for when he is a follower, it is restricted to when his imam does not see the water. 'Wa tamam': meaning the prayer of the person praying is invalidated if the duration of the masah over his khuff is completed while he is in prayer, due to the removal of the purity of the feet. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 327] 'Muddat masih' etc.: it is for a resident one day and one night, and for a traveler three days and their nights. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 327] 'Satiran': he made it absolute, and it is restricted to a covering that it is obligatory for him to pray in, such that he owns it or it is permissible for him, and it is pure or impure and he has something to purify it with or not, except that a quarter of it is pure, so it excludes total impurity and what its owner has not permitted. [Maraqi al-Falah 327, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi adapted] 'Wa tadhakkur fa'itah' etc.: meaning if a person with a valid sequence remembers that he owes a missed prayer before this one, his prayer is invalidated. This invalidation is suspended. If he prays five [prayers] while remembering the missed one and makes it up before the time of the fifth leaves, the description of what he prayed before becomes void and it becomes supererogatory; if he does not make it up until the time of the fifth leaves, it becomes valid and its invalidation is lifted. [Maraqi al-Falah 328] 'Wa istikhlaf' etc.: meaning a reciter led them [in prayer], then an event preceded him in the middle of the prayer, so he appointed that reciter, an ummi from among the followers, then his prayer and their prayers are invalidated. And sunrise during Fajr, and its zenith during the two Eids, and the entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah, and the falling off of the cast from healing and the removal of the excuse of the excused one, and hadath intentionally or by the action of another, and fainting, and insanity, and janaba by looking or wet dream, and the alignment of a desirable woman in an absolute prayer shared in the tahrimah, in one place without a barrier, and he intends her imamate, and the emergence of the 'awrah of one who was preceded by hadath even if compelled to it, like a woman uncovering her forearm, and connected. And sunrise etc.: for example, a man begins the Fajr prayer and the sun rises during it, his prayer is invalidated. 'Wa zawaluha' etc.: for example, a group begins the prayer of Fitr or Eid and the sun passes its zenith while they are in their prayer, their prayer is invalidated. 'Wa suqut al-jabirah' etc.: meaning a man was wiping over a cast, then he began the prayer, and it fell off after healing, his prayer is invalidated. If it falls off not due to healing, it does not invalidate. Intentionally - it indicates that the prayer is not invalidated by preceding hadath, because the one preceded builds upon [the prayer] with the conditions known in building. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 329] 'Aw ihtilam': if it is said there is no need to mention the addition of invalidation to wet dream because of the prior invalidation by sleep? The answer: this is carried on the case where he sleeps during his prayer in a manner that does not invalidate it, then has a wet dream. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi modified 329] 'Wa muhadhat': meaning the alignment of a desirable woman with the man by her shin and ankle in the most correct view, even if she is a mahram for him or his wife, desired, even if past such as an ugly old woman. The correct interpretation of alignment is that the woman stands beside the man or in front of him without a barrier. It is restricted by 'man' indicating the condition that he is legally responsible, otherwise there is no invalidation. It is restricted by 'desirable' to exclude alignment of an amrad, it does not invalidate. And some have held it invalidates, and he made it general in that it includes the free woman, the foreign woman, the wife, and the ugly old woman. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 331, Maraqi al-Falah adapted] 'Fi salat' etc.: the prepositional phrase is in object position as a condition, i.e., while both are in prayer; thus it excludes alignment of a mad woman, for it does not invalidate due to the lack of validity of her prayer. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 329] 'Mutlaqat': so it does not invalidate the funeral prayer. [Maraqi al-Falah 329] 'Mushtarakatan fi al-tahrimah': by their following an imam or her following him. [Maraqi al-Falah 329] 'Fi makan' etc.: if the place differs, such that the woman is on a high place so that nothing of him aligns with anything of her, it does not invalidate. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 330] 'Wa nawa imamataha': if he does not intend it, she is not in the prayer, so the alignment is negated. [Maraqi al-Falah 331] And this condition is rendered unnecessary by the condition of being shared, because there is no sharing except by the imam intending her imamate; because if he does not intend her imamate, her following is not valid. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 331] 'Wa law idtara' etc.: and in al-Khaniyyah: if he is compelled to uncover, he builds [upon the prayer]; otherwise not; and it is stated definitively in al-Tanwir and its commentary. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 331] 'Anhu li-ilmihi' [?]
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive list of invalidators of prayer (mufsidat al-salah) from the Hanafi school, drawn from Nur al-Idah and its commentaries by al-Shalabi, al-Tahtawi, and the text Maraqi al-Falah. The list covers actions, speech, and changes of state that nullify the prayer if they occur intentionally or in certain circumstances. The commentary explains each item in detail. The main invalidators include: responding to a sneeze with 'Yarhamukallah' (an intentional reply in human words), answering a question about whether there is another god with 'La ilaha illallah' (even if it is dhikr, because it is intended as a reply), expressing sad news with 'Inna lillah wa inna ilayhi raji'un' or good news with 'Alhamdulillah', expressing wonder with 'La ilaha illallah' or 'Subhanallah', and any speech intended as a reply even if quoting Quran, such as saying 'Yahya khudh al-kitab' to respond to a request. A mutayammim seeing water (if he is able to use it) invalidates his prayer because tayammum is nullified. Completion of the duration of wiping over khuff (maskh) invalidates prayer for the same reason. Learning a verse by an ummi (someone who cannot recite) invalidates his prayer if he learns it and could have recited it later, but the text says 'ta'allum al-ummi ayah' meaning he learns a verse during prayer, thereby removing his excuse. Finding a covering by a naked person who was praying without covering invalidates because the condition of covering is now met. Ability to bow and prostrate by a person with an excuse (like illness) invalidates his prayer if he was praying with gestures. Remembering a missed prayer by one who observes sequence (tartib) invalidates the current prayer temporarily; if he makes up the missed one before the end of the current time, the current prayer becomes voluntary, otherwise it becomes valid. Appointing an unfit imam (like an ummi replacing a reciter) invalidates the prayer for all. Sunrise during Fajr, zenith during Eid prayer, entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah invalidate the prayer because the time has passed. The cast falling off after healing invalidates, but if it falls without healing it does not. Hadath (breaking wudu) intentionally or by another's action, fainting, insanity, janaba by looking or wet dream, alignment of a desirable woman (when both share the same prayer, same place, with intention of her following or him being her imam), and emergence of awrah (even if compelled) all invalidate. The commentary also clarifies that for alignment, the woman must be desirable (even an ugly old woman counts if desired?), and the man must be legally responsible; the alignment is by shin and ankle; and if the woman is on a higher place, it doesn't count. For hadath or exposure due to compulsion, the prayer may be built upon under certain conditions.

Key Terms
يرحمك الله (Yarhamukallah): A phrase said to a person who sneezes, meaning 'May Allah have mercy on you'. In prayer, saying it intentionally invalidates because it is a human reply.
استرجاع (Istirja'): Saying 'Inna lillah wa inna ilayhi raji'un' upon hearing sad news. This invalidates prayer if said in response to news.
محاذاة المشتهاة (Muhadhat al-mushtahat): Alignment of a desirable woman with a man in prayer, which invalidates the prayer if both share the same prayer (both praying) with one intending the other's imamate, in one place without barrier.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following actions would invalidate the prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Saying 'Alhamdulillah' upon receiving good news while in prayer.
B) Saying 'Subhanallah' without any external reason while in prayer.
C) Reciting Quran silently.
D) Moving three consecutive steps.

Key Takeaway
The prayer is invalidated by any intentional speech intended as a reply to another person, even if it is dhikr or Quranic, and by the removal of a condition of validity such as tayammum's excuse or alignment with a desirable woman.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
15 min
Invalidators of Prayer (Part 1): Time, Splint, Impurity, and Alignment
Ruling list with detailed commentary on invalidators of prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific invalidators related to time, splint, impurity, and alignment of a woman, and explain the conditions for alignment to invalidate prayer.

Core Idea
Sunrise during Fajr and zenith during Eid are time-based invalidators; alignment of a desired woman under specific conditions invalidates prayer.

This lesson examines the first set of invalidators of prayer from Nur al-Idah. These include time-related occurrences (sunrise during Fajr, zenith during Eid), the falling of a splint, intentional hadath, fainting, insanity, janabah, and the complex case of alignment (muhadhat) with a desired woman. Understanding these conditions is crucial to knowing when a prayer must be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the invalidator
For each item in the text, note what action or event causes the prayer to become invalid. For example, sunrise during Fajr is a time-based invalidator.
The text lists multiple invalidators; focus on their defining characteristics.
2
Extract conditions
For the alignment invalidator, list all conditions: the man must be accountable, the woman desired, both in prayer, same place, no barrier, common in tahrimah, and the man intends her imamship.
Each condition is explicitly stated in the commentary.
3
Distinguish invalidation from building
Note that some occurrences do not automatically invalidate; e.g., if a splint falls off not due to healing, or if hadath occurs unintentionally from another, the prayer can be built upon.
The text uses 'yabni' (builds) to indicate that prayer continues.
4
Examine exceptions
The commentary notes that alignment with an insane woman does not invalidate because her prayer is not valid. Similarly, an old woman past desire is included in 'desired' according to the soundest view.
Exceptions are highlighted to avoid over-application.
5
Apply to scenarios
Given a scenario, decide if the prayer is invalid or not by checking each condition. Practice with examples from the commentary.
Use the guided path as a checklist for analysis.
