كتاب الصلاة
ما يفسد الصلاة
للوضوء وقراءته ذاهبا أو عائدا للوضوء، ومكثه قدر أداء ركن بعد سبق الحدث
لا تسبيحه
مستيقظاً، ومجاوزته ماء قريباً لغيره وخروجه من المسجد بظن الحدث، ومجاوزته الصفوف في غيره ،بظنه وانصرافه ظانا أنه غير متوضئ ، أو أن مدة مسحه انقضت،
أو السترة
أو أن عليه فائتة أو نجاسة وإن لم يخرج من المسجد، وفتحه على غير إمامه، والتكبير
وشرحه
في هذه المسائل
أي يفسد الصلاة فتحه
بنية الانتقال لصلاة أخرى غير صلاته إذا حصلت هذه المذكورات قبل الجلوس الأخير مقدار التشهد، ويفسدها أيضاً مد الهمزة في التكبير، وقراءة ما لا يحفظه من مصحف،
من
الصلاة
ومكثه إلخ: أطلقه وهو مقيد بعدم العذر، أما إذا كان به عذر كمكثه لزحام أو لينقطع رعافه، فإنه يبني. وخروجه كما إذا أنزل من أنفه ماء فظنه دما فخرج من المسجد فسدت صلاته. بظن الحدث: قيد بـ"ظن الحدث"؛ لأنه لو ظن أنه افتتح على غير وضوء، أو كان ماسحاً على الخفين فظن أن مدة مسحه قد انقضت، أو كان متيمماً فرأى سراباً فظنه ماءً، أو كان في الظهر فظن أنه لم يصل الفجر، أو رأى حمرة في ثوبه فظن أنها نجاسة فانصرف حيث تفسد صلاته وإن لم يخرج من المسجد؛ لأن الانصراف على سبيل الرفض. (البحر الرائق) وانصرافه إلخ أي إذا انصرف المصلي عن موضع صلاته بظن أنه غير متوضئ أو مدة مسحه انقضت أو أن عليه فائتة تجب عليه أداؤها أولاً، تفسد صلاته في الصور كلها. المسجد: اعلم أنه قد وقع في نسخ "نور" "الإيضاح كلها بعد هذا ما صورته: "والأفضل الاستئناف خروجاً من الخلاف"، وفي بعضها: "الأفضل "الاستئناف" فقط، وهذا مما لا يحصل ؛ فإن المسائل كلها حكم فيها بفساد الصلاة معنى أفضلية الاستئناف؟ فلعلها من الشارح، ووقع ههنا سهو من الناسخين، فألحقها في المتن. غير إمامه: يشمل فتح المقتدي على المقتدي وعلى غير المصلي وعلى المصلي ،وحده وفتح الإمام والمنفرد على أي شخص كان، وكل ذلك مفسد إلا إذا قصد به التلاوة دون الفتح ونظيره ما لو قيل له: ما مالك؟ فقال: الخيل والبغال والحمير، فإنه يفسد صلاته إن أراد به جواباً، وإلا فلا وإن فتح على إمامه لا تفسد استحساناً. تبيين الحقائق: ۳۹۳/۱] والتكبير إلخ : قيد بـ"التكبير"؛ لأنه لو نوى بقلبه فقط لا يكون قاطعاً للأولى، وأخرج بـ"الصلاة" الصوم، وأخرج بـ " أخرى" ما إذا كانت عين الأولى. مثال الفساد كالمنفرد إذا نوى الاقتداء، وعكسه كمن انتقل بالتكبير من فرض إلى فرض أو نفل وعكسه بنيته مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٣٤]
فما
إذا حصلت إلخ قيد لبطلان الصلاة في جميع ما ذكره من قوله: "ورؤية متيمم ماء إلخ".
Book of Prayer
What Invalidates Prayer
And sunrise during Fajr, and its zenith during the two Eid prayers, and entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah, and falling off of the splint after healing, and removal of the excuse of the excused one, and hadath intentionally or by the action of another, and fainting, and insanity, and janabah by looking or wet dream, and alignment of a desired woman in an absolute prayer common in tahrimah in a single place without barrier and he intended her imamship, and appearance of the private part of one preceded by hadath even if compelled to it, like a woman uncovering her forearm,
And its explanation
And sunrise etc.: For example, a man began the Fajr prayer and the sun rose during it, so his prayer becomes invalid. And its zenith etc.: For example, a group began the Fitr or Eid prayer and the sun reached its zenith while they were in their prayer, so their prayer becomes invalid. And falling off of the splint etc.: That is, a man was wiping over a splint, then he began prayer, and it fell off after healing, so his prayer becomes invalid; and if it fell off not due to healing, it does not invalidate. It indicates that prayer is not invalidated by preceding hadath; because the one preceded builds upon the known conditions in the building. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 329]
Or wet dream: If it is said there is no need to mention the addition of invalidation to wet dream because it is already invalidated by sleep? The answer is that this is interpreted as when he slept in his prayer in a manner that does not invalidate it, then he had a wet dream [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with modification: 329]. And alignment: i.e., alignment of the man with a desired woman by her shin and ankle according to the soundest view, even if she is his mahram or wife who is desired, even if she is past desire like an ugly old woman. The correct interpretation of alignment is that the woman stands beside the man or in front of him without a barrier. The restriction to the man indicates the condition that he is obligated, otherwise there is no invalidation. The restriction to 'desired' excludes alignment with an amrad (beardless youth), for it does not invalidate. And some have held that it invalidates. And it was general, so it includes the free woman, the foreign woman, the wife, and the ugly old woman. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 331, Maraqi al-Falah with modification]
In a prayer etc.: The preposition and noun are in accusative as a circumstantial qualifier, meaning while both are in prayer. So alignment of an insane woman is excluded, for it does not invalidate due to the invalidity of her prayer. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 329] Absolute: so the funeral prayer is not invalidated. [Maraqi al-Falah: 329] Common in tahrimah: by their following an imam or her following him. [Maraqi al-Falah: 329] In a place etc.: If the place differed, such as the woman being in a high place such that nothing of her aligns with anything of him, it does not invalidate. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 330] And he intended her imamship: if he does not intend it, she is not in prayer, so alignment is negated. [Maraqi al-Falah: 331] This condition renders the condition of commonality unnecessary, since there is no commonality except by the imam's intention of her imamship, because if he does not intend her imamship, her following is not valid. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 331] And even if compelled etc.: In al-Khaniyah: if he is compelled to uncover, he builds; otherwise not, and it is affirmed in al-Tanwir and its commentary. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 331]
From him due to his knowledge
From
[PAGE_112]
Book of Prayer
What Invalidates Prayer
For ablution and his recitation going or returning for ablution, and his staying for the duration of performing a pillar after preceding hadath, not his tasbih, while awake, and his passing by nearby water for someone else, and his exiting the mosque due to suspicion of hadath, and his passing the rows in other than it due to his suspicion, and his departing thinking he is not in a state of ablution, or that the period of his wiping has expired, or the sutrah, or that he has a missed prayer or impurity even if he did not exit the mosque, and his prompting someone other than his imam, and the takbir
And its explanation
In these issues
That is, his prompting invalidates prayer
With the intention of transitioning to another prayer other than his prayer, if these mentioned things occur before the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud, and also invalidates it the prolongation of the hamzah in the takbir, and recitation from a mushaf of what he does not memorize,
From
Prayer
And his staying etc.: It was unrestricted but it is restricted to the case of no excuse; if he has an excuse like staying due to crowding or to stop his nosebleed, then he builds. And his exiting: like when water came out of his nose and he thought it was blood, so he exited the mosque, then his prayer is invalid. Due to suspicion of hadath: It is restricted by 'suspicion of hadath' because if he thought he began without ablution, or he was wiping over khuffs and thought his wiping period had expired, or he was tayammum and saw a mirage and thought it was water, or he was in Zuhr and thought he had not prayed Fajr, or he saw redness on his garment and thought it was impurity, so he left, then his prayer is invalid even if he did not exit the mosque, because the departure is by way of abandonment. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) And his departing etc.: That is, if the praying person departs from his place of prayer thinking he is not in a state of ablution, or his wiping period has expired, or that he has a missed prayer that he must perform first, his prayer is invalid in all these cases. The mosque: Know that in the copies of Nur al-Idah all after this is: 'And the best is to start anew to exit from disagreement', and in some copies: 'The best is to start anew' only, and this is not obtained; for in all these issues the ruling is invalidation of prayer, so what is the meaning of preferring to start anew? Perhaps it is from the commentator, and here occurred an oversight of the copyists, so they appended it to the text. Other than his imam: This includes the follower prompting another follower, or someone not praying, or the praying person alone, and the prompting of the imam and the individual to any person, and all of that invalidates except if he intended recitation without prompting; and its analogy: if someone said to him: 'What is your property?' and he said: 'Horses, mules, and donkeys', it invalidates his prayer if he intended it as a response; otherwise no. And if he prompts his imam, it does not invalidate by istihsan. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/393] And the takbir etc.: It is restricted by 'takbir' because if he intends in his heart only, it is not a cutter of the first. And by 'prayer', fasting is excluded, and by 'another', if it is the same as the first. Example of invalidation: the individual if he intends to follow, and its opposite: one who transitions by takbir from a fard to a fard or nafl and its opposite by his intention. [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 334]
So what
If it occurs etc. is a restriction for the invalidation of prayer in all that he mentioned from his statement: 'And seeing of water by a mutayammim etc.'
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah lists the invalidators of prayer (mufsidat al-salah) in the Hanafi school, followed by a detailed commentary. The invalidators are divided into two sections on pages 111-112. The first section covers: sunrise during Fajr (if the sun rises while one is in Fajr prayer, it invalidates), zenith of the sun during Eid prayers (if the sun reaches zenith during Eid prayer, it invalidates), entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah (if the time for Asr enters while one is in Jumu'ah prayer, it invalidates), falling off of a splint after healing (if one was wiping over a splint and it falls off after healing, prayer invalidates; if it falls off without healing, it does not), removal of an excuse (e.g., a woman's excuse of istihadah ends while she is praying, invalidates), intentional hadath or by another's action (e.g., if someone forces water into one's mouth causing wudu to break), fainting, insanity, janabah due to looking or wet dream (with the nuance that if one sleeps in a way that does not invalidate prayer and then has a wet dream, it invalidates), alignment of a desired woman (muhadhat al-mushtahah) with specific conditions: the man must be a responsible person, the woman must be desired, they must be in the same place without barrier, both in a prayer that is absolute (not funeral) and common in tahrimah (by following the same imam or her following him), and the man must intend her imamship. Also, appearance of a limb that is part of 'awrah due to necessity (e.g., a woman uncovering her forearm) invalidates. The commentary explains each point with examples and cites sources like Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah. The second section continues with more invalidators: leaving the prayer for ablution and reciting while going or returning, staying for the duration of a pillar after hadath without excuse (but if there is an excuse like crowd or nosebleed, one may build), passing by nearby water for someone else (i.e., if one sees water and goes to it for someone else's benefit), exiting the mosque due to suspicion of hadath (e.g., thinking one has broken wudu), passing the rows in a mosque other than one's own due to suspicion, departing from one's place thinking one is not in wudu, or that the wiping period expired, or that one has a missed prayer, or impurity on one's clothes (even if not exiting mosque), prompting someone other than one's imam (if one prompts another follower or someone not praying, it invalidates, but prompting one's imam does not by istihsan), and the takbir (if one says takbir with the intention of switching to another prayer, it invalidates). The commentary also notes a copyist error about 'starting anew' being appended to the text. The overall lesson is a comprehensive list of invalidators with their conditions, as per the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity (minor or major) that breaks wudu or requires ghusl.
محاذاة المشتهاة (muhadhat al-mushtahah): Alignment of a man in prayer with a woman who is desired, in the same place, without barrier, while both are in prayer and the man intends her imamship.
الجبيرة (al-jabirah): A splint or bandage placed on a wound over which wiping (mash) is permitted during wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first part of the passage, which of the following is NOT an invalidator of prayer?
A) Sunrise during Fajr
B) Falling of splint after healing
C) Passing by water for another's use
D) Intentional hadath

Key Takeaway
Prayer is invalidated by specific events; knowing them ensures that one does not continue an invalid prayer and can repeat it correctly.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
15 min
Invalidators of Prayer (Part 2): Actions During Prayer, Prompting, and Takbir
Ruling list with commentary on invalidators involving movement, speech, and intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the invalidators related to leaving the prayer, exiting the mosque, prompting, and takbir, and apply the conditions for each.

Core Idea
Leaving the prayer for wudu, exiting the mosque out of suspicion, and intentional prompting of others invalidate prayer; intent matters in takbir.

This lesson covers the second set of invalidators from Nur al-Idah, which focus on actions that sever the continuity of prayer. These include leaving for ablution, staying after hadath, exiting the mosque due to false assumptions, departing from one's place thinking one is impure, prompting someone other than the imam, and the takbir for transitioning to another prayer. Understanding these ensures the prayer remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify actions that break continuity
The text lists actions like leaving for wudu, staying for a pillar after hadath without excuse, exiting the mosque, and departing from the prayer place. These break the state of prayer if done deliberately or based on incorrect assumptions.
Focus on the element of intent: if there is a legitimate excuse, the prayer is built upon.
2
Distinguish between exiting and building
If a person has a valid excuse (e.g., crowding, nosebleed), they may stay or exit without invalidating. The commentary specifies that building is allowed for the excused.
The default is invalidation unless an excuse is present.
3
Analyze prompting (fath) and its exceptions
Prompting someone other than your imam invalidates, except if intended as recitation. Prompting the imam is allowed by istihsan. Also, if one is asked a question and answers with the intention of informing, it invalidates.
The key is intention: if the words are meant as recitation or not as a response, they do not invalidate.
4
Understand the takbir condition
If one says takbir with the intention of switching to another prayer, it invalidates the current prayer. However, if one only intends in the heart, it does not invalidate.
The physical utterance of takbir with intention of transition is necessary for invalidation.
5
Apply to scenarios
Given scenarios involving staying after hadath, exiting mosque, or prompting, determine if the prayer is invalid or if building is allowed.
Check for excuses and intentions.

كتاب الصلاة
ما يفسد الصلاة
وطلوع الشمس في الفجر، وزوالها في العيدين، ودخول وقت العصر في الجمعة، وسقوط الجبيرة عن برء وزوال عذر المعذور، والحدث عمداً أو بصنع غيره، والإغماء، والجنون، والجنابة بنظر أو احتلام ومحاذاة المشتهاة في صلاة مطلقة مشتركة تحريمة في مكان متحد بلا حائل ونوى إمامتها وظهور عورة من سبقه الحدث ولو اضطر إليه، ككشف المرأة ذراعها،
وشرحه
وطلوع الشمس إلخ : مثلاً شرع رجل في صلاة الفجر وطلعت الشمس في أثنائها فسدت صلاته. وزوالها إلخ: مثلاً شرع قوم في صلاة الفطر أو العيد فزالت الشمس وهم في صلاتهم فسدت صلاتهم. وسقوط الجبيرة إلخ أي كان الرجل ماسحا على جبيرة، فشرع في الصلاة فسقطت بعد برء فسدت صلاته، ولو سقطت لا عن برء لا تفسد عمدا أفاد أن الصلاة لا تفسد بسبق الحدث؛ لأن المسبوق به يبني بالشروط المعلومة في البناء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٢٩]
أو احتلام إن قيل لا حاجة إلى ذكر إضافة البطلان إلى الاحتلام لسبق بطلانها بالنوم؟ فالجواب أن هذا محمول على ما إذا نام في صلاته على وجه لا يبطلها فاحتلم [حاشية الطحطاوي بتغيير : ٣٢٩] ومحاذاة: أي محاذاة الرجل المشتهاة بساقها وكعبها في الأصح ولو محرماً له أو زوجة اشتهت ولو ماضياً كعجوز شوهاء، والتفسير الصحيح للمحاذاة هو أن تقوم المرأة بجنب الرجل أو قدامه من غير حائل، إنما قيد بالرجل إشارة إلى اشتراط كونه مكلفاً، وإلا فلا فساد، وقيد بـ"المشتهاة" احترازاً عن محاذاة الأمرد فإنها لا تفسد، وشدّ من أفسد بها، وأطلق فيها فعمت الحرة والأجنبية والزوجة والعجوز الشوهاء. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ۳۳۱، مراقي الفلاح بتصرف]
في صلاة إلخ الجار والمجرور في محل نصب على الحال أي حال كونهما في صلاة، فخرج محاذاة المجنونة، فإنها غير مفسدة؛ لعدم انعقاد صلاتها. [حاشية الطحطاوي (۳۲۹] مطلقة : فلا تبطل صلاة الجنازة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٢٩] مشتركة تحريمة: باقتدائهما بإمام أو اقتداؤها به مراقي الفلاح (۳۲۹] في مكان إلخ: فلو اختلف المكان بأن كانت المرأة على مكان عال بحيث لا يحاذي شيء منه شيئا منها لا تفسد [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٣٠] ونوى إمامتها فإن لم ينوها لا تكون في الصلاة فانتفت المحاذاة. [ مراقي الفلاح: ٣٣١] وهذا القيد مستغنى قيد الاشتراك؛ إذ لا اشتراك إلا بنية الإمام إمامتها؛ لأنه إذا لم ينو إمامتها لا يصح اقتداؤها. حاشية الطحطاوي: ۳۳۱] ولو اضطر إلخ وفي "الخانية " : إذا اضطر إلى الكشف يبني، وإلا لا، وبه جزم في التنوير وشرحه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٣١]

Book of Prayer
What Invalidates Prayer
And sunrise during Fajr, and its zenith during the two Eid prayers, and entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah, and falling off of the splint after healing, and removal of the excuse of the excused one, and hadath intentionally or by the action of another, and fainting, and insanity, and janabah by looking or wet dream, and alignment of a desired woman in an absolute prayer common in tahrimah in a single place without barrier and he intended her imamship, and appearance of the private part of one preceded by hadath even if compelled to it, like a woman uncovering her forearm,
And its explanation
And sunrise etc.: For example, a man began the Fajr prayer and the sun rose during it, so his prayer becomes invalid. And its zenith etc.: For example, a group began the Fitr or Eid prayer and the sun reached its zenith while they were in their prayer, so their prayer becomes invalid. And falling off of the splint etc.: That is, a man was wiping over a splint, then he began prayer, and it fell off after healing, so his prayer becomes invalid; and if it fell off not due to healing, it does not invalidate. It indicates that prayer is not invalidated by preceding hadath; because the one preceded builds upon the known conditions in the building. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 329]
Or wet dream: If it is said there is no need to mention the addition of invalidation to wet dream because it is already invalidated by sleep? The answer is that this is interpreted as when he slept in his prayer in a manner that does not invalidate it, then he had a wet dream [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with modification: 329]. And alignment: i.e., alignment of the man with a desired woman by her shin and ankle according to the soundest view, even if she is his mahram or wife who is desired, even if she is past desire like an ugly old woman. The correct interpretation of alignment is that the woman stands beside the man or in front of him without a barrier. The restriction to the man indicates the condition that he is obligated, otherwise there is no invalidation. The restriction to 'desired' excludes alignment with an amrad (beardless youth), for it does not invalidate. And some have held that it invalidates. And it was general, so it includes the free woman, the foreign woman, the wife, and the ugly old woman. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 331, Maraqi al-Falah with modification]
In a prayer etc.: The preposition and noun are in accusative as a circumstantial qualifier, meaning while both are in prayer. So alignment of an insane woman is excluded, for it does not invalidate due to the invalidity of her prayer. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 329] Absolute: so the funeral prayer is not invalidated. [Maraqi al-Falah: 329] Common in tahrimah: by their following an imam or her following him. [Maraqi al-Falah: 329] In a place etc.: If the place differed, such as the woman being in a high place such that nothing of her aligns with anything of him, it does not invalidate. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 330] And he intended her imamship: if he does not intend it, she is not in prayer, so alignment is negated. [Maraqi al-Falah: 331] This condition renders the condition of commonality unnecessary, since there is no commonality except by the imam's intention of her imamship, because if he does not intend her imamship, her following is not valid. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 331] And even if compelled etc.: In al-Khaniyah: if he is compelled to uncover, he builds; otherwise not, and it is affirmed in al-Tanwir and its commentary. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 331]
From him due to his knowledge

What Invalidates Prayer
For ablution and his recitation going or returning for ablution, and his staying for the duration of performing a pillar after preceding hadath, not his tasbih, while awake, and his passing by nearby water for someone else, and his exiting the mosque due to suspicion of hadath, and his passing the rows in other than it due to his suspicion, and his departing thinking he is not in a state of ablution, or that the period of his wiping has expired, or the sutrah, or that he has a missed prayer or impurity even if he did not exit the mosque, and his prompting someone other than his imam, and the takbir

That is, his prompting invalidates prayer
With the intention of transitioning to another prayer other than his prayer, if these mentioned things occur before the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud, and also invalidates it the prolongation of the hamzah in the takbir, and recitation from a mushaf of what he does not memorize,
From
Prayer
And his staying etc.: It was unrestricted but it is restricted to the case of no excuse; if he has an excuse like staying due to crowding or to stop his nosebleed, then he builds. And his exiting: like when water came out of his nose and he thought it was blood, so he exited the mosque, then his prayer is invalid. Due to suspicion of hadath: It is restricted by 'suspicion of hadath' because if he thought he began without ablution, or he was wiping over khuffs and thought his wiping period had expired, or he was tayammum and saw a mirage and thought it was water, or he was in Zuhr and thought he had not prayed Fajr, or he saw redness on his garment and thought it was impurity, so he left, then his prayer is invalid even if he did not exit the mosque, because the departure is by way of abandonment. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) And his departing etc.: That is, if the praying person departs from his place of prayer thinking he is not in a state of ablution, or his wiping period has expired, or that he has a missed prayer that he must perform first, his prayer is invalid in all these cases. The mosque: Know that in the copies of Nur al-Idah all after this is: 'And the best is to start anew to exit from disagreement', and in some copies: 'The best is to start anew' only, and this is not obtained; for in all these issues the ruling is invalidation of prayer, so what is the meaning of preferring to start anew? Perhaps it is from the commentator, and here occurred an oversight of the copyists, so they appended it to the text. Other than his imam: This includes the follower prompting another follower, or someone not praying, or the praying person alone, and the prompting of the imam and the individual to any person, and all of that invalidates except if he intended recitation without prompting; and its analogy: if someone said to him: 'What is your property?' and he said: 'Horses, mules, and donkeys', it invalidates his prayer if he intended it as a response; otherwise no. And if he prompts his imam, it does not invalidate by istihsan. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/393] And the takbir etc.: It is restricted by 'takbir' because if he intends in his heart only, it is not a cutter of the first. And by 'prayer', fasting is excluded, and by 'another', if it is the same as the first. Example of invalidation: the individual if he intends to follow, and its opposite: one who transitions by takbir from a fard to a fard or nafl and its opposite by his intention. [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 334]
So what
If it occurs etc. is a restriction for the invalidation of prayer in all that he mentioned from his statement: 'And seeing of water by a mutayammim etc.'
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah lists the invalidators of prayer (mufsidat al-salah) in the Hanafi school, followed by a detailed commentary. The invalidators are divided into two sections on pages 111-112. The first section covers: sunrise during Fajr (if the sun rises while one is in Fajr prayer, it invalidates), zenith of the sun during Eid prayers (if the sun reaches zenith during Eid prayer, it invalidates), entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah (if the time for Asr enters while one is in Jumu'ah prayer, it invalidates), falling off of a splint after healing (if one was wiping over a splint and it falls off after healing, prayer invalidates; if it falls off without healing, it does not), removal of an excuse (e.g., a woman's excuse of istihadah ends while she is praying, invalidates), intentional hadath or by another's action (e.g., if someone forces water into one's mouth causing wudu to break), fainting, insanity, janabah due to looking or wet dream (with the nuance that if one sleeps in a way that does not invalidate prayer and then has a wet dream, it invalidates), alignment of a desired woman (muhadhat al-mushtahah) with specific conditions: the man must be a responsible person, the woman must be desired, they must be in the same place without barrier, both in a prayer that is absolute (not funeral) and common in tahrimah (by following the same imam or her following him), and the man must intend her imamship. Also, appearance of a limb that is part of 'awrah due to necessity (e.g., a woman uncovering her forearm) invalidates. The commentary explains each point with examples and cites sources like Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah. The second section continues with more invalidators: leaving the prayer for ablution and reciting while going or returning, staying for the duration of a pillar after hadath without excuse (but if there is an excuse like crowd or nosebleed, one may build), passing by nearby water for someone else (i.e., if one sees water and goes to it for someone else's benefit), exiting the mosque due to suspicion of hadath (e.g., thinking one has broken wudu), passing the rows in a mosque other than one's own due to suspicion, departing from one's place thinking one is not in wudu, or that the wiping period expired, or that one has a missed prayer, or impurity on one's clothes (even if not exiting mosque), prompting someone other than one's imam (if one prompts another follower or someone not praying, it invalidates, but prompting one's imam does not by istihsan), and the takbir (if one says takbir with the intention of switching to another prayer, it invalidates). The commentary also notes a copyist error about 'starting anew' being appended to the text. The overall lesson is a comprehensive list of invalidators with their conditions, as per the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الفتح (al-fath): Prompting or correcting someone in prayer, usually by reciting a verse or phrase to help them.
التكبير (al-takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'. In this context, using takbir to transition to another prayer invalidates the current one if uttered with that intention.
الاستئناف (al-isti'naf): Starting anew; restarting the prayer from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second part of the passage, which of the following invalidates prayer?
A) Staying to stop a nosebleed.
B) Prompting the imam with the intention of recitation.
C) Leaving the mosque due to suspicion of hadath that turns out to be false.
D) Intending in the heart to switch to another prayer without uttering takbir.

Key Takeaway
Actions based on suspicion of impurity or invalidity, as well as intentional transitions to other prayers, invalidate the prayer unless a valid excuse permits building.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Invalidators of Prayer: The Role of Assumption and Excuse
Enumeration of invalidators of prayer with commentary on conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the primary actions that invalidate prayer according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between invalidating actions based on certainty versus assumption (zann) with or without excuse.

Core Idea
A prayer is invalidated by specific actions; many hinge on acting upon a mistaken assumption (zann) without excuse.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lists the nullifiers of prayer. It is not enough to know merely the list; one must understand the conditions that turn an otherwise permissible action into an invalidator. The key theme is the role of 'zann' (strong assumption) and the distinction between having an excuse or not. The commentary (sharh) clarifies that staying still after hadath is only invalid if without excuse, and exiting the mosque is only invalid if based on zann.

Guided Path
1
Classify each invalidator
Group the listed actions into categories: actions related to wudu (going for wudu, reciting while going/returning), actions based on mistaken assumptions (exiting mosque, turning away, passing through rows), actions related to recitation/takbir (prompting others, intending another prayer, elongating hamza), and physical preconditions (performing pillars with uncovered private parts or impurity).
This helps internalize the scope of mufsidat.
2
Identify the role of zann
For each action that involves an assumption (e.g., exiting mosque based on thinking wudu is broken), check if the text explicitly uses 'zann' (ظن). Understand that without zann—i.e., with certainty or mere doubt—the ruling changes. For certainty, the prayer is already invalid by the hadath itself; for doubt, the prayer remains valid.
Zann is a strong assumption that leads to action; it is not certainty or suspicion.
3
Distinguish excuse from no excuse
For actions like staying still after hadath, the commentary stresses that if there is an excuse (e.g., crowding, nosebleed), the prayer is not invalidated. Identify which invalidators have an explicit excuse exception and which are absolute.
The Hanafi school values continuity of prayer; only deliberate or careless invalidators break it.
4
Apply to a novel scenario
Consider a person who sneezes during prayer and thinks he has broken wudu (but actually hasn't). He then exits the mosque to redo wudu. Determine whether his prayer is invalid by examining the conditions of zann and excuse.
Answer: It is invalid because he acted on zann without excuse; exiting on zann is invalidating.
5
Summarize the legal principle
State the overarching rule: 'Deliberate actions or actions based on unjustified assumption (zann) that interrupt the continuity of prayer invalidate it; actions with a valid excuse or based on certainty do not invalidate (though certainty of hadath already invalidates).'
This principle unifies the seemingly disparate list.

[مراقي الفلاح: ٣٣٧]
وعدم إعادة الجلوس إلخ كمن صلى صلاة وجلس في آخرها، وتذكر بعد ما قعد قدر التشهد أنه ترك سجدة صلاتية في ركعة من هذه الصلاة، فسجدها و لم يعد الجلوس الأخير فسدت صلاته؛ لأنه لا يعتد بالجلوس الأخير إلا بعد تمام الأركان نائماً : أي رجل صلى صلاة وأدى ركنا من أركانها حال كونه نائما، ولم يعده بعد الانتباه منه تفسد صلاته وقهقهة إمام إلخ أي صلى مسبوق مع الإمام، فلما جلس الإمام في القعدة الأخيرة وأتمها قهقه مكان التسليم، تفسد صلاة المسبوق لا صلاة الإمام أما فساد صلاة المسبوق فلكون المفسد في وسط صلاته، وأما عدم فساد صلاة الإمام؛ فلأن المنافي وجد في آخر صلاته.
Things that invalidate prayer: [Invalidated by] going for ablution and reciting while going or returning for ablution, and his staying for the duration of performing a pillar after the occurrence of an event, not his glorification, while awake; and his passing by water nearby belonging to someone else, and his exiting the mosque due to an assumption of an event; and his passing through rows in other than it due to his assumption; and his turning away assuming he is not in ablution, or that his wiping period has expired, or that there is a missed prayer, or impurity, even if he did not exit the mosque; and his prompting someone other than his imam; and the takbir with the intention of transition to another prayer other than his prayer if these mentioned [actions] occur before the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud. It also invalidates elongating the hamza in takbir, and reciting from a mushaf what he does not know by heart. [Commentary: His staying etc.: It is unrestricted, but it is restricted to absence of excuse. As for if there is an excuse, like his staying due to crowding or to stop his nosebleed, then he builds upon [his prayer]. And his exiting, like when water came out of his nose and he thought it was blood, so he exited the mosque, his prayer is invalidated. By assumption of event: It is restricted by 'assumption of event' because if he thought he began without ablution, or he was wiping over khuffs and thought that his wiping period had expired, or he was performing tayammum and saw a mirage and thought it was water, or he was in Zuhr and thought he had not prayed Fajr, or he saw redness on his garment and thought it was impurity and turned away, then his prayer is invalidated even if he did not exit the mosque, because turning away is [equivalent to] rejection. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) And his turning away etc.: i.e., if the praying person turns away from his place of prayer assuming he is not in ablution or his wiping period expired or that there is a missed prayer he must perform first, his prayer is invalidated in all cases. The mosque: Know that in copies of Nur al-Idah after this there is: 'The better is to start anew to exit from difference,' and in some: 'The better is to start anew' only, and this is not obtained; for all the cases are judged to have invalidation of prayer, so what is the meaning of preference of starting anew? Perhaps it is from the commentator, and here an oversight from the copyists occurred, so they appended it to the text. Other than his imam: It includes the prompting of a follower to another follower, to a non-praying person, and to the praying person alone, and the prompting of the imam and the one praying alone to any person, all of that is invalidating except if he intended recitation and not prompting; and a similar case is when someone is asked: 'What is your property?' and he says: 'Horses, mules, and donkeys,' then it invalidates his prayer if he intended it as an answer, otherwise not; and if he prompts his imam, it does not invalidate by istihsan. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/393) And the takbir etc.: It is restricted to takbir because if he intended only with his heart, it does not cut off the first [prayer]; and by 'prayer' fasting is excluded; and by 'another' the case where it is the same [prayer] is excluded. An example of invalidation is the one praying alone when he intends to follow; and its opposite is someone who transitions by takbir from one obligatory prayer to another or supererogatory and its opposite by his intention. (Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 334) So if these occur etc.: This is a condition for the invalidation of prayer in all that he mentioned from his saying: 'And the sighting of water by a mutayammim etc.' And performing a pillar or its possibility, such as bowing, while uncovering the private parts or with a preventing impurity; and the follower's preceding [the imam] in a pillar in which the imam did not share with him; and the follower's following the imam in sajdat al-sahw for the one who is preceded; and the non-repetition of the final sitting after performing a essential prostration that he remembered after the sitting; and the non-repetition of a pillar performed while sleeping; and the laughter of the imam of the one who is preceded; and his intentional event after the final sitting; and the salaam at the end of two rak'ats in other than a two-rak'at prayer, thinking he is a traveler or that it is Friday, or that it is tarawih like Maghrib, and the four-rak'at of a resident when he was resident in Isha, or he was new to Islam and thought the obligatory prayer was two rak'ats. (Then commentary: Or its possibility: i.e., the passage of time that would suffice for performing a pillar. (Maraqi al-Falah 337) Uncovering the private parts etc.: What is meant by uncovering the private parts is what includes the limb; the summary is that much uncovering in much time is harmful, and little in little is not harmful, like much a quarter in little, and little in much. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 337 with some rearrangement) And the follower's preceding etc.: Like when he bowed and raised his head before the imam and did not repeat with him, or after him and made salaam; and if he did not make salaam with the imam and preceded him in bowing and prostrating in all rak'ats, he makes up a rak'at without recitation; because he is a mudrik (latecomer) initially [as] the imam's prayer is subsequent, and he makes up before the imam finishes; and he missed the first rak'at by leaving following the imam in bowing and prostrating, so his bowing and prostrating in the second become a make-up for the first, and in the third for the second, and in the fourth for the third, so he makes up after him a rak'at without recitation. (Maraqi al-Falah 337) For the one preceded: That the one preceded stands after the imam has made salaam or before his salaam after the imam's sitting to the extent of tashahhud, and the one preceded ties his rak'at with a prostration, then the imam remembers sajdat al-sahw and he follows him, then his prayer is invalidated; because he followed after the occurrence of separation and its obligation, so his prayer is invalidated. And we restricted the standing of the one preceded to being after the imam's sitting to the extent of tashahhud; because if it was before, it does not suffice him; because the imam still has an obligation that the one preceded cannot perform alone, so his prayer is invalidated. (Maraqi al-Falah 337) And the non-repetition of the final sitting etc.: Like someone who prayed a prayer and sat at its end, and after he sat to the extent of tashahhud he remembered that he skipped a prostration of prayer in one rak'at of this prayer, so he prostrated it and did not repeat the final sitting, then his prayer is invalidated; because the final sitting is not considered valid until after the completion of the pillars. While sleeping: i.e., a man who prayed a prayer and performed a pillar of its pillars while being asleep, and did not repeat it after awakening, his prayer is invalidated. And the laughter of the imam etc.: i.e., a person prayed behind an imam, and when the imam sat in the final sitting and completed it, he laughed in place of the salaam; the prayer of the one being preceded is invalidated, not the imam's prayer. As for the invalidation of the one preceded's prayer, it is because the invalidating factor occurred in the middle of his prayer; and as for the non-invalidation of the imam's prayer, because the contradictory occurred at the end of his prayer.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive listing of actions that invalidate the prayer (mufsidat al-salah) according to the Hanafi school, as found in Nur al-Idah with interlinear commentary. The author begins by enumerating various nullifiers including: going to perform wudu during prayer, reciting while going or returning for wudu, staying still long enough to perform a pillar after the occurrence of hadath (without excuse), passing by water belonging to another without need, exiting the mosque due to a mistaken assumption of breaking wudu, passing through rows outside the mosque due to such assumption, turning away from the prayer direction assuming impurity or missed obligation, prompting someone other than the imam, and pronouncing takbir with the intention of transitioning to another prayer. The commentary clarifies that mere accidental passing by water does not invalidate unless the water is near and the person leaves prayer for it. Exiting the mosque is invalidating only if done based on a mistaken assumption (zann) of hadath; if one is certain of hadath, exiting is required and prayer is not invalidated because the hadath itself already invalidated. Similarly, turning away from prayer place based on mistaken assumption invalidates. The text also discusses that prompting (fat-h) on someone other than the imam invalidates, with exceptions for cases where one intends only recitation. The second part covers additional nullifiers: performing a pillar (like ruku) while the private parts are uncovered or with a preventing impurity; the follower preceding the imam in a pillar; the follower following the imam in sajdat al-sahw when the follower is a masbuq (one who missed part); not repeating the final sitting after performing a forgotten prostration; not repeating a pillar performed while sleeping; the imam's laughter when there is a masbuq; intentional hadath after the final sitting; and ending the prayer with salaam after two rak'ats in non-two-rak'at prayers under mistaken assumptions. The commentary explains each: for example, a follower who competes with the imam in bowing and prostration throughout all rak'ats must make up a rak'at without recitation. The laughter of the imam invalidates the masbuq's prayer but not the imam's own, because for the imam it occurred at the very end. This passage is studied as part of the fiqh of salah, where students must memorize these nullifiers and understand their conditions.

Key Terms
مكثه قدر أداء ركن (mukthuhu qadra ada'i rukn): Staying still for the duration that would suffice to perform a pillar, e.g., one ruku or two long sujuds, after the occurrence of hadath (ritual impurity) without a valid excuse.
ظن الحدث (zann al-hadath): A strong assumption (not certainty) that one has broken wudu or that the duration of wiping has expired, leading to actions that invalidate prayer if acted upon incorrectly.
القهقهة (al-qahqaha): Loud laughter that includes letters (not just smile) and is intentional; in the context of prayer, it invalidates prayer if it occurs during the prayer, and for a masbuq (latecomer) it invalidates his prayer if the imam laughs at the end.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in Nur al-Idah, which of the following actions invalidates the prayer?
A) Reciting from a mushaf what one does not know by heart
B) Reciting a memorized verse from memory
C) Both A and B
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi nullifiers of prayer are conditioned by the presence or absence of excuse and the nature of the assumption (zann); not every interruption invalidates—only deliberate or careless actions based on unjustified assumption.

Actions That Invalidate Prayer (Mufsidat al-Salah)
List of prayer invalidators with commentary on conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the actions that invalidate prayer (mufsidat) and apply the conditions under which they invalidate.

Core Idea
A prayer is invalidated only when a mufsid occurs with awareness and without corrective action, except where intention matters.

Knowing what invalidates prayer is essential for every Muslim to preserve the validity of their worship. The Hanafi school outlines specific actions that nullify prayer, but each has conditions and exceptions. This lesson parses the classic list from Nur al-Idah with commentary that clarifies the precise scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify each mufsid
Read the list of invalidators from the text and note them: uncovering awrah, impurity, follower preceding imam, etc.
2
Analyze the condition of kashf al-'awrah
The ruling depends on how much is exposed and for how long. Distinguish 'much in much time' vs. 'little in little time'.
Much exposure in a short time is also harmful, but minimal exposure is excused.
3
Understand the follower's precedence (musabaqa)
If a follower performs a pillar before the imam and does not repeat it with him, prayer is invalid. If it happens in every rak'ah, he makes up an extra rak'ah without recitation.
The key is whether the follower intentionally fails to repeat the pillar with the imam.
4
Analyze masbuq scenarios
A masbuq must not follow the imam in sajdat al-sahw after standing independently. Also, if he stands before the imam sits for tashahhud, it is impermissible.
The masbuq's separation (infirad) is the critical moment.
5
Synthesize the timing principle
Some invalidators (like the imam's laughter) affect only the masbuq's prayer because they occur in the middle of his prayer, while at the end of the imam's prayer they do not invalidate the imam's.
The position in one's own prayer matters: middle vs. end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يفسد الصلاة
مع كشف العورة أو مع نجاسة مانعة، ومسابقة المقتدي بركن لم يشاركه فيه إمامه ومتابعة الإمام في سجود السهو للمسبوق، وعدم إعادة الجلوس الأخير بعد أداء سجدة صُلبية تذكرها بعد الجلوس، وعدم إعادة ركن أدّاه نائماً، وقهقهة إمام المسبوق، وحدثه العمد بعد الجلوس الأخير، والسلام على رأس ركعتين في غير الثنائية ظانا أنه مسافر أو أنها الجمعة، أو أنها التراويح كالمغرب ورباعية المقيم وقد كان مقيما العشاء، أو كان قريب عهد بالإسلام فظن الفرض ركعتين.
وهي كشف إلخ: المراد بكشف العورة ما يعم العضو منها، والحاصل أن الكشف الكثير في الزمن الكثير مضر، والقليل في القليل غير مضر كالكثير ربع في القليل، والقليل في الكثير. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٣٧] ومسابقة المقتدي إلخ كما لو ركع ورفع رأسه قبل الإمام ولم يعده معه، أو بعده وسلم، وإذا لم يسلم مع الإمام وسابقه بالركوع والسجود في كل الركعات قضى ركعة بلا قراءة؛ لأنه مدرك أول صلاة الإمام لاحق، وهو يقضي قبل فراغ الإمام، وقد فاتته الركعة الأولى بتركه متابعة الإمام في الركوع والسجود فيكون ركوعه وسجوده في الثانية قضاء عن الأول، وفي الثالثة عن الثانية، وفي الرابعة عن الثالثة، فيقضي بعده ركعة بغير قراءة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٣٧] للمسبوق بأن قام المسبوق بعد ما سلم الإمام أو قبل تسليمه بعد قعود الإمام قدر التشهد، وقيد المسبوق ركعته بسجدة، فتذكر الإمام سجود سهو فتابعه فسدت صلاته؛ لأنه اقتدى بعد وجود الانفراد ووجوبه فتفسد صلاته، وقيدنا قيام المسبوق بكونه بعد قعود الإمام قدر التشهد؛ لأنه إن كان قبله لم يجزه؛ لأن الإمام بقي عليه فرض لا ينفرد به المسبوق، فتفسد صلاته. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٣٧] وعدم إعادة الجلوس إلخ كمن صلى صلاة وجلس في آخرها، وتذكر بعد ما قعد قدر التشهد أنه ترك سجدة صلاتية في ركعة من هذه الصلاة، فسجدها و لم يعد الجلوس الأخير فسدت صلاته؛ لأنه لا يعتد بالجلوس الأخير إلا بعد تمام الأركان نائماً : أي رجل صلى صلاة وأدى ركنا من أركانها حال كونه نائما، ولم يعده بعد الانتباه منه تفسد صلاته وقهقهة إمام إلخ أي صلى مسبوق مع الإمام، فلما جلس الإمام في القعدة الأخيرة وأتمها قهقه مكان التسليم، تفسد صلاة المسبوق لا صلاة الإمام أما فساد صلاة المسبوق فلكون المفسد في وسط صلاته، وأما عدم فساد صلاة الإمام؛ فلأن المنافي وجد في آخر صلاته.
What invalidates prayer: with uncovering of the private parts or with preventative impurity, and the follower preceding the imam in a pillar in which the imam did not join him, and the follower following the imam in the prostration of forgetfulness for the one who is preceded [by the imam], and not repeating the final sitting after performing a substantive prostration that he remembered after sitting, and not repeating a pillar that he performed while asleep, and the laughter of the imam of the one preceded, and his intentional hadath after the final sitting, and saying salam at the end of two rak'ahs in other than the two-rak'ah prayer thinking he is a traveler or that it is Friday, or that it is tarawih like Maghrib and the four-rak'ah of the resident while he was resident for Isha, or he was new to Islam and thought the obligatory prayer is two rak'ahs. And it is: uncovering etc.: what is meant by uncovering the private parts is what includes the limb, and the conclusion is that much uncovering in much time is harmful, and little in little time is not harmful, like much in a quarter in little, and little in much. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 337] And the follower preceding etc. as if he bowed and raised his head before the imam and did not repeat it with him, or after him and said salam, and if he did not say salam with the imam and preceded him in bowing and prostration in all rak'ahs, he makes up a rak'ah without recitation because he is a latecomer who caught the first part of the imam's prayer, and he makes up before the imam finishes, and the first rak'ah was missed by him leaving following the imam in bowing and prostration, so his bowing and prostration in the second counts as qada for the first, in the third for the second, and in the fourth for the third, so he performs after it a rak'ah without recitation. [Maraqi al-Falah: 337] For the one preceded: that the preceded one stands after the imam said salam or before his salam after the imam sat for the duration of tashahhud, and the preceded one tied his rak'ah with a prostration, then the imam remembered the prostration of forgetfulness and he followed him, then his prayer becomes invalid because he followed after separation and its obligation occurred, so his prayer becomes invalid, and we restricted the preceded one standing being after the imam sat for the duration of tashahhud because if it was before it, it is not permissible for him because the imam still has an obligatory act that the preceded one cannot do alone, so his prayer becomes invalid. [Maraqi al-Falah: 337] And not repeating the final sitting etc.: like one who prayed a prayer and sat at its end, and remembered after sitting for the duration of tashahhud that he left a prayer prostration in a rak'ah of this prayer, so he performed it and did not repeat the final sitting, his prayer becomes invalid because the final sitting is not counted except after completion of the pillars. While asleep: i.e., a man prayed a prayer and performed a pillar of its pillars while being asleep, and did not repeat it after waking up, his prayer becomes invalid. And the laughter of the imam etc.: i.e., a preceded one prayed with the imam, then when the imam sat in the final sitting and completed it, he laughed instead of saying salam, the prayer of the preceded one becomes invalid, not the imam's prayer. As for the invalidity of the preceded one's prayer, it is because the invalidator occurred in the middle of his prayer. As for the lack of invalidity of the imam's prayer, it is because the contradictory occurred at the end of his prayer.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement enumerating the actions that invalidate prayer (mufsidat al-salah) according to the Hanafi school. It opens with the heading 'ما يفسد الصلاة' (what invalidates prayer) and then lists specific scenarios. The commentator then elaborates on each item. First, uncovering the private parts ('awrah) or having a preventative impurity (najasa mania) invalidates prayer, but the amount of exposure and duration matters: much exposure over much time is harmful, while little over little is not. Second, a follower (muqtadi) preceding the imam in a pillar (rukn) that the imam has not yet performed invalidates the prayer; the commentary gives the example of bowing and raising the head before the imam. If the follower consistently precedes the imam in every rak'ah, he must make up one rak'ah without recitation. Third, a masbuq (one who joins late) must not follow the imam in the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) after having stood independently; doing so invalidates his prayer. Fourth, if one remembers a missed prostration after the final sitting, he must repeat the sitting after performing the prostration; failure to do so invalidates the prayer. Fifth, a pillar performed while asleep must be repeated after waking; otherwise the prayer is invalid. Sixth, the imam's laughter at the end of the prayer invalidates only the masbuq's prayer, not the imam's, because the invalidator occurs in the middle of the masbuq's prayer but at the end of the imam's. The passage is a dense legal list typical of matn texts, requiring careful parsing of conditions.

Key Terms
كشف العورة (kashf al-'awrah): Exposing the private parts which are obligatory to cover during prayer.
نجاسة مانعة (najāsah māni'ah): Impurity that prevents the validity of prayer if present on the body, clothes, or place.
مسابقة المقتدي (musābaqat al-muqtadī): The follower performing a pillar before the imam, which invalidates prayer if done in all rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a masbuq stands after the imam has sat for the tashahhud, and then the imam performs sajdat al-sahw which the masbuq follows, what happens to the masbuq's prayer?
A) The prayer is valid because following the imam is obligatory.
B) The prayer becomes invalid because the masbuq followed after having separated.
C) The prayer is valid but requires sajdat al-sahw.
D) The prayer becomes invalid only if the masbuq intended to follow.

Key Takeaway
Each mufsid has specific conditions; knowing them ensures the validity of prayer and proper corrective measures.

The Reader's Slip: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Invalidating Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation slip rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on whether a recitation slip invalidates prayer, and apply the mufta bihi position to specific examples.

Core Idea
A recitation slip invalidates prayer only if it grossly changes the meaning, regardless of whether the mistaken word exists in the Quran.

Recitation mistakes during prayer are common and often cause concern. The Hanafi school has internal differences on when such mistakes invalidate the prayer. This lesson clarifies the key criteria and the relied-upon ruling, using examples from the classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Recognize that the dispute is about unintentional recitation slips (zallat al-qari) during prayer and whether they invalidate. The issue is not about intentional errors, which invalidate by consensus (except if the slip is praise).
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: invalidation depends on whether the meaning changes grossly (taghayyur fahish). Abu Yusuf: invalidation depends on whether the mistaken word has an equivalent in the Quran.
3
Understand the criteria
For Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, only gross meaning change matters; existence of the word is irrelevant. For Abu Yusuf, if the word exists in the Quran, the prayer remains valid even if meaning changes; if not, it invalidates.
Grammatical errors (i'rab) are not considered by either.
4
Apply to the four cases
Work through the four examples: (1) Iblis for Idris (gross change, word exists), (2) 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' for 'Ahad' (no change, exists), (3) 'hadha al-ghubar' for 'hadha al-ghurab' (gross change, word does not exist), (4) 'qiyamin' for 'qawwamin' (no change, does not exist). Determine the ruling for each according to both positions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: gross change of meaning invalidates. This is the majority view and is applied in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زلة القارئ
قال المحشي: لما رأيت مسائل زلة القارئ من أهم ما يجب العلم بها، والناس عنها غافلون، ووجدت ما في "الطحطاوي" على "المراقي" أوفى ما في هذا البحث ألحقته بهذا الكتاب مراعاة لمن سلك طريق الهدى، واجتنب سبل الهوى؛ ليكون واقيا لي من النيران، ووسيلة إلى الجنان، ورجحانا في ميزاني عند خفة الميزان، وعليه التكلان. قال: تكميل: زلة القارئ من أهم المسائل، وهي مبنية على قواعد ناشئة من الاختلافات لا كما قاعدة تبني عليها، فالأصل فيها عند الإمام ومحمد رحما: تغير المعنى تغيراً فاحشا، وعدمه للفساد، سواء كان اللفظ موجوداً في القرآن، أو لم يكن، وعند أبي يوسف له إن كان اللفظ نظيره موجوداً في القرآن لا تفسد مطلقاً تغير المعنى تغيرا فاحشا أولا، وإن لم يكن موجودا في القرآن تفسد مطلقا، ولا يعتبر الإعراب أصلا، ومحل الاختلاف في الخطأ والنسيان، أما في العمد فتفسد به مطلقا بالاتفاق إذا كان مما يفسد الصلاة، أما إذا كان ثناء فلا يفسد ولو تعمد ذلك أفاده ابن أمير الحاج.
زلة القاري [أي وقوع الزلل من القارئ في الصلاة. (الطحطاوي على الدر) وذهب بعض العلماء إلى عدم ا بخطأ القارئ أصلا ذكره في "القنية"، وحكي عن أبي القاسم الصفار أن الصلاة إذا جازت من وجه، وفسدت من وجه، يحكم بالفساد إحتياطا إلا في باب القراءة؛ لأن للناس فيها عموم البلوى (الطحطاوي على الدر) تغير المعنى إلخ: وفي "المضمرات": قرأ في الصلاة بخطأ فاحش، ثم أعاد، وقرأ صحيحا فصلاته جائزا، قال أبو السعود هذا يقتضي عدم فسادها بالخطأ في القراءة مطلقا تغير المعنى أم لا كان للكلمة التي وقع بها الخطأ مثل أو لا للفساد لف ونشر على الترتيب، أي إن تغير المعنى بزلة القارئ فسدت الصلاة عندهما، وإلا لا، ولا يشترط كون اللفظ المقروء به موجوداً في القرآن. سواء كان اللفظ إلخ اعلم أن المسألة على أربعة أوجه : إما أن يكون مثل اللفظ المقروء به زلة موجودا في القرآن أو لا، وكلاهما على نوعين: إما أن تغير المعنى تغيرا فاحشا أو لا، فالأول كما إذا قرأ: وإبليس وذا الكفل مكان قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِدْرِيسَ وَذَا الْكِفْلِ، والثاني: كما إذا قرأ: قُلْ هُوَ اللَّهُ أَحَدٌ مكان قوله تعالى: أحد، والثالث: كما إذا قرأ: "هذا "الغبار" مكان قوله: هَذَا الْغُرَابِ، وكذا إذا قرأ: "يوم تبلى السرائل" باللام في آخره مكان الراء في السَّرَائِرُ ، والرابع: كما إذا قرأ "قيامين" مكان وقوامين، والمعتبر في عدم الفساد عند عدم تغير المعنى كثيرا وجود المثل في القرآن عند أبي يوسف عليه، والموافقة في المعنى عندهما.
Chapter of the Reader's Slip
The commentator said: When I saw that the issues of the reader's slip are among the most important things that must be known, and people are heedless of them, and I found what is in al-Tahtawi on al-Maraqi is the most complete in this research, I appended it to this book out of consideration for whoever follows the path of guidance and avoids the paths of desire; so that it may be a protection for me from the Fire and a means to Paradise, and a weight in my scale when the scale is light. And upon Him is reliance. He said: Completion: The reader's slip is among the most important issues, and it is built upon rules arising from differences, not a single rule. The principle according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, is that change of meaning grossly invalidates, and absence of change [means] no invalidation, whether the word exists in the Quran or not. According to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, if the word's equivalent exists in the Quran, it does not invalidate absolutely, whether it changes meaning grossly or not; and if it does not exist in the Quran, it invalidates absolutely. And grammatical inflection (i'rab) is not considered at all. The point of difference is in error and forgetfulness. As for intentional [slip], it invalidates absolutely by consensus if it is among that which invalidates prayer. But if it is praise (thana'), it does not invalidate even if done intentionally; Ibn Amir Hajj reported that. Reader's slip: i.e., the occurrence of a slip from the reciter in prayer. (al-Tahtawi on al-Durr) And some scholars went to not paying attention to the reader's error at all; it is mentioned in al-Qunyah. And it is narrated from Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar that if the prayer is valid from one angle and invalid from another, it is judged invalid out of precaution except in the chapter of recitation, because people are generally afflicted with it. (al-Tahtawi on al-Durr) Change of meaning etc.: In al-Mudmarat: He recited in prayer with a gross error, then repeated and recited correctly, his prayer is valid. Abu al-Su'ud said: This implies non-invalidation by error in recitation absolutely, whether meaning changes or not, whether the word has a similar [in the Quran] or not. For invalidation, there is a twisted and spread arrangement: i.e., if the meaning changes by the reader's slip, the prayer becomes invalid according to them [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad], otherwise not. And it is not a condition that the recited word exist in the Quran. Whether the word etc. Know that the issue has four aspects: either the word read by slip has an equivalent in the Quran or not, and each is of two types: either it changes meaning grossly or not. The first is like when he reads: 'and Iblis and Dhul-Kifl' instead of His saying: {and Idris and Dhul-Kifl}; the second is like when he reads: 'Say He is Allah, One' instead of His saying: 'One'; the third is like when he reads: 'this dust' instead of His saying: {this crow}, and also when he reads: 'yawma tubla al-sara'il' with lam at the end instead of ra' in {al-sara'ir}; and the fourth is like when he reads: 'qiyamin' instead of 'qawwamin'. And what is considered in non-invalidation when the meaning does not change much is the existence of a similar in the Quran according to Abu Yusuf, and the agreement in meaning according to them [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad].
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is an inter_madhhab_dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the effect of a recitation mistake (zallat al-qari) during prayer on its validity. The commentator begins by emphasizing the importance of this topic and explains that he has appended the material from al-Tahtawi's commentary on al-Maraqi. The core ruling: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, a slip that grossly changes the meaning invalidates the prayer, regardless of whether the mistaken word exists in the Quran. According to Abu Yusuf, if the word's equivalent exists in the Quran, the prayer is not invalidated at all, whether the meaning changes or not; but if no equivalent exists, it invalidates absolutely. Grammatical errors (i'rab) are not considered. The disagreement applies only to unintentional errors (forgetfulness or mistake); intentional errors invalidate by consensus if they would invalidate the prayer, except if the slip is praise (thana'). Some scholars (like those mentioned in al-Qunyah) hold that recitation errors never invalidate prayer due to general need. The passage then categorizes four cases with examples: (1) reading 'Iblis and Dhul-Kifl' instead of 'Idris and Dhul-Kifl' – meaning changes grossly and the word exists in Quran; (2) reading 'Say He is Allah, One' instead of 'One' – meaning does not change and word exists; (3) reading 'this dust' instead of 'this crow' – meaning changes and word does not exist; (4) reading 'qiyamin' instead of 'qawwamin' – meaning does not change but word does not exist. According to Abu Yusuf, cases (1) and (2) do not invalidate because the word exists in the Quran; cases (3) and (4) invalidate because the word does not exist. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, cases (1) and (3) invalidate (gross meaning change), while (2) and (4) do not (no gross change), regardless of existence in the Quran. The practical consequence: the ruling differs depending on the imam followed; the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, relying on the change of meaning as the primary criterion.

Key Terms
زلة القارئ (zallat al-qāri'): A slip or mistake made by the reciter in Quran recitation during prayer.
تغير المعنى تغيرا فاحشا (taghayyur al-ma'nā taghayyuran fāḥishan): A gross change in meaning of the recited verse due to the slip, which invalidates prayer according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
ثناء (thanā'): Praise or glorification of Allah, which may be recited even if mistaken, and does not invalidate prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, which of the following recitation slips invalidates the prayer?
A) Reading 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' instead of 'Ahad' (one) - meaning unchanged, word exists.
B) Reading 'Iblis' instead of 'Idris' - meaning changes grossly, word exists.
C) Reading 'qiyamin' instead of 'qawwamin' - meaning unchanged, word does not exist.
D) Reading 'al-sara'il' instead of 'al-sara'ir' - meaning changes grossly, word does not exist.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a recitation slip during prayer invalidates only if it grossly changes the meaning, according to the relied-upon position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

The Reciter's Mistake: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Invalidating Prayer
Explains foundational disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on zillat al-qari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on zillat al-qari and apply the criterion to a given mistake scenario.

Core Idea
A recitation mistake invalidates prayer only if it changes the meaning obscenely (Abu Hanifa) or if the mistaken word has no Quranic counterpart (Abu Yusuf).

This passage introduces a foundational disagreement within the Hanafi school on when a recitation mistake (zillat al-qari) invalidates the prayer. While Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that any change of meaning in an obscene manner breaks the prayer, Imam Abu Yusuf adds an extra condition: if the mistaken word has a similar counterpart elsewhere in the Quran, the prayer remains valid even if the meaning changes. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly applying the rulings in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and legal effect
The act is a recitation mistake (zillat al-qari) during prayer. The legal effect is either invalidation (batil) or validity depending on conditions.
2
State the positions of the two imams
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: invalid if meaning changes obscenely (fahish); otherwise valid. This rule applies regardless of whether the mistaken word exists in the Quran.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and its criterion
Abu Yusuf: if the mistaken word has a similar counterpart in the Quran, the prayer is never invalidated (even if meaning changes obscenely). If no counterpart exists, it invalidates absolutely.
The existence of a similar word is the key factor.
4
Apply to the four example scenarios
Work through each of the four cases mentioned (Iblis/Idris, Ahad/Allah, ghubar/ghurab, qayyamin/qawwamin) and determine the ruling under each imam.
This clarifies the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زلة القارئ
كتاب الصلاة
۱۱۳
باب زلة القارئ
توهم
أنه ليس له
قال المحشي: لما رأيت مسائل زلة القارئ من أهم ما يجب العلم بها، والناس عنها غافلون، ووجدت ما في "الطحطاوي" على "المراقي" أوفى ما في هذا البحث ألحقته بهذا الكتاب مراعاة لمن سلك طريق الهدى، واجتنب سبل الهوى؛ ليكون واقيا لي من النيران، ووسيلة إلى الجنان، ورجحانا في ميزاني عند خفة الميزان، وعليه التكلان. قال: تكميل: زلة القارئ من أهم المسائل، وهي مبنية على قواعد ناشئة من الاختلافات لا كما قاعدة تبني عليها، فالأصل فيها عند الإمام ومحمد رحما: تغير المعنى تغيراً فاحشا، وعدمه للفساد، سواء كان اللفظ موجوداً في القرآن، أو لم يكن، وعند أبي يوسف له إن كان اللفظ نظيره موجوداً في القرآن لا تفسد مطلقاً تغير المعنى تغيرا فاحشا أولا، وإن لم يكن موجودا في القرآن تفسد مطلقا، ولا يعتبر الإعراب أصلا، ومحل الاختلاف في الخطأ والنسيان، أما في العمد فتفسد به مطلقا بالاتفاق إذا كان مما يفسد الصلاة، أما إذا كان ثناء فلا يفسد ولو تعمد ذلك أفاده ابن أمير الحاج.

Chapter of the Mistake of the Reciter. The commentator said: Since I saw that the issues of the reciter's mistake are among the most important things that must be known, and people are heedless of them, and I found what is in al-Tahtawi's commentary on al-Maraqi is the most comprehensive in this research, I appended it to this book... The fundamental rule according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) is: if the meaning changes in an obscene way, the prayer is invalidated; and if not, it is not invalidated, regardless of whether the word exists in the Quran or not. According to Abu Yusuf: if the word has a similar counterpart in the Quran, it does not invalidate the prayer at all, whether the meaning changes obscenely or not; but if it does not have a similar counterpart in the Quran, it invalidates absolutely. And i'rab is not considered at all. The disagreement is in error and forgetfulness. As for intentional mistakes, it invalidates absolutely by consensus if it is something that invalidates prayer. But if it is praise, it does not invalidate even if intentional... The reciter's mistake means the occurrence of a slip by the reciter in prayer... Know that the issue has four aspects: either the word recited by mistake has a counterpart in the Quran or not, and both types are divided into whether the meaning changes obscenely or not. The first: like reciting 'And Iblis and Dhul-Kifl' instead of 'And Idris and Dhul-Kifl'. The second: like reciting 'Say: He is Allah, the One' instead of the verse. The third: like reciting 'this dust' instead of 'this crow', and similarly 'Yawma tubla al-sara'il' with lam instead of ra in 'al-sara'ir'. The fourth: like reciting 'qayyamin' instead of 'qawwamin'. What is considered for non-invalidation when the meaning does not change much is the existence of a similar word in the Quran according to Abu Yusuf, and accordance in meaning according to the two.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the reciter's mistake. The commentator first explains why he appended this discussion from al-Tahtawi. Then he presents the foundational disagreement within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that if the recitation mistake changes the meaning in an obscene (fahish) way, the prayer is invalid. If the meaning does not change, the prayer remains valid. This rule applies whether the mistaken word exists in the Quran or not. Imam Abu Yusuf, on the other hand, distinguishes based on whether the mistaken word has a similar counterpart elsewhere in the Quran. If it does, the prayer is not invalidated at all, even if the meaning changes. If it does not, the prayer is invalid. The disagreement only applies to mistakes of error or forgetfulness; intentional mistakes always invalidate if they are of a kind that invalidate prayer (e.g., not praise of Allah). The text then defines 'zillat al-qari' and mentions that some scholars argued that mistakes in recitation never invalidate due to general need. The passage then details four scenarios based on existence of a similar word and change of meaning, giving examples: (1) changing 'Idris' to 'Iblis' (meaning change, no similar word), (2) adding 'Ahad' after 'Allahu' (no meaning change, similar word), (3) changing 'ghurab' to 'ghubar' (meaning change, similar word?), and (4) changing 'qawwamin' to 'qayyamin' (no meaning change, no similar word?). The last line notes that Abu Yusuf requires the existence of a similar word for non-invalidation, while the two imams require accordance in meaning. This sets up the detailed rulings that follow.

Key Terms
زلة القارئ (zillat al-qāri'): A slip or mistake made by the reciter during prayer recitation.
تغير المعنى (taghayyur al-ma'nā): Change of meaning of the recited verse due to the mistake. If obscene (fahish), it invalidates according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Change of meaning in an obscene manner

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on zillat al-qari; the later relied-upon view often favors Abu Yusuf's criterion of the existence of a similar word.

Mistakes in Recitation: The Later Hanafi Fatwa on I'rab and Similar Errors
Details the fatwa on i'rab mistakes and analogous errors like tashdid and madd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on i'rab mistakes in prayer and explain why the later school adopted Abu Yusuf's view.

Core Idea
A mistake in i'rab does not invalidate prayer, even if meaning changes, due to the removal of hardship.

This passage addresses the first specific issue in the chapter: errors in grammatical inflection (i'rab) during salah. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute and the eventual consensus of later scholars who adopted the more lenient position of Abu Yusuf. The ruling is then extended to analogous errors like lightening a shaddah or shortening a madd. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the principle of raf' al-haraj (removal of hardship) that underlies the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Dispute
The act is making a mistake in i'rab (e.g., wrong case ending) while reciting Quran in prayer. The dispute: does it invalidate the prayer? The text distinguishes between when meaning changes and when it does not.
Consensus exists that if meaning does not change, prayer is valid.
2
Locate the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani held that if the i'rab mistake changes the meaning, the prayer is invalid. Abu Yusuf held that i'rab is not considered; thus, the prayer remains valid regardless of meaning change.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's Dalil and the Later Consensus
Abu Yusuf's basis: i'rab is not an essential element of correct recitation; the prayer is valid despite grammatical errors. Later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) agreed, citing raf' al-haraj (removal of hardship) because most people cannot master i'rab. They ruled that i'rab mistakes never invalidate, even if the mistaken reading implies kufr.
This principle overrides the earlier stricter view.
4
Recognize the Extension to Similar Errors
The text explicitly includes: lightening a shaddah, shortening a madd, separating an idgham, and their opposites. These are treated identically to i'rab mistakes: they do not invalidate prayer according to the later fatwa.
The ruling is unified across these categories.
5
Determine the Operative Fatwa (Mufta Bihi)
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf, supported by the later consensus. Therefore, any mistake in i'rab or analogous error (takhfif, qasr, etc.) does not invalidate the prayer, whether the meaning changes or not, and even if intentional (as long as not a substantive change that constitutes kufr, but even then the fatwa is non-invalidation).
This is the fatwa given in al-Khulasa, al-Nawazil, and other later works.

وفي هذا الفصل مسائل: الأولى: الخطأ في الإعراب ويدخل فيه تخفيف المشدد، وعكسه، وقصر الممدود، وعكسه، وفك المدغم وعكسه، فإن لم يتغير به المعنى لا تفسد به صلاته بالإجماع كما في "المضمرات"، وإذا تغير المعنى نحو أن يقرأ: ﴿وَإِذِ ابْتَلَى إِبْرَاهِيمَ رَبُّهُ﴾ (البقرة: (١٢٤) برفع "إبراهيم" ونصب "ربه" فالصحيح عنهما: الفساد، وعلى قياس قول أبي يوسف : لا تفسد ؛ لأنه لا يعتبر الإعراب وبه يفتى وأجمع المتأخرون كـ محمد ابن مقاتل، ومحمد بن سلام، وإسماعيل الزاهد، وأبي بكر سعيد البلخي، والهندواني وابن الفضل والحلواني على أن الخطأ في الإعراب لا يفسد مطلقا، وإن كان مما اعتقاده كفر ؛ لأن أكثر الناس لا يميزون بين وجوه الإعراب، و في اختيار الصواب في الإعراب إيقاع الناس في الحرج، وهو مرفوع شرعا.
